Farmer-Labor (Prog.)
Farmer-Labor Party - Progressive Faction\n§LFounded in 1930 as a broad alliance of progressive and labour organisations, the Farmer-Labor Party has steadily grown throughout the 1930s. After several false starts in the 1920s, Farmer-Labor has emerged as the primary vehicle for left-wing politics in the United States, for the first time clearly orienting American politics on class lines.\n\nOutside of the Socialist Party, various Progressive politicians compete in elections under the Farmer-Labor label. Some, such as members of the La Follette family's Wisconsin Progressive Party, are members of their own distinct organisations, while others are members of state Farmer-Labor organisations hewing more closely to the national party line. These non-socialist members of Farmer-Labor are often more agriculturally-oriented, and believe in a more limited platform of social benefits and the nationalisation of utilities and certain industries, as well as the empowerment of organised labour.§!\n
Democrats (Lib.)
Democratic Party - Liberal Faction\n§LThe oldest continually active political party in the world, the Democratic Party was founded over 100 years ago in 1828 by Andrew Jackson and Martin van Buren. Originally an agrarian populist party upholding Jeffersonian principles, it transformed first into a (generally) pro-slavery party, then into agrarian and southern opposition to the Republicans, and then into a western, southern, and increasingly urban party with liberal inclinations.\n\nThe liberal wing of the Democrats, usually associated with the north, follows largely in the legacy of Woodrow Wilson. Democrats (Con.)
Democratic Party - Conservative Faction\n§LThe oldest continually active political party in the world, the Democratic Party was founded over 100 years ago in 1828 by Andrew Jackson and Martin van Buren. Originally an agrarian populist party upholding Jeffersonian principles, it transformed first into a (generally) pro-slavery party, then into agrarian and southern opposition to the Republicans, and then into a western, southern, and increasingly urban party with liberal inclinations.\n\nThe conservative wing of the Democrats, usually associated with the south, has been dominant in that region since the end of reconstruction. It is the natural ruling party in most of the south, with nomination tantamount to election. Divided between agrarian reactionaries and more reform-minded moderate conservatives, they are generally opposed to Civil Rights reform and cartelisation of the economy, supporting smaller businesses and landowners.§!\n
Democrats (React.)
Democratic Party - Reactionary Faction\n§LThe oldest continually active political party in the world, the Democratic Party was founded over 100 years ago in 1828 by Andrew Jackson and Martin van Buren. Originally an agrarian populist party upholding Jeffersonian principles, it transformed first into a (generally) pro-slavery party, then into agrarian and southern opposition to the Republicans, and then into a western, southern, and increasingly urban party with liberal inclinations.\n\nPerhaps the most anachronistic section of the party are the reactionaries of the Deep South, who have for years maintained their opposition to liberalising trends represented by those such as Al Smith. Nativist, white supremacist, and generally reactionary, albeit with populist elements, these southern Democrats are quickly becoming tired of the national party leadership, and may jump ship if the opportunity arises, as figures like Theodore Bilbo and Eugene Talmadge reconsider their place in the party.§!\n

Union (Reactionaries)
Union Party - Reactionary Faction
$USA_authoritarian_democrat_party_union_long_tt$\n§LThe newest major party in US politics, the Union Party was recently formed primarily as a vehicle for Huey Long's bid for the Presidency, when it became clear he would not be able to attain the Democratic nomination. A broad-tent alliance comprising Democrats, reactionaries, and anti-syndicalist Progressives, they are united by little more than their shared opposition to the Smith Administration, and at least a temporary unity behind Long as their leader.\n\nThough traditionally Long's base of support has been in the midwestern farm states, reactionary and populist southern Democratic leaders such as Eugene Talmadge and Theodore Bilbo have rallied behind Long out of their opposition to Smith. These southern Democrats are united primarily by their belief in white supremacy and disdain for Smith's particular brand of liberalism. Their unity behind Long however is clearly conditional, and unlikely to last if push comes to shove.§!\n

America First
America First Committee
$USA_national_populist_party_compromise_long_tt$\n§LWith the outbreak of civil war, far-right and isolationist tendencies gained considerable popularity. Though those views were previously represented in the Union Party, Huey Long's abandonment of that electoral vehicle divided the far-right. Some joined Long in returning to the Democrats. Others however, inclined to a more clearly conservative view, chose to follow a different path. The result is the America First Committee, a political pressure group advocating for isolationism, anti-syndicalism, and traditional values. Headed by former Long ally Gerald L. K. Smith (who Long fired in mid-1937), and famed aviator Charles Lindbergh, the organisation initially showed promise, however soon its momentum stalled, and it appears unlikely that it will be a decisive power player any time soon.§!\n

U.S. Military
United States Military\n§LOnce viewed as an unthinkable taboo, the United States Military has crossed the rubicon, decisively intervening in civilian affairs and establishing an emergency military government in Washington to see America through its present crisis. Applauded by hardline conservatives in Congress, and denounced by the rest of the nation, General Douglas MacArthur has taken the reins in a country beset by Civil War. With few allies outside of his own clique and the Conservative Coalition which invited him to march on the capital, the future of MacArthur's regime is uncertain.§!\n

Inter-American Defense College
The Inter-American Defense College is designed to improve science and develop research with members of the League of American States.\n
The Great Depression
Since the collapse of the New York Stock Market in 1925, the United States has been gripped by an unprecedented economic malaise that has come to be termed the Great Depression. After the agonising years of Frank Lowden's presidency, many hoped that the Democrats under Al Smith could return the nation to prosperity. Despite an outpouring of hope surrounding his election in 1928 however, President Smith has ultimately proved unable to pull the country out of its malaise. As Congress has been reluctant to endorse overtly interventionist measures, and Smith has tended towards managerial and structural reforms, dissatisfaction with the political mainstream grows. The situation has been on a gradual upturn since the Depression's nadir in 1929, as well as the interruption of the recession of 1931, but the struggling state of the economy is fueling radical discontent on both sides regardless. Support for the left-wing Farmer-Labor Party grows, while a big-tent Democratic Party is hopelessly divided on what action needs to be taken.
The Great Depression
The Great Depression which has gripped America for over a decade gradually improved under the stewardship of Al Smith, but Smith's personal reluctance for radical reform and an inability to pass significant reform through Congress made any such progress painfully slow. But now, the situation has been blown apart. Black Monday, the collapse of the Berlin Stock Market in February, has resulted in a renewed wave of economic damage that is spreading throughout American society. Small businesses, already struggling in the inclement economic climate, fall bankrupt by the thousands as it appears any progress made since 1931 has been wiped out in a matter of days and weeks. Rightly or wrongly, fingers are being pointed at the White House, and whoever sits within it come 1937 has a seemingly impossible problem to solve.
A House Divided
The United States is in crisis. The Great Depression, which has been ravaging our nation for over a decade, has still not let up. With Congress split between a divided Democratic Party, a weakened Republican Party and an insurgent Progressive bloc, President Smith has been unable to fix the many ills facing American society, and voters are abandoning the centre in droves. On the left, the Socialist Party of America has grown into a legitimate political force across the Steel Belt, while on the right an eclectic coalition of nationalists, anti-syndicalists, spurned progressives and disillusioned liberals flock to the banner of Senator Huey Long, whose rhetoric grows increasingly violent as the acrimony of his quest for the Democratic nomination heats up.
The United States is a house divided. The Great Depression, which has been ravaging our nation for over a decade, has only been worsened by the Berlin Stock Market Crash. The recent Democratic National Convention has collapsed in ignominy, with Huey Long's populist faction of the party walking out and exacerbating the deep-seated polarisation of American society. Congress is now hopelessly divided between four feuding coalitions, and President Smith is now forced to govern through executive orders if anything is to be done at all. In a climate of radicalisation and violence, confrontations between strikers spurred on by Socialist Party militancy and the growing paramilitaries aligned with the Longist movement score the midwest. America faces a four-way race for the presidency, and it looks unlikely that any one man will win a majority in the Electoral College.
The United States stands on the brink. While the Great Depression grips the nation in an iron vice, the political system has been shattered. For the second time in two elections, the Presidency was thrown to a contingent election, no man able to win a majority in the Electoral Collage in the incredibly tight race. The contested election means fingers are being pointed in every direction, as radicals cry of corrupt bargains to keep the nation out of the hands of the majority, strikes grow with ever more militancy, and political violence rolls on. Tears in the very fabric of American society grow with each passing day, and a national tragedy looks to be on the horizon.
The United States stands on the brink. For the first time in American history, the presidency is vacant. As the House is incapable of certifying the results of the election, no contingent election for either the Pesidency or Vice Presidency can be held. As Smith's term ends, outgoing Secretary of State Cordell Hull finds himself as a seat-warmer while the Presidency is decided, an unenviable position as the nation is on the brink of civil war. With the headless federal government paralysed, the seemingly inevitable national calamity seems only days away from coming to pass...
Strike Season
While the initial years of the Great Depression proved damaging for union activities, there has since been massive growth in both the scale and militancy of organised labour, spurred on by awful economic conditions and the legacy of the syndicalist revolutions in France and especially Britain. The election of President Smith, a man considered an ally of the AFL, ironically encouraged labour militancy, as Smith both passed pro-union reforms such as the Wagner Act, and failed to put forward a compelling progressive economic vision. The failure of the administration to foster any enduring sense of recovery has sparked a new wave of strikes, far larger and more numerous than at any prior point in American history. Syndicalist organisers like Elizabeth Gurley Flynn and William Foster fan the flames - perhaps hoping that the strikes could be the seeds of a revolution of their own - and violent altercations along picket lines by armed strike breakers and paramilitaries fuel them ever further.
General Strike
With the nation in the midst of a political crisis, a general strike has engulfed the steel belt. The massacre of Cox's marchers has destroyed any remaining faith in a peaceful resolution to labour issues. Instead, in both wildcat and organised fashion, workers in key industrial sectors, CIO, IWW, and even AFL alike, have joined together and walked off the job. By far the largest strike in American history, it represents the culmination of the militant labour actions of the past year, as well as of the mobilisation of American labour towards the far-left, a trend which now seems destined to lead to cataclysmic violence.

Recovering from the Civil War
While we may have won the Civil War, our country is in ruins. Most people are forced to barter; electricity, running water, and other basic services barely function; and millions are starving or ill, especially the thousands and thousands of orphans.
While we may have stopped the cholera epidemics and famines, most of the country is still on fire. The only place one can find any modicum of stability is the heavily guarded military depots containing newly-delivered famine relief aid and medicine.
The cities have returned to some level of stability, and currency is starting to come back into use as bartering fades. The mass graves are now covered in saplings and flowers as the nation slowly claws itself back from collapse.
Government-run agencies have started to put people back to work, and some respectable businesses have reopened. The threat of mass starvation has passed, though it is not uncommon to see small hordes of orphans and elderly rooting through trash in the cities.
The scars of the war, visible just months ago, have largely faded from the country. Factories have re-opened, and trains, buses, and other forms of public transportation have started running with some regularity. America has nearly returned to its pre-war standard of living.

The last decade has not been a shining one, to say the least. The Great War's fallout largely ended the prosperity of the pre-war era, as the economy proceeded to initially stagnate, then fall into a depression, with Presidents McAdoo and Lowden being unable, unwilling or too indecisive to stem the tide. What little progress has been made has largely been erased by crisis after crisis - first the British Revolution of 1925, followed by the Creditanstalt collapse of 1931.
While we are no longer in the depths of the depression as in 1929, the country's political sphere continues to grow increasingly febrile - if the tide is not stemmed soon, the situation may spiral out of anyone's control...
With Black Monday entirely erasing all of the gains made under President Smith, the economy has reached its worst state in two decades. The country's political sphere, already increasingly febrile, is quickly reaching a fever pitch - if the situation is not stabilised, it may spiral out of anyone's control...

Victory in the Civil War
Separatists have again failed in their mission to destroy the union of the United States of America. Though both radical socialists and populists dug into our power base, we have proven the power of legitimate government once more. The would-be dictators Reed and Long are no longer welcome in America.
Democracy Triumphs!
Though the temptation towards autocracy was great, America stood with its three branches intact, without giving up to executive authority. Congress is called into emergency session and the Appellate Courts are dealing with their mountain of paper trying to sort out the consequences.
Constitutional Education
A common talking point by radicals and populists was the idea that the Federal Government is a voluntary organisation. Some even claim to use ridiculous false loopholes like naval law or the rights to secede from the union. We must correct this by making the U.S Constitution as widely available as possible.
Defend Democracy
Out of the former rebel states, reports have come in of voter intimidation based on class and race. Furthermore, candidates are running for office without an oath of allegiance to the United States. We must protect the people's right to vote, and ensure that politicians do not incite rebellion again.
Bill of Rights Reminder
Building off of a Constitutional education initiative, Congress has approved an education push to younger Americans on the importance of our Bill of Rights. This will also allow citizens to better appeal for their rights in a non-violent manner.
American Values
The passive promotion of civil government through high minded publications was undercut sharply by pamphlets and private publishers that promoted an uncivil government. Congress has decided that a multifaceted approach to instilling American values through mass media will finally undercut pamphleteers.
Restore Legitimacy
The numerous embassies we were not able to staff during the crisis have finally received relief. We shall re-establish ourselves in the world community as a stronger and more unified nation with an expanded diplomatic corps.

Destroy Radicalism
While the US Government tolerates political discourse, Congress has rallied against the syndicalist and distributionist platforms of Long and Reed. Legal bodies found to be advocating for trade unions or mutualist organisations will be prosecuted under the 1917 Sedition Act.
Strengthen Democracy
During the civil war, democratic processes were halted at the local level. Many elections in the border areas were skipped in order to focus more time on the existential crisis of the war for America. Democracy shall now rise from the ashes, and Congress has appointed a committee to ensure elections take place at the local level once more.
Loyalty to America
The early 1930s was the era of loyalty to men over ideals. Reed, Long, and even MacArthur accrued a sort of clique of allies that saw their leaders as above the law. Several Congressmen have come out to apologise for their statements made during the war.
Ensure Political Stability
Although it is opposed by some of the legislators, the use of the FCC to monitor the airwaves against rebel radio stations is necessary. This measure, along with several other forms of censorship, is still necessary to end rebel pockets within the Contiguous U.S.
Protect Democracy
The 17th Amendment enhanced the democratic representation in America, but failed, in the long run, to make the electoral process more democratic. Congress shall strengthen the democratic process directly through the review of poll taxes and registries of felons, to ensure the word of the law is followed.
Land of the Free
The use of penal labour in the prisoner of war camps is no longer tolerable to Congress. Although the fate of these prisoners is still up to the court's system, their exploitation in both loyal and rebel states should be rolled back.
Home of the Brave
The veterans of the Second Civil War have sacrificed it all to preserve their home, if only they didn't have to fight other Americans. Despite protests from the House, the Senate has wisely extended veterans' benefits to the rebel soldiers, so long as that recipient re-affirm their oath to all the American people.
For the People
The people of America, as a collective, are our constituents and our lifeblood. A holiday in thanks to the American people has been passed through Congress to make the former Labor Day into \
A More Perfect Union
The goal of the United States as an independent nation is to form a more perfect union of the people of the United States, not the exaltation of a single doctrine or political movement as Reed or Long claimed. The President has spoken on the irreducible complexity of America's relationship to its people.
Begin Reconstruction
The nation had suffered greatly long before this war started. It is both a monumental task and an opportunity to unify transportation networks and push through bolder economic ideas to elevate American industry above this ailing world.
Rebuild American Railroads
The railroad networks that cross America are in shambles, and war-era constructions are jury-rigged to older tracks. Congress has approved a rebuilding of our railroad network in the form of mandatory third rail electrification. Electrified tracks will force our energy grid to reform as a result.
Electrification Program
In order to accommodate the mandatory Third Rail, as well as ensure the safety of the more remote parts of America, an electrification project is approved to cross all state lines. Congress is now pulling state governments to fund transformers and hydroelectric power, as it is their responsibility.
Business Subsidies
Small businesses in America have struggled to expand their employment opportunities, which is contributing to unemployment. The issue of unsafe working conditions returning to prominence due to the need for faster production has led to agitated workers. Congress has approved a federal purse to subsidise small businesses.
Rebuild America's Industry
America's exports have fallen during the depression despite taking a laissez-faire position on trade laws. Exports are also one of the main ways we measure economic activity. We must invest in the tertiary services our industrial businesses use in order to lower their bottom line and increase output.
Economic Investments
A bolder strategy is devised by Congress to assist in economic recovery. Traditional notions that government purchases are negatively associated with growth, newer theories hold that smart purchases can stimulate the economy.
Fate of the Unions
It is time for Congress to hear the testimony of rebellious unions. Some are calling for just their chair-people to resign, while others insist on collecting transcripts of union meetings, paving the way for prosecuting all active members.
Rebuild America's Roads
The state-funded interstate highway system was an easy target for sabotage. We must cooperate with the states in order to ensure safe commerce and travel through America once more.
American Industrial Might
The war may have temporarily reinvigorated heavy industry, but its design was temporary and facilities were essentially built on top of closed factories. We must bring our safety and management efficiencies to bear in order to make this upswing permanent.
Rebuild Agricultural Industry
In order to transport and process the food to feed our nation, we must encourage innovative preservation and agronomy sciences. Congress has set up a fund to investigate this and several politicians have contributed to it directly.
Aviation Industry
The United States used to lead the world in civilian aircraft manufacturing. Now assembly line systems in Germany have us outpaced. Congress has spoken to intelligence agencies about what we can do to encourage businesses to adopt these techniques, including our contractors.
Farming Subsidies
It is necessary to subsidise farms for crops we are in need of, and to pay farmers to terminate their fields of lost assets for products like tobacco we don't need right now, but want the skilled labour to still be available.
Maritime Industry
The Merchant Marine was severely damaged in the war, and Congress has approved the extension of veteran benefits to those active duty sailors who are not on tour if they become a Merchant Marine in their downtime.
Oil Production
The oil fields of the Midwest burned as our country was fighting. We must control these fires, stop future sabotage, and invest in synthetic oil to ensure that more of the country can make use of vehicles.
Reconstruction Over
The years of poor economic management and civil strife have not left our minds, but their most damning effects are diminished.
President MacArthur has proclaimed he would not concede victory to the very partisans who caused the civil war. His American Junta promises a national restoration and adoption of functional democracy as MacArthur sees it. Elimination of unnecessary politicians and appointment of more competent officials will bridge the gap between people and politics.
Army Education
Parents' organisations have come out to claim that we willingly let children into the military underage. Our solution is to divert prospective youth into military education while keeping them in public school. The ideas of physical education and morals taught by Bellamy will revive that old nationalist fervour that failed us in the 1910s.
National Youth Administration
The simultaneous pull to mandate a higher working age is countered by the multitude of unemployed youth strewn across America. The solution is to establish a National Youth Administration in order to provide work and education to Americans too young to vote.
The American Legion
With the American Legion National Commander Smedley Butler now a fugitive, it is necessary to rebuild the organisation to remove the stain of partisan politics. No longer will National Commanders be permitted to campaign for politicians, nor will they be permitted to stay once they are career politicians.
Loyal to the Flag
Unlike the tyrants and despots that are common in the Americas, MacArthur desires not to be a Great Man, but to be a respected and mortal leader of Americans. Loyalty to the unchanging ideal of America must be put above himself, so long as MacArthur's popularity holds out.
Martial Law
With Congressional approval, habeas corpus is suspended in accordance with the Constitution. As the threat of invasion from Syndicalist and Populist forces still looms over part of the land, the writ of habeas corpus and free speech are still suspended for political expediency.
Second American Protective League
As the largest part of the Continuous United States has been pacified, it is essential that American citizens remain vigilant. The reformation of the League aims to create a free information system to report potential populist or syndicalist spies to the Federal Government and to discourage public protest.
Control Congress
Many former Democrats and Republicans have folded into MacArthur's new regime, while holdouts have fled. Fortunately, we were able to fill their vacancies with qualified, trustworthy individuals. These new Congressmen are not politicians per se, they are instead public servants for the American people.
Signals Intelligence Service
Cryptographic machines designed to interact with their sender to create an encryption that cannot be easily broken are the newest toy in our arsenal. The Signals Intelligence Service, which required the installation of underground cables to ensure secrecy, has finally been implemented.
Executive Order 7250-A
An Executive Order signed by President MacArthur aims to bring an end to the threat of foreign infiltration. This order restores some parts of the Alien and Sedition Acts, notorious in the early 1800s. State legislatures are already appealing cases to the Supreme Court. It is firmly believed, however, that MacArthur's new judges will side in his favour.
Empower the Army
A crisis has already arisen in our new military administration. The Army and Navy are constantly at each other's throats over funding and political kickbacks. We need to relegate the Navy to a secondary governmental position and grant the Army full power.
Old Soldiers Never Die
The new regime recognises the long struggle of the officers who left their homes to protect their nation, and to the many who didn't return home. Thanks to an Executive Order, officers may now pursue a technical education in universities or go into law. This will ensure loyalty long after we fade away.
The Commander-in-Chief
The role of the President as Commander-in-Chief goes back to President Washington. Washington set the precedent of retiring from active duty upon taking office, which MacArthur promises he will do once the national emergency is ended. Like Washington, MacArthur will remain ready to respond to threats to the nation.
National Rehabilitation
The creeds of Long and Reed were wrong: it was not the industrialists and businessmen that caused civil strife, but the greedy career politician who gave them posts and took their money. We shall rehabilitate the capitalists to their proper position in American society.
Root out Traitors
Our intelligence services have identified the enablers of radicalism and greed in America. They are the disloyal Prohibitionists, Grangers, Holy Rollers and foreigners that enabled the SPA and Longists to grow. These organisations have been rightfully banned for their implicit betrayal.
American Stratocracy
MacArthur has finally restored nationalist fervour and functional democracy as he sees it. While some complain that career politicians have been replaced by officers, few will argue that the bureaucracy hasn't improved. The American people can now trust their politicians to use legal means to achieve their goals.

The Social Security Act
With Congress soon re-entering session, it will soon be our last chance to push forward any new significant legislation before the election. President Smith, wanting to leave office on a high note, and hoping to weaken the pension issue as an attack on the next Democratic nominee, has chosen to focus on passing Social Security. Though the path to passage is difficult, we believe we may just have the votes for one more win.
Failure Of the Social Security Act
The economic crisis in Germany has reached America's shores. In a panic, Congress has tabled the Social Security bill, essentially killing President Smith's last hope for a major legislative accomplishment. Now the nation waits with bated breath to see what its government will do to address the crisis.
Introduce the Garner-McNary Bill
The renewed crisis on Wall Street demands immediate action by the administration. President Smith has called on Congress to pass emergency economic relief legislation to prevent a return to the dark days of 1929. To that end, Democratic Speaker John Nance Garner and Republican Senator Charles McNary have co authored a relief bill, which has the support of the President.
The Bill Fails
The Garner-McNary Bill has failed to pass. This leaves America without a clear route towards recovery, and with a growing insurgency that will need to be addressed.
War Plan White
War Plan White is a military action plan to contend with domestic violence or an insurgency. It's time to dust off the plan and deal directly with the growing violence in America.
Deploy the National Guard
The violence caused by supporters of Huey Long and the Socialist Party is only getting worse. We need to increase funding to National Guard units, and put them where their efforts will count most.
MacArthur's Plan
General MacArthur has raised a solid point: New York City and Texas are two of our most vital, yet vulnerable, strongholds. MacArthur has a plan that could see one of these areas secured, should the violence escalate to a full civil war.
The Bill Passes
The Garner-McNary bill has been passed! This is good news for America's economy - though now we must find ways to fund the bill, or the good news isn't going to last.
Shipyard Funding Scheme
Two major shipbuilding companies are vying for federal relief funding, and the one we select could mean a large number of new jobs in the region. The trouble is: which one do we focus on?
The Barkley Plan
Alben Barkley, Democrat and junior Senator for Kentucky, has proposed a plan which would see the Garner-McNary bill funded by increased corporate income taxes. The plan is controversial with some, but it just might give the economy the boost it needs.
The New Industrial Act
We need to kickstart heavy industry in America's heartlands, where the Great Depression has hit the hardest.
Demand Payment of Docking Fees
After the British Revolution, to avoid mothballing the remaining Royal Navy, the Canadian Government docked many formerly British ships in American ports at discounted docking rates. The question of payment for this service however has remained a sore spot in American politics. While it's unlikely Canada could repay all of their fees right now, demanding repayment will appease isolationists in Congress, whom we believe will join the political fringe if not appeased.
Reconciliation with Canada
The isolationists are elated, but at the cost of our relations with Canada. We can try rebuilding those relations by offering a compromise: some assistance from Canada now, with the fees deferred until after the war. In exchange, we'll reduce the import tariffs from the Entente.
Raise Entente Tariffs
Canada refused to pay the docking fees - unsurprisingly - and thus in return our only option is to press punitive tariffs on Entente goods imported into the US. That will put some money in our coffers, though repairing relations with Canada will take a long, long time.
President Borah
The election of the Republican candidate to the presidency after months of speculation has come as a relief to the American people. A progressive in the old Teddy Roosevelt mold, William Borah will have to prove that the old parties can meet a progressive moment.
President Landon
The election of the Republican candidate to the presidency after months of speculation has come as a relief to the American people. A moderate but not a conservative, Alf Landon will have to lean on the establishment to save the republic.
Re-light the Western Torch
Not one for idleness, President Borah enters office with an ambitious plan to save the republic. While some suggest otherwise, the radicals can be distinguished from one another: while the socialists are destructive, and cannot be reasoned with, Huey Long is a known quantity, and winning him over to Borah's reform program may be the key to building a national consensus.
The Iron Fist
Radicalism has become a disease afflicting America. Both Long and the Socialists threaten to tear the country apart, and engage in open street violence to get their way. Enough is enough. We must put our foot down at once to suppress the growth of anti-constitutional movements, even if it costs us important political capital.
The First 100 Days
While President Landon may be a moderate, he recognises the need for immediate relief to American businesses, and now intends to shore up employment by pushing through a blanket relief bill. Faced with the opposition of the radicals however, he will have to thread the needle through a fractured congressional centre in order to achieve a victory early into his administration.
President Olson
The American people have demanded and gotten change. The first Farmer-Labor President, Floyd Olson has ridden a radical coalition of the left to the White House. Now he must deliver on the promises of a coalition gradually growing more radical than he is.
Legalise Expropriation of Idle Factories
Across the nation, hundreds upon thousands of factories lie dormant, due to the failure of their operators to turn a profit. As the burden of capitalist failure is cast downwards, millions of workers lie unemployed next to the empty factories in which they once worked. Enough is enough. If the capitalists will not run these factories, we will seize them and run them ourselves, and we will make work for those who have been left behind.
Enforce Labour and Lynching Laws
Some of the few positive developments of the Smith Administration were the passage of various labour laws, and the Anti-Lynching Act. Though these represent an important step forward, they often went unenforced in Smith's time. We will rectify this. With the full force of the federal government, we will make the rights promised to workers and African-Americans a reality.
President Long
The impossible has occurred and Huey Long has gained the presidency on a third-party ticket. His allies do not, however, have control over the Senate or the House of Representatives, and President Long thus faces both a wary legislature and a country on the verge of utter chaos.
The Nye-Sweeney Banking Bill
Wall Street banks have long trodden over the common American with impunity, foreclosing on properties and destroying livelihoods. That the instruments of financial power in this country remain outside of the control of the American people is a disgrace. The Nye-Sweeney Banking Bill rectifies this by placing banking activity under democratic control, bringing in popular accountability and binding Wall Street to the will of the people.
Deputise the Minutemen
Day by day, America falls further into chaos. Violent anarchists and criminal syndicalists roam freely, spreading sedition and inciting mayhem in the name of foreign radicalism. As it becomes clear that local law enforcement is incapable of meeting the threat alone, we must bolster their numbers by deputising loyal and patriotic Minutemen, who will stamp out the criminal element and restore order to the country.
War Department Expansion
The United States War Department has seen a shrinkage over the last half-decade through austerity measures. Now it is vital that staffing be expanded and new innovators enter the department, ready for reform.
Army Reform Debate
The question of the hour, which direction should the US Army take to not only respond but anticipate a prolonged land war? The opinion of MacArthur is a given, having already prepared for this conflict within his inner circle.
Air Force Debate
The Air Force, having the funding necessary to expand, lacks the precise direction and leadership needed to effectively advance. With numerous requests to fund research, and competing minds insisting that they are the key to victory in the skies.
Adna Chaffee Reform Plan
MOLLUS recipient Adna Chaffee Jr. proposes that the Army step up production of more expensive armoured vehicles, as well as plan out new specialised divisions to complement a more mobile war.
Lesley McNair Reform Plan
McNair proposes refining the inherent advantage the US Army has in delivering a mass quantity of support to infantry attacks. This will require an intensive employment increase in war industries.
Standardise the M1
The M1 designation infantry weapon has been in trial for years, wasting contracts. The final decision on which design will go into production will be answered in a timely manner now.
Defence Contractors
Private enterprise has become an undeniable part of our military industry. It is time we draw up contracts and see what they can do to help us.
Restart Examining Boards
The Army's review process has had its share of reformers, but by-and-large the system has remained stagnant for a decade. McNair insists that improvements can be made.
Efficient Production Program
The unemployed masses that stand waiting for a job are the perfect test subjects for creating taylor-timekeeping tables for efficient production.
Shock and Awe
Entrenchment can turn an open field into a stagnant killing ground, and despite our better nature, we must employ the heaviest artillery shells in order to force our enemies to retreat in such a scenario.
Take the Fight Abroad
Finally, the top brass is satisfied with the progress we have put into the Army. Now we just need a target to put rubber to the road.
Military Research
Our national security is threatened by the asymmetrical advancement of technology. We cannot be blindsided by an enemy with some previously unknown weapon of war. We must increase military research and development funding drastically.
Increase Military Spending
Congress must approve a larger Army budget for the coming year. It will undoubtedly help the civilian economy down the line.
Liberty Bonds
Funding the war effort will require more than victory gardens and volunteerism. Liquid assets are in short supply, especially with our economic programs ongoing. We can capitalise on public trust and implement War Bonds as most other free nations do.
Army Rangers
Training Regiments to acclimatise soldiers into new environments will enable American soldiers to fight effectively no matter where the course of war may take them. The Rangers are a newly proposed force conceptualised around adaptation to harsh terrain, with the purpose of introducing their advancements slowly the Army as a whole. Let us found this organisation.
Walkie Talkies
Usually military equipment has strong names. Walkie Talkie? How did that slip through the system? Our generals claim that this new untethered communication device will enable our troops to speak effectively when they're in the field. And we called it Walkie Talkie?
Defense Logistics Agency
The layout of the United States may be suited for interstate commerce, but is unprepared for massive deployments. We must correct this.
Increase Military Production
The gratefully employed are in our factories toiling towards victory, though they may not believe that. Where propaganda has failed, monetary incentive will work to increase production.
Tank Competition
Tank designs are a dime a dozen, we need a streamlined system to determine which design will best fill its role in combat.
Armoured Cavalry
Top officers have long had experience in cavalry and have designed and planned to transform motorised and tanks to fit new needs. Working closely with the government, the military, Henry Ford and other Industrialists, we can make this plan a reality.
G.I. Bill
Young men have a variety of motivations for going to war. The G.I. Bill will hopefully encompass those motivators that patriotism cannot reach.
Fighter Development
While we were still stuck with the P-26 Peashooter, our national companies have made huge breakthroughs with the P-36 Hawk, the Seversky P-35, the P-39 Airacobra and the new Prototypes of the P-40 Warhawk which could give us an edge on the battlefield. Let us fund these companies so that their projects may enter mass production.
Expand the Air Corps Tactical School
We are in need of a space to train new pilots for the variety of operations the Air Force handles. In Virginia, a section of the ACTS has remained loyal to us, despite all shortcomings of the Air Force, and their installations and expertise may prove vital to train the airmen of tomorrow.
Create the WASPs
The Women Air Force Service Pilots will help support the Air Force, while they will be subordinate to the main male air-force and not be allowed to fly in combat situations, they will help to keep our boys flying in the air.
'Screaming Eagles' Program
General John C.H. Lee is insisting on starting off a new experiment in Air Assaults done in response to the Hang-glider operations pioneered in Europe. With airborne forces we will be able to overwhelm defenders from multiple angles in ways that it was impossible decades ago. As such, the general staff has authorised the experiments and funding shall be diverged to it.
R.A.D.A.R. Development
RADAR, the top-secret technology to detect air movement will allow our sky watchers to rest easy at night.
Expand the USAAC
The United States Army Air Corps, in service since 1926, has largely remained on the sidelines of military development. Despite receiving a meagre budget, they've yet managed to innovate in many aspects and High Command barely sees any reason to reform. Provided High Command's disputes in the past few years with Airmen, it has been decided they'd be better off remaining as an integral part of the Army.
Create the USAAF
The United States Army Air Force is the success of both the airman and the politician. With the dream of Billy Mitchell realised in all but name, we can now focus on improving on Harold L. George's doctrine and enhancing America's long-range strike capabilities.
Modernise Cavalry Tactics
It was apparent from our observers in the Weltkrieg that new tactics and technologies are becoming vital in the battlefield. Bearing this in mind, it's no wonder General Chaffee has seen fit to redistribute new manuals specifying how to use and counter armoured advances as the old counter-cavalry tactics grow outdated.
Mechanisation Program
The speeds Chaffe is promising on new vehicles will require a systematic change in how we build and maintain military vehicles.
Top-Notch Artillery
Artillery pieces will need to be stronger as well as lighter if we are to respond to battlefield changes as the plan dictates. McNair's expertise in the 1920s with the Examining boards seems to have not gone to waste, and he has proposed an overhaul of the American Artillery production which he projects will lead to artillery pieces being easier to produce and repair, as well as more accurate on the battlefield.
Production Prioritisation
As our War Industry hums along, McNair has stressed the necessity of the usage of both Anti Air and Anti Tank cannons to stop both armoured and aerial threats dead in their tracks. However, High Command will require some solid report evidence to divert the funding McNair is requesting...
Air-To-Ground Cooperation Exercises
While the USAAC has technically worked with the Army for well over a decade, they have hardly ever worked together. The Army is now requesting the Air Force to support their advances, and provided that doing so blindly might lead to friendly fire, generals are being paired in specific combat areas to exercise their coordination and to make sure our casualties are minimised.
CAS Model Development
As the Air Corps never intended to be integrated into the army, hardly any development has gone into newer Close Air Support Models. Thankfully, Contractors have already been kind enough to provide us with prototypes like the Brewster XSBA-1 and the already ageing Northrop A-17 \
Strategic Bomber Development
America hardly has any enemies within attack range to fear. As such, there has been a generalised thought that has been taking over the USAAF, spread by a group led by famous airmen like Carl Spaatz. The Army has dubbed them the \
Strategic Bombing Doctrine
The idea pushed by Spaatz and his acquaintances is a rather simple one: The Enemy won't be able to continue fighting if the home for which they are fighting for no longer exists. By destroying both their industry and their fighting spirit at the homefront, our troops will prevail both in morale and equipment on the front line.
Long Range Escorts
While having better bombers is vital to win the war of tomorrow at the enemy's doorstep, these bombers can seldom operate on their own. They will need an escort capable of facing off enemy fighters and come back in one piece. Luckily for us, plane designer Kelly Johnson has contacted us with a new and innovative design: The P-38, dubbed \
Aerodrome Construction
We should pepper the nation with airfields, enabling our Airmen to reach any part of the nation easily.
Central Operating Bases
We should concentrate on safer, larger airfields strategically located near major zones of control.
Flexible Bombers
The Army has stated they require multi-purpose air craft that can easily adapt to battle situations. Thankfully for us, our private contractors have come up with the NA-40, which could serve as a baseline to a new flexible bomber model, which the airmen insist on naming after Billy Mitchell despite High Command's protests. We shall fund these development efforts.
Quesada's Close Air Support
General Quesada has a very hands-on attitude to directing Air missions, and his approach to air tactics is near revolutionary for our young Air Force. Let us fund his efforts and help distribute his manuals to pilots so our CAS doctrine may be the best in the world!
New Arms Factories
The main trouble with creating a military industry is that facilities under our control were already reduced from the Great Depression to reduce redundancies. We have had to expand facilities and repurpose old buildings in order to manufacture parts needed for heavy weapons in our territory.
New Tank Assemblies
Armoured warfare will change the face of the battlefield forever. We cannot sid idly as the world rearms, and with the Tank, we may be able to beat our enemies in a matter of weeks instead of years. As such, it would be a priority for us to build more of these deadly machines, so that we may be ready for fight for freedom not only in America, but on the whole world.
Create the Women's Army Corps
Despite protests from socially conservative elements in the US Army, the Commander-in-Chief has stood firm in defence of the Women's Army Corps. Led by Secretary of the Department of Health, Oveta Hobby, the WAC has received more than twice their requested number of volunteers. Women's Auxiliary will help maintain and safeguard our weapons of war, and keep our massive supply chain working.
Rifle Improvements
While the M1 Johnson managed to see us through the Civil War, its flaws were as noticeable when it was adopted as they are now. However, with the criticism we have gathered during the civil war, we have contacted the original designer, and he has assured us that by redesigning the barrel, gas cylinder, and front sight assembly, he will make the Garand an even more reliable and deadly weapon.
'This We'll Defend'
The US Army has reached a new peak in both size and efficiency. We can rely on them to defend our values both domestically and abroad, and in the process, High Command has managed to learn some valuable lessons that give us an edge over inexperienced militaries.
Malin Craig's plan is the only plan that guarantees a large fighting force in the shortened time frame we have given.
Hierarchical Reorganisation
The meritocracy in the US Army has fallen to the wayside for nepotism and incompetence. We must reaffirm the code of the US Army and ingrain this in our staff hierarchy.
Joint Chiefs of Staff
The disputes common in the Federal inter-service politics persist in our own government. In order to avoid this interdisciplinary contention from spilling over, we must ensure that all our Chiefs of Staff are given equal attention.
Establish a New Officer Training Centre
With the immediate danger posed to our most prestigious officer schools, we must reorganise and fund new schools in safer territory.
A Gun for Every Hand
A priority of General Craig is not only the Mobilisation of large infantry units, but the consistency of supplies for them. As such, he insists that a second budget needs to be drawn, one that favours Weapon contractors heavily to produce more equipment so our troops at the front may be able to fight with a full kit against any threat.
Engineer Corps Expansion
We are finally able to provide enough infrastructure and planning to provide Engineering Corps in the field. Through coordinating our intelligence network with scouting and surveillance systems, we are able to ensure that non-combat elements in battle are accounted for and able to complete their tasks.
American Auto Industry
Since the invention of the automobile, it has been taken up in earnest by the people of America. Most of the factories for cars are in the North, where the syndicalists are running things. However, J. Kaiser has moved from the North, so we should encourage other companies to follow in his footsteps.
Spaatz's Air Superiority
General Carl Spaatz has long since been growing in notoriety within the USAAC and USAAF. The success of his ideas on the field of battle have proven that Spaatz's approach to air warfare may be correct, and as such, the Army should focus on promoting and distributing manuals regardless of disagreements with the \
US Navy
The American navy, an institution whose history is so deeply interwoven with that of the nation as a whole, has been in steady decline after years of neglect. No more! We must again turn our attention to naval affairs.
Great White Fleet
The Great White Fleet was the height to American naval power. We should look back at it for inspiration. A great fleet of battleships and dreadnoughts will ensure we always have naval superiority.
Defending America's Trade
Trade is the lifeblood of America. We should focus our naval doctrine on making sure that it is protected from enemy raids.
Fleet Carrier Plan
Carriers are the wave of the future. We should invest in their research and construction to better project naval power.
Battleship Development
Battleships are the kings of the high seas. We should start research into new models with bigger guns and better anti-air protection.
Battle Cruiser Development
Battle-cruisers present a middle balance between heavy battleships and faster cruisers. We should ensure we have some in our navy.
Coast Guard
Restoring the Coast Guard will ensure that trade moves smoothly, criminals are stopped at sea, and those in danger are rescued.
Light Cruiser Development
Lighter cruisers are important in anti-air operations, as well as attacking enemy destroyers and submarines. We should ensure our navy has a handful of these in order to stay balanced.
Naval Aviation
Naval aviation is the future of warfare on the high seas. We should ensure that our air designs are capable of being launched from carriers and destroying the enemy fleet without even endangering our own.
Expand Dockyards
Our dockyards are somewhat inadequate to fight a war on their own. We need to ensure that new naval production facilities are constructed to support the war effort.
Submarine Development
Submarines allow us to wreak havoc on enemy shipping and heavy ships. We should ensure that our designs stay up to date against enemy destroyers and anti-submarine tactics.
Liberty Ships
Our shipyards, previously dedicated to commercial shipping, can easily be converted to produce massive numbers of convoys to supply our allies around the world.
Maritime Industry
America has a naval tradition rivalled only by the great powers of Europe, and an equally illustrious history of naval production and innovation. With the dockyards and merchant marine now much improved, let us focus on streamlining and better integrating the increasingly national process of naval production.
New Admirals
In the face of crisis, many admirals committed the greatest treason - desertion. We should train a new generation of naval leaders to ensure our continued maritime dominance.
Create the WAVES
Women can serve many auxiliary roles in the navy, freeing up men for combat duty. While this might be socially controversial, it will significantly help the war effort.
Improve the Marine Corps
The Marine Corps was the epitome of American power projection around the globe. From the shores of Tripoli to the halls of Montezuma, the Marines were always there. We should ensure they have modern equipment and training.
Expand the Marine Corps
We need to enlarge the Marine Corps, and ensure that they are able to project our power around the globe.
Naval Training
While the Naval Academy in Annapolis was destroyed in the fighting of the Civil War, we still have plenty of facilities able to train a new generation of naval leaders and sailors.
Semper Fi
Semper Fidelis means \
America Rules the Waves
Following our extensive investments into naval research and construction, we have regained our place as one of the world's leading naval powers. Anchors away!
Back in Business
The nation has seen some troubles which meant it could not act as an international power, not as it deserves to be - but that has now changed. America is ready to re-enter the world stage.
Rebuild the Monroe Doctrine
The troubles in Europe and elsewhere are not ours. America belongs to the New World, and to that end we must endeavour to stake out our place in it. It is our destiny to be the master of North America and protector of South America, and woe betide those who would stand in our way.
Defend the New World
The first step in achieving dominance is to ensure that our future enemies and allies are fully aware of our intentions. Welcome our presence or not, however, we are coming.
Rightful Domain
North America is our first and foremost concern. We will not condone hostile nations on America's borders, and we must prepare our military to guard our domain by both land and sea.
Treaties of Cooperation
The League of American States will be an organisation of friendly neutrals in North and South America, one where the United States is both protector and kindly guide.
New American Imperialism
Americans are not imperialists - we go only where we are welcomed, and enforce our will only where it is necessary to maintain order in the West. For the benefit of all.
Pax Americana
The great struggle of the New World is over, and in the end, we witnessed the survival of genuine American democracy. With our industry reinvigorated, our military unmatched, and our resolve unbreakable, we will announce to the world that the 20th century will not be owned by that of Paris or Berlin but the start of an American era. Only under the United States' leadership will the world be able to experience peace and stability.
Enter the Fray
America belongs on the world stage, and while we are hesitant to be drawn into foreign alliances we will not hesitate to use our military might to stamp out threats around the world that will eventually find us.
The Arsenal of Democracy
The Good Neighbour Policy necessitates an internal programme to ready arms for future conflicts. This Arsenal of Democracy, as the President calls it, will enable us to supply war material to even the hardest to reach places in South America in service of fighting tyranny and Syndicalism.
Longer Reach
If we are to project our power onto the rest of the world, we must achieve the ability to do so through our naval power.
On the Beach
Our enemies must fear American soldiers landing on their shores, and to that end we must work to ensure that we have the skill and power to take advantage of our longer reach.
Working with our Allies
American expertise must be put at the disposal of our allies - or, at least, the enemies of our enemies. If they fight better, then together we stand a chance of victory.
The American Century
The great ideological struggle for world peace has established the explicit power of the American industry and economy. America is essential to victory over tyranny and Syndicalism and will be essential in preserving world peace should we succeed.
Fortress America
America has been through hell, and the time has not yet come for us to become embroiled in foreign difficulties. We must look to our home, ensure it is in order, and defend our walls should enemies come knocking on our doors.
Man the Walls
The first step in our defence must be to ensure our walls are well-guarded. The world should fear American military might, but only if they choose to engage us.
Business of Neutrality
Neutrality has its benefits in that our enemies are few, and thus our trading partners are plentiful. If America is to build itself into a true world power, we must do so on the back of the mighty American dollar.
Looking Inward
Never again should America face instability and the threat of civil war. We must look inward, and deal with our internal troubles, rather than gazing out to places Americans don't belong.
America Leaps Forward
With our efforts consolidated and our focus clear, together the United States can leap forward into the coming century - well ahead of the rest of the world.
Peace at Last
Our efforts have borne fruit, and at last America knows the true peace that strength and sacrifice can bring.
The United States of America nearly abandoned isolation to intervene in the European War, but ultimately kept out of the conflict. The result was a Central Powers victory, and the country struggled economically thereafter. European trade declined and the repayment of loans to the Entente was precluded by the German victory. Internationally isolated, the nation now faces mounting internal dissent as the aging and unpopular Smith Administration is challenged by new, radical political forces on the left and right. With malaise at home and only a modest reputation overseas, things aren't looking good for the United States...

The United States of America
Though spared the horrors of the European War, the United States has fared poorly in its aftermath, as the German-led global order has taken hold. The prosperity of neutrality gave way to a stagnant economy in the early 1920s, as President §lWilliam Gibbs McAdoo§!, who had only narrowly succeeded Woodrow Wilson, failed to contain social and labour unrest, making enemies of both conservatives and progressives alike. McAdoo's successor, Republican §mFrank Lowden§!, was faced with an even greater crisis however: the British Revolution severed America's trade links with its largest remaining major trading partner, leading to the collapse of the New York Stock Exchange in April and December 1925, which allowed the Berlin Stock Market to take its place at the forefront of the world economy. Lowden's administration struggled to respond effectively, pursuing generally non interventionist policies and continuing to raise tariffs, further damaging American trade relations.\n\nThe election of §lAl Smith§! in 1928, initially welcomed by progressives and reformers, soon failed to live up to grand expectations. Though Smith successfully stopped the bleeding and stabilised the banking sector, he continued to reject any large interventionist measures, particularly any that would send the budget into deficit. Spurned by the Democrats once again, progressive and labour forces united for the first time with the Socialist Party in a progressive political alliance, the §SFarmer§!-§RLabor§! §rParty§!, which opposed the Smith administration from the left, and forced the 1932 election to the House of Representatives, where Smith was re-elected with their consent. Within the Democratic party meanwhile, a growing opposition bloc headed by §nHuey Long§! united by a common contempt for Smith gains ground, as Long adopts increasingly radical rhetoric in advocating for his \
Parties and Factions
The §lDemocratic§! §cParty§!\nThe oldest continually operating political party in the world, The Democrats have had a storied history, having transformed from a (generally) pro-slavery party, into agrarian and southern opposition to the Republicans, and then into a western, southern, and increasingly urban party with liberal inclinations. Currently, the leading faction of the Democrats are the §lliberals§!, including both President §lAl Smith§! and Vice President §lJoe T. Robinson§!. Generally supported by northern \
Organised Labour
In the United States, §Ylabour unions§! have for decades been divided between multiple competing trade union centres. Ideological conflicts over industrial versus craft unionism, as well as the relationship between labour and political parties and politics in general have often dominated discussion of union activities.\n\nThe oldest and most established of the union centres is the §lAmerican Federation of Labor§!. The AFL, headed by president §lWilliam Green§!, has traditionally been dominated by conservative proponents of §lcraft unionism§!, who have spurned industry-wide organising as well as the organisation of immigrants and unskilled workers. Politically, it has been opposed to the idea of binding labour to any singular political party, opportunistically supporting both Democrats and Republicans (though usually the former) when they serve labour's interests.\n\n§SIndustrial unionists§! who had previously worked within the AFL split from it in 1929 to form the §SCongress of Industrial Organizations§!. The CIO, headed by President §SSidney Hillman§!, supports both organisation by industry as well as the §SFarmer§!-§RLabor§! §rParty§!, to which it is formally affiliated and sends a membership levy. Since its split from the AFL, the CIO has grown rapidly, cornering the steel and automobile industries which the AFL previously declined to organise. The CIO also retains looser and more informal ties to the §RSocialist Party of America§!, from which it draws a significant share of its activists and leadership. A prominent outgrowth within the CIO is the ultra-syndicalist §oTrade Union Educational League§!, led by §oWilliam Z. Foster§! and §oEarl Browder§!. Following Foster's strategy of \

Black Monday Hits America
Catastrophe! Just a few days ago, news reached the shores of the United States by wire, informing us of a massive wave of panic-selling in the Berlin Stock Market, which has led to a general collapse of investor confidence. The persistent sense of dread that has permeated American life - the feeling that, even when the economy has been on an upturn, another two steps backward are just around the corner - has now been proven correct. By the end of the day, a massive sell-off in the New York Stock Market followed.\n\nOn Sunday, the Dow Jones had already been sliding, but had fallen only two percent. By the end of trading on Monday, however, it fell by twelve percent, and on Tuesday, another eleven percent. A full quarter of all investments had been wiped out within two days. Despite William C. Durant and other members of the Rockefeller family attempting to rally the market with a substantial buy-off, the market has continued its plummet, with some economists airing concerns that it may simply continue indefinitely, until there is no more value to lose - investor confidence has been shattered for the foreseeable future.\n\nWhile this stock market crash had almost no impact on the vast majority of Americans, owing to the fact that only a tiny percentage of the population has investments, fear has permeated the middle and working classes as well. Already, massive strikes have been planned by all major unions in protest of the predicted wave of terminations and wage cuts, and demonstrations have begun in the countryside by farmers. North, South, East, and West, exactly the same course of events, and therefore the same atmosphere, pervades now as it did prior to the woes of 1925. As far as the American people can tell, there is simply no hope for the future.
This is just not our year.
Father Charles Coughlin
Three years ago today, Father Charles Coughlin started doing a weekly radio broadcast in America and more than 50 million people turn on their radios and listen. Father Charles Coughlin's CBS Radio Broadcasts
Charles Couglin is a Canadian-born Catholic priest who was assigned to the National Shrine of the Little Flower in Michigan in 1923. He began broadcasting his Sunday Sermons in 1926 on a local radio, and despite working in a relatively small parish he quickly gained traction among Catholics amid KKK violence and general anti-Catholic sentiments.\n\nBy 1930 his program was signed to the Columbia Broadcasting System (CBS) and his weekly topics shifted from religion to politics - taking aim at income inequality, banking, and Jews. He attracted significant controversy, and CBS refused to renew their contract so Coughlin established an independently financed radio network and continued to achieve popularity in the backdrop of the Great Depression. His popularity allowed him to found the National Union for Social Justice in 1934 and his shows drew tens of millions of listeners each week.\n\nThings have come to a head with the NUSJ holding a series of massive rallies in Cleveland Municipal Stadium, where Coughlin predicted the NUSJ will take half of Ohio thanks to the large slate of NUSJ backed candidates. He also presided over the so-called Townsend Convention, demanding further expansions of old-age pensions, and formally endorsed Huey Long for President. Exhausted by the frenzy of activity, Coughlin nearly fainted by the end of his speech.\n\nFather Coughlin's words have divided the Catholic-American world, with even his friend Joseph Kennedy (a leading Massachusetts Democrat and prominent Catholic) attempting to convince him to tone down his rhetoric. Bishop Francis Spellman, at Kennedy's suggestion, as well as other members of the Catholic clergy have sought to muzzle Coughlin, but only Bishop Michael Gallagher of Detroit has the authority to do so. The bishop, a supporter, has refused though he is said to be in poor health. The Federal government has entertained denying him a broadcasting license, but that might further radicalise his followers.
Coughlin is a becoming a danger to the public, shut him down.
I hate what he says, but I defend his right to say it.

Hardliners within MacArthur's clique insist that the US will fall back into civil war without him, however, while Republicans and some Democrats claim MacArthur would be a tyrant if he stayed.

NAACP and FBI Defame Socialists
During the 1930s, a large part of the NAACP's activities were taken up by litigation in favour of African-American rights. This was due to the retreating strength of the black vote and the diminishing ability of African-Americans to reach office after Plessy v. Ferguson. This avenue was also pursued by the syndicalist aligned International Labor Defense, who countered the NAACP for a decade in a competition for the hearts of black voters.\n\nSeeing no other option and being unwilling to ever compromise with socialists, NAACP leader Walter Francis White has decided to cooperate with the FBI in an anti-socialist public relations campaign. Whether this truly motivates civil rights or further dilutes the current remains to be seen.

Division over Big Business Support
It is known by most Democrats that economic reform is necessary to preserve American integrity, to this end Democrats differ on the agency the government must take towards existing industries that are ailing. A proposed civil works programme to electrify the Southwest using hydroelectric power hit a snag as Democrats could not agree on the role of public works in the marketplace.\n\nThe Works would be able to undercut private electricity companies because it would be able to cross state borders and build dams on public land. Conservative Democrats oppose such intrusions as these, saying that it violates states' rights to govern trade. More liberal-minded Democrats hold fast that the necessity and potential of Public Works outweigh the risks.

William McAdoo Has Died
Former President William Gibbs McAdoo has passed away in his home in California. McAdoo's tenure as president was short and troubled. Though he entered office as a labour reformer, his repression of several strikes made him an object of scorn for the left. Having inherited a sluggish economy from his father-in-law, President Wilson, McAdoo's term in office saw a degree of economic recovery.\n\nHowever, it was not enough to prevent an ignominious defeat at the hands of Frank Lowden in 1924, ending the longest continuous period of Democratic control of the presidency since the first civil war

Boulder Dam Completed
'This morning I came, I saw and I was conquered, as everyone would be who sees for the first time this great feat of mankind. Ten years ago the place where we are gathered was a sparse, forbidding desert. In the bottom of a gloomy canyon, whose precipitous walls rose to a height of more than a thousand feet, flowed a turbulent, dangerous river. The mountains on either side of the canyon were difficult of access with neither road nor trail, and their rocks were protected by neither trees nor grass from the blazing heat of the sun.\n\nThe site of Boulder City was a cactus-covered waste. The transformation wrought here in these years is a twentieth-century marvel.' Thus begins [ROOT.GetLeader]'s speech dedicating the creation of Boulder Dam that has finally been completed today.

Willkie Addresses NAACP
President Willkie, despite being a lifelong Democrat, never actively endorsed the Southern Democrat line on race. An early critic of John Nance Garner for failing to appeal to black voters in 1936, Willkie made up for that with a historic speech at the NAACP Convention. Speaking in favour of integration in the military, and also getting a few jabs at Republicans and Democrats for failing to protect black voters from the SPA.\n\nHis speech ended with a support for Jewish rights to democracy, and forewarned that socialists would target them next if antisemitism reached the levels of racism in America. Democrats in Congress are currently ruminating over how to respond, with most wishing to remain silent until next election season.

Whispers and rumours around Washington were finally confirmed today as the White House spokesperson announced that William Borah died in his sleep of a cerebral hemorrhage at age 74. The charismatic leader of the Republican Party found his administration in a quagmire after his failure to successfully resolve the 1937 general strike, and as a result General Douglas MacArthur placed him under house arrest before announcing himself as acting President under dubious circumstances. The legal status of President Borah remains in question, as is the legitimacy of MacArthur's coup, and likely will continue to be debated by Constitutional scholars.\n\nFor the embattled Federal government however, his death was an uncomfortable reminder of the sordid events leading up to the coup and Federal propagandists have been quick to attempt to go onto the next set of news. Opponents of the federal government have also been quick to lash out against MacArthur despite efforts to silence them in Federal strongholds. Some accuse MacArthur of having the former president murdered, rumours have circulated that the once hopeful American reformer had died from the stress of imprisonment and/or denial of proper medical attention by his guards. But for most, the turmoil following MacArthur's coup continues on, as the idealism of Borah's old-school progressive Republicanism may well have died with him...

Al Smith Passes Away
Today, flags on federal buildings across the nation have been lowered to half-mast to mark the passing of former President Al Smith. A controversial and much maligned figure in the years leading up to his death, Smith lived his last years in relative obscurity in New York, avoiding much public attention during the long years of the civil war.\n\nThe former president passed away at 6:45 A.M. after suffering a heart attack earlier in the morning. Since May, Smith's health has been on the decline, primarily due to the passing of the former First Lady. Diagnosed with heat exhaustion by his personal physician Dr. Raymond P. Sullivan, Smith remained away from public life as some of the nation's top physicians attempted to alleviate his conditions. As the former president's condition became increasingly critical, a call went out for Bishop Francis A. McIntyre to administer the last rites of the Roman Catholic Church.\n\nIn spite of the inspirational nature of Smith's humble rise from newsboy and fishmonger to governor and president, he is despised in many circles of American life. Held responsible by many for the civil war, many of Smith's accomplishments, such as the recovery of the economy prior to Black Monday and the passage of the Costigan-Wagner Anti-Lynching Act, have been overshadowed by his presidency's ignominious end. Nevertheless, Smith privately hoped that history (and God) would absolve him, and vindicate his actions in office as the best possible recourse against the conditions of the day. Only time will tell if that is the case.
Perhaps history will be kinder to him...
Wendell Willkie Passes Away
Today the nation mourns the death of its president, Wendell Willkie. For the past couple of months, the president has been declining in health, however it was hoped that he would make a swift recovery after his heart attack in August. Unfortunately, these hopes were unfounded: years of bad dieting and heavy drinking, charming to reporters in the 1940 election but ever more problematic during his presidency finally caught up to him. His heart attacks had become chronic, and after his hospitalisation on the fourth, he experienced several more before finally passing away today.\n\nShortly after the president's passing, Vice President Alben Barkley took the oath of office. Not long after, an emergency meeting among the Democrats nominated Barkley as Willkie's replacement for the 1944 election, now only a month away. President Barkley has decreed that the week of the president's funeral be declared a period of national mourning to remember and acknowledge the true patriotism and love President Willkie had for the United States.
His soul goes marching on...
Floyd Olson Passes Away
Whispers and rumours around Washington were finally confirmed today as the White House spokesperson announced that Floyd Olson has died today from a resurgent cancer. The charismatic leader of the Farmer-Labor Party found his administration in a quagmire after his failure to successfully resolve the Crisis of 1937, and not long after, he fell into a coma, further dividing the country and bringing it closer to the precipice.\n\nAfter a month as acting president, Quentin Roosevelt has now finally been formally sworn in as President of the United States. Olson's death however has generated substantial controversy surrounding the administration's legitimacy however, as rumours abound on the left that the former president was poisoned on behalf of the establishment. Roosevelt's subsequent retreat from Olson's radical platform has been presented as evidence that this is the case, and few expect that his death will do anything to alleviate the growing national crisis. Nevertheless, a state funeral in Washington has been planned, as Olson will be afforded the full honours granted to a passed president.

MacArthur vs Byrd
With the conclusion of the Second American Civil War and reconstruction underway, the term of the interim President [USA.GetLeader] has come to an end. A sense of normalcy is beginning to be felt across the nation as the democratic process returns to the United States.\n\nPerhaps one of the most popular candidates, Douglas MacArthur, hero of the Second American Civil War, will represent the Republican Party. Hailed as the Cincinnatus of America's darkest hours, MacArthur's military coup may have raised concerns regarding his commitment to American democracy, but citizens were relieved when MacArthur stepped down after his victory. The former Commander-in-Chief of the Federal army is indeed a favoured candidate, with many seeing MacArthur as the fist needed to rebuild and restore America's presence around the world. Celebrities and even some Democrat politicians have voiced their support for the War President. Election observers and advisors have mostly come to the conclusion that MacArthur's victory will be that of a landslide and the former helm of the nation will lead it once more.\n\nRepresenting the Democratic Party will be Harry Byrd, newspaper publisher, and head of the Democratic Party in Virginia. During his time as Virginia state governor, he pushed through constitutional amendments that streamlined state government and allowed for more efficient use of tax dollars. Popular among southern conservatives, Byrd is a vehement anti-desegregationist and has vowed to keep southern institutions segregated.\n\nWith the full resumption of elections in the United States, the time has come for American voters to make their decisions at polls across the country. After a long evening of counting, the final result is...
MacArthur wins an overwhelming victory!
