For the second time in its history, the unity of the United States was tested once more. Against the Workers' Congress of Chicago and the People's Government of Baton Rouge, President Alf Landon commanded the American nation in its desperate bid for survival. Despite the reactionary and radical elements that sought to undermine American freedom, in the true spirit of democracy - the Republican President Landon has announced that the 1940 elections will proceed as usual. Seeking a second term, most observers have predicted that Landon will secure the White House for another four years. The wartime presidency has shown remarkable resilience and determination in the face of such a national crisis. At a time when Americans held such little faith in their government, it was Landon's voice on the radio that encouraged loyalists to remain loyal to the federal government.\n\nRunning against him will be Wendell Willkie of the Democratic Party. While few think that the Democratic Party will be able to contest the popularity of the Republican leadership, it is never too late for a comeback. The lawyer and former executive has vowed to carry on President Landon's policies regarding government social security and has promised a program of full employment based on cooperation between the private and public sectors. Willkie's platform also advocates for America's growing role in the world and, surprisingly for a Democrat, support for the civil rights movement, vowing that he will see the integration of the American Armed Forces.\n\nWith the full resumption of free elections in the United States, the time has come for American voters to make their decisions at polls across the country. Vandenberg vs Hoover
In an unprecedented move that shocked foreign and domestic observers, MacArthur's military coup of the duly elected President in early 1937 threw the nation into the civil war. While many saw the strength in MacArthur's military clique in the months and days leading up to the civil war, few anticipated the general would place himself as acting President, thus undoing everything the founding fathers stood for.\n\nWith the arrest of the dictatorial MacArthur, democracy has finally been restored. The incumbent Republican from Michigan has promised a return to sensible conservative government. A pragmatic conservative and isolationist, he has announced a reconstruction platform based on private initiative with modest government support, as well as non-interference in global affairs. Running against him will be Conservative Democrat Herbert Hoover. Hoover has leaned on his reputation as a humanitarian, engineer, and administrator, promising a swift physical reconstruction, and campaigning on a platform of volunteerism as the basis for private-public partnerships. As the only member of the Smith Administration to survive with his reputation largely intact, Hoover is proving a formidable opponent to the incumbent President.\n\nWith the full resumption of free elections once more in the United States, the time has come for American voters to make their decisions at polls across the country. After a long evening of counting, the final result is...
Vandenberg wins.
Hoover wins.

Hoover vs Taft
Horrifically mauled in the bloodletting of the Second American Civil War, the American nation lies stunned in the appalling aftermath of total war. Across the nation, signs of recovery are beginning to show in the form of soup kitchens, relief centres, and clinics. Slowly but surely, the American nation is recovering and in accordance with the American democratic tradition, the incumbent President Herbert Hoover has announced his bid for presidency in the 1944 elections.\n\nAscending to the presidency after the civil war, Hoover has shown that he is more than competent to handle the position of commander-in-chief. Hoover intends to seek the Democratic domination for the White House for an additional four more years. Pledging to expand his successful reconstruction policies to now include the gradual reconstruction of the American continent, Hoover has marched into this election confident in his chances of continuing his broadly popular moderate policies.\n\nRunning against him and hoping to topple the Democratic dominance is Republican Robert Taft. Taft is the son of a former American president, former President William Howard Taft. As the leader of the American conservative coalition, the former lawyer and Senator received the Republican Party's nomination for the election of 1944. He has consistently spoken out against American intervention in the world's conflicts, arguing that America's priority and place is its recovery at home. A tireless worker with a variety of public and political interests, Taft and the Republicans have worked relentlessly to secure the votes needed to bring down the dominance of progressive Democrats.\n\nWith the full resumption of free elections in the United States, the time has come for American voters to make their decisions at polls across the country. After a long evening of counting, the final result is...
Taft wins.
Hoover wins.

Four years have passed since [USA.GetNameDef] last elected a president - which means that Douglas MacArthur's term is almost up, and that the time has come again to convene an assembly to determine who will sit as the nation's leader. The American nation has begun the process of national recovery with the memories of war and chaos still fresh in the minds of all its citizens. In accordance with the democratic tradition, President MacArthur has announced his desire to run for a second term in the upcoming election of 1944.\n\nPresident MacArthur's term has been spent mostly trying to escape his actions of 1936 as his administration found itself constantly opposed by the Democrats. The memories of MacArthur's military clique still linger in the halls of Congress, with the Democrat opposition, in particular, denouncing MacArthur as an authoritarian demagogue. The establishment Republicans have lost ground in several states for their concessions to Hearst's clique of wealthy business owners - perhaps a sign that MacArthur may not be able to clinch a second term. Nonetheless despite these setbacks, MacArthur has spoken confidently on the campaign trail - hoping to continue to capitalise on his wartime popularity as perhaps America's most influential general since Ulysses S. Grant.\n\nThe Democratic opposition has nominated Georgian Congressman Richard Russell Jr., who hopes to rally his conservative white voting base in the upcoming election. An avowed segregationist and perhaps one of the loudest voices against racial integration, Russell has promised that should he secure the presidency - he will ensure that states continue to keep their rights and traditions of segregation. Russell's outspoken white supremacist views have certainly placed him at odds with those seeking greater racial equality in the United States. Furthermore, Russell has also stressed that his Reconstruction will see the continued harsh, uncompromising position towards former SPA members and the American syndicalists.\n\nWith the full resumption of free elections in the United States, the time has come for American voters to make their decisions at polls across the country. After a long evening of counting, the final result is...
MacArthur wins.
Russell Jr wins.

Across the country, signs of recovery are beginning to show in the form of soup kitchens, relief centres, and clinics. Slowly but surely, the American nation is recovering, and in accordance with the American democratic tradition, the incumbent President Scott W. Lucas pushes for a second term.\n\nRepresenting the Democratic Party, Scott W. Lucas hopes to keep the White House in Democratic hands for the next four years. The Lucas administration saw the gradual integration of the American armed forces and several important agricultural reforms. However, Lucas has been stuck between a rock and a hard place within his own party: Democrats both to his right and his left have criticised his administration, which seemingly has failed to please either side. Nonetheless, Lucas passed his Commission on Civil Rights - marking a substantial breakthrough in American racial relations in the post-war era.\n\nHoping to return the White House to the Republicans is none other than Charles Halleck of Indiana. Halleck's popularity snowballed during the civil war as an outside opponent to federal government management of individual welfare, a staunch opponent of the eastern establishment. Halleck has, in particular, criticised Lucas for his handling of strikes during his presidency. The former lawyer and prosecuting attorney has pledged his support to the Civil Rights movement and has promised to ensure the normalisation of racial relations in the United States.\n\nWith the full resumption of free elections in the United States; the time has come for American voters to make their decisions at polls across the country. After a successful term, President Robert Taft announced his intention to run in the upcoming electoral race of 1948. The signs of war devastation are becoming increasingly uncommon as government and civilian institutions are being re-established in the wake of the great conflict. And so, as America eagerly anticipates for her next commander-in-chief, many speculate that the issues between the two candidates will involve the completion of Reconstruction and America's role in the world's affairs.\n\nHoping to keep Republican dominance of the White House for the next four years is current President Robert A. Taft. As the American conservative coalition leader, the Republican president from Ohio hopes to keep the policy programs of his Reconstruction alive in the next four years. However, after the civil war, his regulation of unions and the workplace has undoubtedly earned him criticism from lingering dissident elements across the country. Pledging to finish the Reconstruction and prioritise America first instead of the international world, Taft hopes to continue upholding his image as a tireless worker for the American people.\n\nThe Democrat opposition to the Republicans is the former governor and senator of Kentucky, Happy Chandler. Sympathetic to the plight of the labour movement, Chandler has sided with the unionisation and organisation of miners in the past, making him a popular candidate amongst those in the Steel Belt. Nonetheless, he is not without controversy - the African-American community is troubled by Chandler's past refusal to repeal the poll taxes and end lynching. While he has promised to build new race relations and smooth integration in the post-war era, some point out his close ties with Harry Byrd, an avowed segregationist.\n\nWith the full resumption of free elections in the United States, the time has come for American voters to make their decisions at polls across the country. After a long evening of counting, the final result is...
Taft wins.
Chandler wins.

With the election of 1948, many in the United States are anxious as to whether or not President Douglas MacArthur will seek a third term. The beloved wartime general who had overseen the country in its darkest days and its current period of Reconstruction shocked his dissenters with his proclamation that he would not seek a third term. In the halls of Congress, MacArthur announced his official retirement from the military and politics - citing age and health and his desire to return home after years of service. Citizens from Washington, D.C. to San Francisco restlessly follow the presidential campaigns between the Republican and Democrat parties.\n\nSeeking to continue the Republican hold on the White House is Republican Charles A. Halleck from Indiana. The former lawyer and prosecuting attorney is a strong proponent of civil rights and has constantly pointed out his opponent Happy Chandler's ties to fierce segregationist Harry F. Byrd. Securing the support of interest groups like the NAACP, Halleck has promised his supporters that should he be elected - he will take measures to begin the process of racial integration and the eventual eradication of segregation.\n\nRepresenting the Democratic Party and hoping to end Republican dominance in the White House is Kentuckian senator and governor. Happy Chandler. A moderate Democrat straddling the line between party factions, he has succeeded in unifying the Democratic cohort behind him. Nonetheless, he is not without controversy - the African-American community is troubled by Chandler's past refusal to repeal the poll taxes and end lynching. Superweapons on a Budget
In the last few years, our military research has focused on the potential for internal conflict, narrowing our focus and budget for longer-term projects. Three plans are presented to the military high command to meet and exceed the military projects of our rivals. The first is a rocket by Goddard theoretically capable of delivering explosives from miles away without risking pilot lives.\n\nThe second is Oppenheimer's planned theoretical bomb using radioactive heavy metals as researched in Austria and Germany. Oppenheimer's Bomb a Success

The breath goes now.
Reich's Failed Explosion
After many delays and several attempts to obfuscate the general staff, Wilhelm Reich's bomb project has been discontinued and it seems millions of dollars have been wasted on bunk. This became apparent to Reich's observers when tests showed that his energy, named Orgone, could induce exothermic reactions that only he and his associates could see.\n\nThe bomb itself was a hollow shell with layers of metal covering that never did explode, save for its collapse when Reich attempted to destroy it during the investigation. This embarrassment is currently making the rounds in the papers. This embarrassment is currently making its rounds in the papers.

Garner-McNary Bill Introduced
With the blessing of President Smith, Republican Senator Charles McNary and Speaker of the House John Nance Garner have introduced a new unemployment relief legislation package. Many in Congress feel that the package does not go nearly far enough, while others wonder how America - in the midst of a massive economic crisis - will possibly ever pay for it.\n\nThe presence of Senators from the Farmer-Labor Party, particularly in the SPA, as well as those aligned with Huey Long complicates things immensely. Even with Smith's support, it's unknown if Garner-McNary has a real chance of passing.
We shall see.
Long and Farmer-Labor Demand Changes
As expected, the early challenges to the Garner-McNary Bill have come from the Longists and Farmer-Labor. Huey Long and his informal caucus have demanded a vast increase in the social security provisions the bill provides, provisions most other Senators say America could never afford. John Reed and the SPA, meanwhile, scoff at the provisions of the bill, which they say does little to protect workers or fundamentally change the reality of the depression.\n\nThough not as set against the bill as their radical comrades in the SPA, the non-socialist Farmer-Labor caucus is sympathetic to Reed's view, and will have to be accommodated if they are to be swayed to our side. All three groups have attracted a lot of media attention, adding to the general sense of disorder and tension in Congress.
Interesting.
Senators Break Ranks
After weeks of negotiations, a number of establishment Senators have broken ranks over the coming vote on the Garner-McNary Bill - most notably Democratic Senator Robert Wagner, who says he will not vote for the bill unless protections for federal unemployment insurance are re-added.\n\nMany other Democratic and Republican Senators are concerned about the influence of the Longists and Farmer-Labor, and claim they will not vote for the bill if any concessions at all are made to either group. Others say that not courting either the Longists or Farmer-Labor will make passage difficult, if not impossible. President Smith will need to intervene in order to save the bill.

General MacArthur's Plan
There is growing concern that America is descending into a possible civil war, and that - despite all our efforts to maintain security - supporters of Huey Long and the SPA simply have too much influence in some parts of the country. The Barkley Plan
Alben Barkley, Democrat and junior Senator for Kentucky, has introduced a bill which will see the relief efforts largely funded by taxing American corporations - in exchange for hefty tax considerations down the line, once the economy has recovered. This has caused considerable controversy in some corners, especially among Longist and SPA supporters.\n\nOthers say it would be far too easy for the next government to reverse the decision, leaving the corporations holding the bag and even worse off than they were before. America Demands Port Fees
It came as a surprise to the Canadian government, but the ambassador from [USA.GetNameDef] has demanded that the Canadian government immediately begin repaying the port fees incurred by us in the years following the British Revolution. While the Americans are gripped in an economic crisis, one Canada has, to an extent, avoided, they must know the Canadians can never repay the fees... not all at once, at least.\n\nSince the retreat of the Royal Navy, there has been a tacit agreement that the fees wouldn't be fully repaid until the Home Islands were recaptured. For the Americans to demand it now, they must either be desperate or must be catering to the more warlike and isolationist elements in their government.
Whatever the reason, we cannot do as they demand.
Canada Refuses
The Canadian government has responded to the demand with a flat refusal. The fees, they say, were never meant to be fully repaid until the Home Islands were retaken.\n\nEven so, their refusal has done its job and fired up the isolationist elements of the American government. President Smith's government has the support it needs, at the cost of relations with the Canadians.
So be it.
Compromise with America?
There has been a break in the chilly relations with the American government since their demand for port fee repayment. They have approached us with an offer: economic assistance now, and an agreement to increase trade with the Entente, in exchange for the rest of the fees being delayed until the Home Isles are retaken... which was, aides point out, the original deal to begin with.\n\nIt might be a way to restore goodwill with our southern neighbours, and even help them, though some are suggesting that there's no point in shovelling our limited funds into a bottomless pit. America is lost, they say, and we should look to our own first.
We agree to the compromise.
They are on their own.
Canada Agrees to Compromise
The Canadian government has reluctantly agreed to the compromise, giving us what payment they can now and accepting the deferment until the Home Isles have been retaken. In exchange, a trade agreement has been put in place with the Entente, something that's likely beneficial for us all.\n\nThe main downside is that the agreement has been viewed as treachery by the Longists and Farmer-Labor, both of which claim our corrupt government has betrayed the very people they fired up only moments before.
We'll take what we can get.

On this particular July 4th, the guns have fallen silent on the American continent, the soldier has returned home, and the lights on the city streets slowly relit. The great civil war that had challenged the unity of the United States for the second time in its short life span has finally ended.\n\nWhile the nation has suffered dramatically in the conflagration, the United States is slowly climbing back on its feet. While not every family can afford the traditional barbeques, the traditional fireworks and parades have returned. President [FROM.GetLeader] gave an official address from [USA.Capital.GetCapitalVictoryPointName] thanking the United States military for their diligence in restoring order and protecting the United States from outside threats. In addition, he included a message of praise for the American people, honouring all who served the nations as combatants or civilians in helping to rebuild the war-torn nation. While there is still much to do, the United States remains a strong nation, and soon, the civil war will be a moment in the history books, a terrible fragment of the past. With this new independence day, the United States honours the restoration of the union and a new era of prosperity and freedom to come. And now, Independence Day reminds them, that once again the United States will be a beacon of democracy to the rest of the world.

MacArthur's Last Speech
Sensing that he would soon be arrested, General Douglas MacArthur has elected to make one final speech before Congress, convincing several of his former allies to do him one last favour. Wearing his old Army uniform, the former Chief of Staff of the United States Army reflected upon the course of the war, his coming fate, and informed the audience that he would not resist arrest. Instead he said that he would accept imprisonment if it would bring the nation back together again without further bloodshed. He stated that he only did what he did in order to protect America, and was grateful for his many years in service as a \
'Old soldiers never die, they simply fade away.'
Douglas MacArthur Arrested
With the Syndicalists and the Longists finally subdued, only [ACC.GetNameDef] and MacArthur's Federal Government remained standing. Both sides, exhausted from the horrendous conflict that had torn apart a nation, have indicated to one another regarding a potential unification by compromise and not arms.\n\nGeneral Douglas MacArthur, the Commander-in-Chief of the Federal Army during the Civil War, shocked the American continent when he announced his resignation from the presidency. The general publicly announced his appointment of Senator Arthur Vandenberg as his successor and his subsequent withdrawal from presidential affairs. While MacArthur's retirement made him appear as a modern-day American Cincinnatus in the eyes of his followers, to some Americans, MacArthur's moves were viewed with the highest of suspicions.\n\nNonetheless, it would appear that [ACC.GetNameDef] has completely subverted MacArthur's gambit. With the American nation waiting anxiously for news of the eventual reunification, the government of [ACC.GetNameDef] sent a strongly worded note to the Federal Government - demanding that MacArthur be tried for his crimes against the American people in exchange for unification. After all, it was MacArthur's military coup of the American government in the bleak winter of 1937 that threw the nation into anarchy. But perhaps most surprising is that the general's choice, newly appointed President Arthur Vandenberg, has been one of the most vocal voices calling for MacArthur's arrest. President Vandenberg has taken to the national radio to denounce MacArthur as a Caesarean dictator, receiving praise and support from [ACC.GetNameDef]. Politically outmanoeuvred and faced with a country desperate for peace, the former commander-in-chief has no choice but to comply with his arrest.

The Presidential Succession
In an ironic, and perhaps fitting, turn of events, the General who once deposed and imprisoned the President in a coup has now himself been arrested. With MacArthur now out of the way, the question looming in Washington is who should be President for the remainder of the 1936-1940 term. Constitutionally speaking, when the President dies or otherwise leaves office before the completion of their term, their Vice President takes up office. However, the MacArthur administration regarded both the presidency and vice presidency as vacant throughout the entire war, leaving him as acting president as secretary of state. This question has brought a new round of partisan bickering as Quentin Roosevelt and his supporters argue that he is the legitimate President of the United States and that the Sacramento Government was a continuation of the Constitutional government throughout the civil war.\n\nFor many former Federalists however, this question cuts deep into the heart of the question of the legitimacy of the Washington government during the Civil War and many argue that Roosevelt's challenge threatens to destabilise the peace and reconciliation process. It would be better to instead allow for Acting President [Root.GetLeader] to serve out the remainder of the term until new elections can be held. Thankfully, both sides have decided to resolve this question peacefully, and it has quickly gone before the Supreme Court. After hearing legal arguments from both sides, the court has announced its verdict that...
...the coup was unconstitutional - Roosevelt is the rightful president.
...the appointment was legitimate - [ROOT.GetLeader] is the rightful president.
Status of the US Army
The defence of the United States has always been an uphill battle. Stretched thin against the vast breadth of the North American continent, the United States Army has had little chance to distinguish itself throughout its 160 year history. It won the bare minimum of victories to maintain American independence during the Revolution and the War of 1812. It performed admirably against a corrupt regime in the Mexican-American War, but half of those forces would provide the seed for the fledgling Confederate Army during the ensuing Civil War. More recently the Army performed barely adequately to subdue the heavily outgunned Spanish and struggled to suppress the half-starved Filipino Insurrection more than 30 years ago.\n\nPrevented from joining in the Weltkrieg on either side, it has suffered in both doctrine and technology, with very few tanks and a small Air Corps subsidiary to the ground forces. With the hobbled lion that was the British Empire on the northern frontier and a syndicalist stronghold poised in the south, the U.S. Army must be asked to defend the Republic from enemies within and without, and few agree that they are up to the task.
They'll have to suffice.
Status of the US Navy
The United States Navy, long the darling child of the American defence establishment has been a strong force in global maritime affairs for nearly fifty years. A rival even to the vaunted Kaiserliche Marine and Royal Navy at their height in the Weltkrieg, it has defended America's shores and sallied forth to spread stability and democracy for nigh on 160 years. From John Paul Jones' raid on the British mainland to the Battle of Manila Bay, the Navy has provided the security needed by the republic from those that would infringe upon our independence from beyond the seas.\n\nAll is not well in the modern day, however. The navy's ships are old, her flagships Weltkrieg-era dreadnoughts even as Germany and the Syndicalists engage in a new naval arms race, and the tattered remnants of the Royal Navy lick their wounds. The new dreadnoughts have been commissioned at the suggestion of senator Benjamin Tillman, along with many projects of the twenties converted to aircraft carriers due to the Great Depression, but the Navy is nowhere near ready to take on the imperial Japanese fleet.\n\nThe Marine Corps fares better, hardened as they are by constant action in tropical locales, but they are small, only a few regiments strong, and are powerless to affect increasing tension at home from their far-flung island bases. The honour guard in Washington, D.C. look increasingly powerless as violence in the nation's capital increases. Our White ships might dominate the waves but many question whether it will be enough to face the gathering storm on the horizon.
Semper Fortis?
Army Doctrinal Debate
With the Outbreak of the American Civil War, the Army High Command has been thrown into chaos. Now not only is a reform plan to deal with the imminent crisis necessary, but also urgent as the rebellious states threaten the unity of America. Luckily for us, several staff members had already been advocating for reform plans since the early 1920s, and they have been summoned by High Command to a meeting for them to lay out their plans.\n\nAfter a session full of army formalities, 4-Star General Malin Craig presented a restructuring and mobilisation plan which would focus on trying to arm as many men as possible while improving and enhancing the High Command to have an edge in planning over our enemies. While many conservative members applauded his traditionalist stance, Major General Adna R. Chaffee criticised his stance, quoting several instances in which planning and mass mobilisation didn't earn the victory to the French in the Weltkrieg, and instead advocating for the adoption of the \
Let us choose well.
Air Force Independence Debate
The Air Force has remained as a mostly token part of the Army, with barely any investment going towards it during the 1920s and 1930s. However, air developments during these last decades have proven that a strong air force is a vital asset for an army who wishes to come out victorious from the battlefield.\n\nUnfortunately, the Army High Command in many aspects refuses to acknowledge this, and as a result, sparks conflict with many Air Branch generals who wish to direct the development of their own branch. With the country's integrity at stake, the High Command has decided to negotiate with the Air Force Generals, and the result of the negotiations is pretty clear: The Air Branch will not stand for a continuation of the Status Quo, and demands that at best, their force is given significant autonomy from the Army and reorganise as the United States Army Air Force, and at worse for the United States Army Air Corps to be expanded and supported to suit the needs of the battlefield.\n\nWith the High Command being undecided on the issue, the final decision has been sent to the War Department, where it has been forwarded to the Secretary of War to decide on the matter.
Let us choose well.
Adna R. Chaffee Dies
After months of struggle in the hospital, Major General Adna R. Chaffee has unfortunately passed away due to cancer. Considered by many as the father of American Armored Corps, the mentor of many tank crews and officers and one of the main reformers of the US Army, his death has taken most of the High Command by surprise.\n\nLuckily, he had laid out his plans to High Command clearly, so while his death is a tragic turn of events, it won't hinder our army reforms.
His Expertise will be missed Nonetheless.
Tank Competition
While our tanks in the assembly line have proven useful, Chaffee considers that their role is too spread for them to be effective. Right now our tanks are too slow to be used to take advantage of breakthroughs, but not armoured enough to sustain anti-tank projectiles, let alone tank-to-tank combat.\n\nSince achieving both is simply unachievable with the current state of our nation, we can however focus on one aspect so that our tanks may serve a specific role.
Striking Fast is our Priority.
Striking Hard is our Priority.
Seizure of Civilian Trucks
After Chaffee announced his Motorisation program for the Army, a proposal was sent to the Secretary of War by the War Department to decide on the requisition of civilian vehicles in order to supply our fast-growing army. With his approval, we have begun seizing vehicles from the civilian populace, although to our surprise, some proud patriots line up next to our storages to volunteer their vehicles for the incoming fight.\n\nWhile not all their vehicles have proven to be useful for us, we have managed to requisition a fair amount of trucks which can either be modified to transport troops with ease or which are sturdy enough to transport our troops at once.
We thank you for your service.
Production Prioritisation
As the American industry hums along McNair's artillery designs, a new debacle has begun among members of the High Command. Front Line reports of complete squads being wiped out by enemy dive bombings have been a concern of the staff since the beginning of the American Civil War, but the quick development of armoured elements in the enemy forces are overwhelming our army of mostly barely-equipped grunts.\n\nAfter asking for extra resources to the War Department, extra investments have been authorised for the Army, but they'd need to be addressed to a particular type of countermeasures against the enemy tactics, and so the High Command must choose wisely what it shall invest it in...
Anti Tank Guns are vital.
Anti Air Guns are more important.
First Paradrop Exercise
While technically speaking, the first paradropping exercises were practised in 1930 with biplanes dropping machine gun squads, today a major breakthrough has been achieved in the airborne department. After finishing a rigorous conditioning and training programme started two weeks ago, a lottery was made to decide the jumping order of the experimental paradropping platoon made up of volunteers.\n\nWhen the Douglas C-33 took off from Langley Airfield and finally was put into position to start the experiment, Second Lieutenant William T. Ryder became the first American Paratrooper after making his jump and landing near Fort Benning. The second man, however, refused to jump, and so the first enlisted man to become a paratrooper was Pvt. William N. \

Formation of the First Paratrooper Divisions
With the success of our scheduled mass jumps and with the blessing of General John C.H. Lee, the recently reopened Fort Eustis had begun taking volunteers for paratrooper units. While originally the high training standards and relatively high mortal risk initially caused few volunteers to show up, the high command authorised a triplication of the paratrooper wage as opposed to the foot soldier wage.\n\nSoon enough, the 501st Parachute Battalion was formed, quickly followed by other battalions and regiments. After a week recruitment, the number of volunteers was enough to form 5 paratrooper divisions for us to utilise. While these divisions still lack combat experience, this breakthrough in Airborne tactics should not be underestimated, and the High Command is looking forward to seeing their investment in these divisions pay off.

Conservative Army Elements Complain About the Creation of the USAAF
With the decision from the Secretary of War to form the US Army Air Force, which in consequence granted huge autonomy to the Air Force Officers, many officers have spoken out against the reform.\n\nOne of the main points of contention is that, with the budget already pretty split between the Army and the Navy, the Army Air Force will now more than ever be a money sink that would be badly needed for the ground troops. Regardless of their heated complaint letters to the War Department, the decision has been made, and reforms are ongoing, so there's no going back.
They'll have to learn to respect each other.
MacArthur Attacks the Navy
With more and more government funding being diverted to the navy, Chief of Staff MacArthur has taken up a severe accusation to the Secretary of War: He believes the recent investments on the navy are part of a plot that he had discovered in the early 1930s where the Navy would dominate the Army in the field and just turn the Army into a subordinate garrison force.\n\nWhile the Secretary has managed to calm the General down and reassure him that the army's role in the battlefield will always come first, word of the meeting has gone out and many Admirals, including MacArthur's bitter rival Admiral Hart, are already sending letters asking for MacArthur's resignation.\n\nWhile the relations between MacArthur and navy have been bad for years, this is yet another sad example of how the inter-service rivalry has done nothing but grow in the last few years.
What's wrong with them? We won't win battles by bickering!

Adoption of the M1 Helmet
Ever since the Weltkrieg proved that helmets were vital to protect the infantry from flying fragments of exploded ordnance, the American Army has utilised the British Mk I helmet designed by John L. Brodie, which gave it its current nickname. While adopted, the US never saw a need to mass produce it, and instead continued to buy the model from the British in the cheap during their depression in the early 1920s.\n\nWhile these helmets were effective at the time, our experience in the civil war has proven that even the Brodie is no longer suitable for modern combat and, as such, a research team was created under Major Harold G. Sydenham to look for alternatives. The research team concluded that by removing the Brodie's brim, by adding side pieces and earpiece, and by incorporating the suspension system into a separate inner liner, the new helmet could provide a protection the Brodie could never afford.\n\nThe original test item was known as the TS3, and it received a favourable report from the Infantry Board in the recent weeks. With the approval of the War Department, it will soon enter mass production to supply our rapidly growing army.
Glad we finally got rid of the Brodies.
The Victory Book Campaign
As thousands of new recruits flood into training camps across the country, community librarians have recognised an opportunity to lend their support to our government. Individual libraries sponsored book drives to donate to their local military bases. In the last few months, members of the American Library Association met to discuss a plan for a coordinated nationwide drive to supply the troops with free books.\n\nThe ALA presented their idea to the United Service Organisations and The Red Cross, who have received their idea enthusiastically and begun setting up more than four hundred recreational clubs on the outskirts of military camps. The Red Cross wanted books to send to military hospitals, remote camps with no libraries, their overseas clubs, and prisoners of war. The two organisations decided to split the project's funding, while the ALA provided technical know-how and both began campaigning for government approval.\n\nWhile our military is reluctant of accepting donated books, there is a real need for entertainment for our soldiers in the field and Army high command decided to give its approval to the project.
Let's hope our soldiers enjoy it.
Cancellation of the Victory Book Campaign
While the Victory Book Campaign has paved the way for institutions like the Council on Books in Wartime and the War Book Panel, the Campaign itself is beginning to draw criticism from the Army. Unfortunately, the Campaign was not well suited for combat units, as soldiers found the bulky hardcovers unsuitable for use in the field.\n\nMany of the books donated were deemed unfitting by the revision committees. Of the over 10 million books gathered last year, VBC staffers have discarded over half of them. While the goal of the VBC is still popular, the Army has ordered the VBC to close and has begun plans with the CBW to create a new programme to entertain our soldiers.
Something Ends, Something Begins.

Creation of a Sniper Program?
With the harsh lessons in urban warfare we have been forced to learn, we've come to realise that our army is woefully unprepared to face a new danger of the battlefield: Enemy Snipers. While Snipers proved their usefulness during the Weltkrieg, the Army high command had never seen any reason to expand upon it as it was seen as a situational solution for the battlefields of Europe.\n\nHowever, fighting in the American mountains, cities and forests has proved that not only they were wrong, but also costed us dearly, as we lack the means to counter-act enemy sniper operations, let alone send off snipers of our own to eliminate High Value Targets. As such, a proposal has reached High Command to kickstart one similar to the Sniper training that Canada put their snipers through in the Weltkrieg.
The Proposal Passes.
The Proposal is Shut Down.

While the first test group was drawn from volunteers from all the US Army, there has been a significant performance difference between the Marine and Ranger volunteers compared to the regular army volunteers.\n\nAs such, both branches are contesting for the funding of the War Department to continue the Sniper Program, and we can only pick one. Which branch shall we support?

Creation of the Office for Emergency Management
With the outbreak of the civil war, the President has dispatched the creation via executive order of an office that functioned to assist the President in clearing information on immediate defence measures. With it, the Office for Emergency Management has been born to maintain liaison with national defence agencies and to coordinate the national defence programme, as well as keep both the Army and Navy in direct contact with the President.\n\nHowever, the mess of agencies, offices and commissions we have generated in the last few decades continues to grow, and many agree that our government should start looking into ways of reducing the amount of offices and increase the efficiency of existing ones.
For now, this will do.
Creation of the United States Office of War Information
Due to a lack of a centralised government agency to work as a distributor of wartime information, civilian newspapers present news as they discover and interpret it, with different outlets overlapping their stories with slight variations and the public hardly knowing what is true and what is propaganda.\n\nAs such, and with permission of both the War Department and the President, the Office of War Information has been created to work as a connection between the battlefront and civilian communities. While many independent news outlets have expressed their concerns over a centralised agency becoming the sole distributor of wartime information, most experts agree that this is a necessary move.
They have nothing to fear, we shall spread only the truth!
Changing the USAAC Roundel?
With the outbreak of the American Civil War, the issue has been brought up that our air planes share the same air force patch as our enemies.\n\nWhile radio communication has allowed us so far to distinguish between friend and foe, reports of friendly fire and unexpected enemy attacks abound, and the Air Force officers have come with a proposal to change our roundel from the star symbol within a blue circle with a red dot in the middle to a different roundel so our anti air units may better differentiate our planes from the enemy's. What should we do?
Let the enemy change it! This roundel is ours.

The War Department Relocates to the Main Navy and Munitions Buildings
With the Department of State leaving almost no room for the War Department to grow near the White House, the Secretary of War has authorised the War Department to move to a different location. It is to be to an ammunition warehouse provided by the navy. However, the warehouse is still too small the hold the ever growing War Department, with a new wing having been ordered to be constructed to accommodate newly employed staff.\n\nWe estimate that we will need a larger structure to consolidate the 24.000 workers in offices scattered among 17 separate sites, as well as a possible additional 10.000 or more new workers that we are planning to include soon as our nation falls into conflict.

McNair's Report on the State of the Army
Under the High Command's orders, General McNair has compiled a report of all the major flaws our army possesses at the moment that we will need to solve if we wish to prevail against our enemies in the civil war. The major summary sent to the War Department lists the following issues:\n\n1. Obviously deficient training of small units and in minor tactics.\n2. Faulty employment of the infantry division and of its combat teams.\n3. Failure fully to appreciate the purpose of motor vehicles and exploit their capabilities.\n4. Inadequate reconnaissance and lack of contact between adjacent units.\n5. Inadequate support of infantry by division artillery.\n6. Faulty signal communications.\n7. Too passive employment of antitank guns.\n8. Improper employment of horse cavalry.\n9. Neglect of ammunition supply and evacuation of wounded.\n10. Unreal situations due to faulty umpiring.\n\nIn the same manner, other issues have been brought up by other officers in which they include shortages of qualified staff officers and commanders to fill all the staff roles and deficiencies in individual training that would delay the effectiveness of unit training.
We have to reform if we wish to prevail.

Pentagon is Finished
With the final wing finally finished, the War Department has finally found its own home and the building now sports a reinforced concrete structure, using 680,000 tons of sand dredged from the Potomac River and Indiana limestone for the building's façade.\n\nIt occupies 28.7 acres (116,000 m2), and includes an additional 5.1 acres (21,000 m2) as a central courtyard, with the hallways being so large that messengers are being issued with roller skates and bikes to speed up messaging between offices.

Trial of the Federalist Generals
With the civil war now over, and our enemies at our mercy, the Army has finally begun the trials against the Federalist generals. While some generals have fled into exile, the generals who were caught are now waiting for the verdict of the military tribunal. However, despite what the public believes, it's not as easy to carry out the trials as it was originally anticipated. Most trialled generals don't have any particular record of unnecessary violence, and even those that do can still claim they were following orders. The Second Session of the 74th Congress
The coming of January marks the return of the 74th Congress from its annual recess. As Senators and Representatives return to Washington from their home states, the narrow Democratic majority in both houses prepares the President's administrative agenda, in what will be Al Smith's final year in office.\n\nLast year, the administration racked up several important legislative accomplishments, such as the Costigan-Wagner Anti-Lynching Act and the National Labor Arbitration and Enforcement Act. One initiative that eluded passage, however, was the newest version of the Social Security bill. Denounced by the left as insufficient in the face of systemic depression and the right as government overreach, we had immense difficulty cobbling together a majority for the bill last year, particularly with the Democratic losses of the 1934 midterms.\n\nThe President has made his desire to see through the passage of the Social Security bill in the new session abundantly clear. The creation of an old-age benefits system would represent one last substantial victory for the administration and would undercut the rhetoric of Smith's political opponents both within and outside of the Democratic Party. Both the Farmer-Labor Party and Huey Long have emphasised the need for a system of old-age pensions, so the passage of the act would go a long way towards disarming one of their key policy appeals.

Social Security Dies in Committee
The recent crash on the New York Stock exchange has sent Washington into a panic. With Wall Street continuing to tumble, fears of a return to the darkest days of 1928 have aroused a deep sense of dread among lawmakers and allies of the administration. With conditions in Europe appearing far more severe than during the recession of 1931, and trade barriers flying up once more, it appears as if the period of recovery that has characterised Smith's second term has come to a sudden halt.\n\nAs lawmakers scramble to put together a response, the first major victim of the crash appears to be what was once meant to be the crowning jewel of the President's final year in office: the Social Security bill. As Congress' priorities have rapidly shifted elsewhere, the Senate has voted to table the bill, even as it appeared to be on the verge of passage in the House just a week ago, essentially killing it for the foreseeable future. With the main piece of the President's legislative agenda dead on arrival, the path forward for the administration seems unclear and tumultuous.

The Blame Game
The recent panic in Congress has greatly exacerbated the woes the Administration has faced in its second term. Ever since Smith's election in 1928, the Democratic Party has consistently declined in popularity, seeing its congressional majorities whittled down to threadbare margins. The flurry of stabilising legislation that stopped the bleeding in 1929 has slowed to a crawl, so the President has little to show for his second term. Worse still, the Democratic Party is on the verge of tearing itself apart. Huey Long has intensified attacks on President Smith, transparently plotting to find an angle with which to run for President later this year.\n\nWith Black Monday spreading across the Atlantic, Congress appears paralysed. Social Security is dead, and the major parties struggle to find consensus, as Farmer-Labor and the Longists reap the rewards of seven years of generally conservative government. The Hearst papers have continued their long running feud with the President as well, a rivalry active since Smith attacked Hearst in 1919. Hearst comes just short of openly calling for Douglas MacArthur to march on Washington and establish a dictatorship. Such words are finding receptive ears among men imminently about to lose their fortunes, as leading firms are seemingly destined for bankruptcy in the next few months, if not weeks.\n\nWith the progress of the past seven years seemingly falling apart around him, President Smith has met with his cabinet to discuss the steps that must be taken to save the nation's economy once more. Cordell Hull, the Secretary of State, called for the President to further lower trade barriers, while Vice President Joe T. Robinson proposed to push forward with emergency legislative action. Hull, as well as Secretary of Commerce Herbert Hoover, among the more popular members of the administration, and finally Huey Long, an oft-mentioned name with regards to the Democratic nomination, seconded Robinson's proposal, which was then accepted by the President. With the aid of his Vice President, an experienced wheeler-and-dealer with enduring connections in the Senate, President Smith has called a special session of Congress to pass emergency relief legislation.

Rubber Workers on Strike
As the economic situation has continued to deteriorate, labor militancy has skyrocketed across the United States. On the morning of the 14th, the city of Akron, Ohio came to a virtual standstill after approximately 10,000 workers and sympathetic citizens went on strike in the country's largest rubber plant: the Goodwin Tire Factory. This sudden action was in response to company plans to lay off hundreds of workers and slash the wages of the remainder by upwards of 50% in order to adjust for losses inflicted by Black Monday.\n\nBefore the city's citizens or the strikers were prepared, the local deputies and an associated organisation of thugs and paramilitaries, the so-called 'Law and Order League', fell on the lot. While hand-to-hand combat raged for the first half hour, the frustrated deputies began to draw their pistols, and fired into the crowd at point-blank range. Enraged, sympathetic citizens and unionists similarly armed themselves, and before either side knew it, a full-blown battle for the city had broken out.\n\nThough the scuffle was brief, it quickly sent shockwaves through the community. The people of Akron, some of whom were horrified at how quickly the situation had spiralled out of control, agreed with the local unionists to stand down, in exchange for blanket pardons for all those whom were involved. Nevertheless, unions nationwide, even those affiliated with the comparatively moderate AFL, have taken this outbreak of violence as a warning. Across the country, particularly in the steel belt, paramilitary activity led by local Red Guards and other socialist-led organisations has spiked as unions play host to military-style training. Calls among anti-socialist hardliners for decisive action to disarm and even dismantle unions have increased, but thus far have gone unheeded by either federal or state authorities.

West Virginia Abolishes Term Limits
Since John Reed shocked the nation by winning the state in the election of 1928, West Virginia has been a stronghold of the Socialist Party. Though the party's hold on the state was tenuous (with them narrowly losing the Senate seat up in 1930), through the 1930s the party has gradually tightened its grasp over the red bastion. It has enacted pro-union policies, partnered with the IWW mining union to build up a reliable pro-SPA patronage system, and brought certain industries and utilities into state ownership. Since Socialist J.H. Snider was elected Governor in 1928, the SPA has gradually increased its share of both state houses, gaining a majority in the House of Delegates in 1930 and the Senate in 1932.\n\n1932 also marked a changing of the guard. Governor Snider, a moderate ally of Norman Thomas' faction of the party, was term-limited, and replaced as governor by radical Miles Stone, who hews closer to the line of party leadership. Under Stone, the party has further solidified its grip over the state, bringing itself into alignment with the IWW and winning a two-thirds majority in both houses of the state legislature in 1934. This enabled the Socialist Party to amend the state constitution, overriding the few remaining legal checks available to anti-socialist forces in the state.\n\nThe most recent amendment affects Governor Stone most directly. Under West Virginia's constitution, governors are limited to a single consecutive term. With a special session of the state legislature, however, that section has been rewritten to allow Governor Stone to run for re-election. The amendment represents a clear step towards further SPA dominance over the state, a process further exemplified by the decision of Congressman Robert L. Hogg, the last remaining non-Socialist in the state's house delegation, not to run for re-election. With Robert L. Hogg's imminent departure, and Senator Mathew M. Neely's re-election looking ever more unlikely, it appears as if the Socialists will soon have uncontested control over the state's congressional delegation.

The Great St. Patrick's Day Flood
When it rains, it pours - unfortunately for the United States, this is to be taken both metaphorically and literally. The winter of 1935-36 has seen extremely heavy snowfall, even by the standards of the Northeast. Widespread melting has already clogged infrastructure and caused some limited flooding, although to date it was nothing that the locals couldn't handle.\n\nOver the past week, however, this situation has become catastrophic; unusually heavy rainstorms, starting on March 9th and continuing unabated, have triggered flooding from Maine to Maryland, and even sections of northern Virginia. Funding for Mt. Rushmore
For the third time since 1927, a grant request has been put forward in Congress to allocate federal funding to the long-stalled 'Shrine of Democracy' project: a plan to carve four collossal statues into the face of Mount Rushmore in South Dakota. The brainchild of local historian Doane Robinson and famed sculptor Gutzon Borglum - the creator of Georgia's colossal 'Shrine to the Confederacy' - Robinson originally intended for the carvings to depict towering figures of the American West such as Lewis & Clark, Red Cloud, Sacagaewa, John C. Fremont, and Crazy Horse, but Borglum instead favoured commemorating four of America's most influential Presidents, settling on George Washington, Thomas Jefferson, Theodore Roosevelt, and Abraham Lincoln.\n\nThe two men and their supporters argue that the project will not only help the local economy, but also have a psychological impact on our flailing nation, revitalizing faith in the future. In addition to this, the Department of the Interior has received a letter from Lakota chief Henry Standing Bear, offering to turn over 900 acres of his own land in order to get a carving of Crazy Horse added to the project.\n\nAs such, we are faced with three possibilities: to finance the work at Mount Rushmore, to take up Henry Standing Bear's deal and include Crazy Horse alongside the Presidents, or to simply reject the proposal and allocate the funds elsewhere.

The Tupelo-Gainesville Tornado Outbreak
The southeastern United States is no stranger to natural disasters. The Great Mississippi flood struck at the first height of the Great Depression, leaving hundreds of thousands homeless and partially resulting in the election of Huey Long as Governor of Louisiana. In a year featuring numerous severe weather events, the south has yet again found itself as a central victim.\n\nAcross the southeast an outbreak of 14 different tornadoes has wreaked havoc between Arkansas and South Carolina. The towns of Tupelo, Mississippi, and Gainesville, Georgia, have been the most severely affected locations: in total, over 200 people died in each town due to powerful tornadoes.\n\nIn Tupelo, a tornado swept through residential areas, tearing apart buildings and killing and injuring countless families. Gainesville meanwhile saw its tornado hit the Cooper Pants Factory, collapsing the building and causing a fire which killed as many as 125 workers trapped on the top floor.\n\nAll told, over 400 people have died in the outbreak (mainly concentrated in Tupelo and Gainesville), and the tornadoes have also caused over 10 million dollars in property damage. In the aftermath of the disaster, President Smith has announced his intention to visit the affected area, though it is unlikely that his presence will be warmly received. In any case, federal aid will be arriving shortly in the affected areas, which will hopefully begin the process of healing for these communities.

Fred Weiss, a disgruntled associate, opened fire at point-blank range as Long and his entourage exited the building down a corridor, but incredibly, the gun jammed. As a result Long's hand-picked bodyguards emptied their firearms into Weiss. He was struck more than 60 times, even after falling to the floor.\n\nAlmost immediately, conspiracy theories have spread like wildfire across the United States. Long himself has intentionally inflated the idea that his enemies among the dominant two-party system had arranged the attempt. As political violence becomes normalized, a worrying trend in American politics since Black Monday: a failure of faith in the fundamental soundness of civic institutions. Despite tough times in the past, a constant has always been a core belief that these civic institutions, such as the media, Congress, Courts, and others, genuinely worked for the people, albeit flawed. No longer. It seems now that people only want to believe in what they want to hear, making it impossible for the government to re-establish any degree of credibility among the population at large, creating a vicious feedback cycle of constant radicalization, distrust, and clashing narratives. Political hatred seems well on its way to be the norm, rather than the exception.

The Farm Crisis
Since the end of the European War, US agriculture has been in a state of perpetual economic crisis. During the war, there was an agricultural boom, as the global market tightened and global demand for US agricultural products boomed. The end of the war put a stop to this however, both because European agriculture began to once again meet domestic demands, as well as due to the new tariff walls erected by Mitteleuropa, which essentially closed off the German economic bloc to US agriculture. This crisis of overproduction severely reduced the price of US agricultural goods, cratering the profitability of farms and causing many farmers to go bankrupt.\n\nJust as recovery seemed to be near however, the Great Depression struck. Prices fell even further, and foreclosures and bank failures left many farmers penniless, wandering the American countryside. The institution of new tariffs under President Lowden and the subsequent reluctance to lower them again by President Smith further exacerbated the United States' isolation from global trade, cratering prices further. As if this was not bad enough, in recent years the Dust Bowl has seen many remaining farmers lose their livelihoods due to crop failure.\n\nThese cascading catastrophes have resulted in a growing radicalisation in rural America. Both Farmer-Labor and Huey Long's movement have sought to exploit the growing anger and fury coming from farmers and rural communities towards the establishment and economic elites. As banks and Wall Street speculators are blamed for the state of the Farm Crisis, radical rhetoric gains more and more traction, threatening to engulf the countryside. The Republican National Convention
It has long been the case that the Republicans hold their nominating convention first, and the Democrats second. With one exception in 1888, this order has held since the days of Lincoln, disregarding the fleeting presence of major third parties such as the People's Party, and now Farmer-Labor. Optimism abounds at this year's Republican National Convention, as the people generally appear tired of the Democrats, and change seems to be in the air.\n\nMuch as things change however, much they stay the same. Primary elections have been a feature of major party presidential politics since the days of Theodore Roosevelt. Though generally non-binding, they provide an astute indication of the mood of the public. This year, progressive Republican and Idaho Senator William Borah, among the last of the Roosevelt breed of Republican, has almost completely swept the GOP primaries. With the winds behind his back, Borah's advocacy of a return to Roosevelt-style progressivism, and his left-criticism of the Smith Administration have made him few friends among the conservative wing of the party.\n\nThe Conservatives however realise the precariousness of their position. Borah has momentum, and the country is in a generally progressive mood after the disappointments of the Smith years. Conservatives, most prominently Michigan's Arthur Vandenberg, are therefore reluctant to throw their hat in the ring in their own right.\n\nAs such the Conservative wing of the party has rallied behind Moderate Kansas Governor Alf Landon. A pragmatic yet liberal moderate with a strong electoral record, Landon presents a broadly acceptable alternative that is nonetheless in-tune with the mood of the country. With the backing of the establishment, Landon faces down Borah's insurgency on the floor of the convention...
The insurgency wins out: Borah gets the nomination!

The Lion of Idaho Roars
Though considerable press attention has been on the latest scandals affecting the floundering Democrats and the latest bout of violence triggered by the Longists and Leftists, the Republican Party has been hard at work trying to build a workable electoral coalition for November.\n\nBalancing their conservative, liberal, and progressive wings, the selection of a progressive ticket has not stopped them from attempting to appeal to a disparate selection of voters across the country. Republican campaigners have been knocking on doors, soliciting funds from businesses large and small, blasting the Smith administration for its incompetence, blasting Long for corruption, and stoking fears of a socialist revolution.\n\nThis is hardly Borah's first campaign of course - an experienced political operator, Borah has made himself a major powerbroker in Republican elections across the 1920s despite his hatred of both intrigue and tobacco (making him a poor fit for the literal smoke-filled back rooms). An energetic campaigner and seeking to recast the Republican party as a progressive one, he has worked to expand his reach from beyond the Great Plains - shoring up GOP strongholds in the North and West.\n\nStill, with competition intense and violence escalating, one has to wonder if this will be enough. The establishment may have locked ranks behind him on a national scale, however many local political machines have locked out aligned candidates on the down ballot. His attempts at winning over Farmer-Labor and Union Party voters, and his party's attempts to woo disaffected Democrats have only had limited success. It is clear that this will be a long and hard fought campaign.

A Convention Brawl
It started as a simple dispute over procedure. Two different state delegations from Mississippi demanded to be seated: one pro-Long and one anti-Long. The ruling by the convention's credentials committee in favour of the anti-Long delegation started a wave of boos and jeers from Long's supporters. Successive challenges to other pro-Long delegations intensified the situation. Long demanded a chance to speak, hoping to sway the convention as Bryan had in 1896, but was denied.\n\nThe mood among the Long crowd went from bad to worse. The final straw was an attempt to revoke the credentials of the Louisiana delegation, in favour of an anti-Long alternative slate. At this, the Long crowd rose. Long's brother, Earl, swore at Vice President Robinson, before being caught up in a brief fist-fight with him, a brawl that left the younger man worse off before he was restrained by other attendees. The incident ultimately proved the last straw for Long's supporters, who proceeded to leave the convention en masse.\n\nAfter a short round of voting, the convention, now much friendlier to the administration, rallied behind Robinson, after Hoover withdrew his name from consideration. After Robinson was nominated for the presidency, Hoover was offered the second spot on the ticket, but again declined, obviously seeing it as a futile effort, and looking towards a run in 1940. An alternative was found in Indiana Governor Paul V. McNutt, a photogenic northerner with strong electoral credentials. The new Democratic ticket now seems to stare towards electoral oblivion, as Long openly prepares his forces for a parallel convention.
What madness!

The Union Party Convention
For days, Huey Long has stoked anticipation of a third-party run for President. Few expected his rejection by the Democrats to end his presidential ambitions, and now Long has taken the stage to confirm just that. Denouncing the Democratic Party as irrevocably corrupt, he and his allies have founded the Union Party, an alliance of convenience between populists such as Charles Couglin, Francis Townsend, and William Lemke, more reactionary Democratic politicians such as Eugene Talmadge and Theodore Bilbo, as well as a host of fringe figures such as Gerald K. Smith. Drifting adjacent to the Union Party orbit are several leading corporate executives such as Henry Ford, John Henry Kirby, Alfred P. Sloan, and Robert E. Wood.\n\nAlong with the new party, Long has announced that Montana Senator Burton K. Wheeler, his longtime friend and partner in the Senate, will be joining him as his Vice Presidential nominee. Wheeler is a progressive who was elected to a Senate seat in 1922, becoming a well known populist legislator with ties across the political spectrum. As a Senator, Wheeler is popular due to his leadership in several anti-corruption inquiries, and his willingness to challenge the establishment and even the White House. In addition to having many allies among the progressive movement and organised labour, Wheeler is also known for his isolationist and nativist views - voting for legislation clamping down on immigration and also for diplomatic non-intervention.\n\nLong's choice of Wheeler has helped to give the Union Party a more cohesive identity as a Western populist party, but some have criticized it as being too narrow in scope to actually win in November. Many conservative Democrats who expressed some interest in the party have now begun to distance themselves, threatening the inroads the Union Party has made in the south. Still, a shared vision can do wonders for a party's image, especially as the other major parties struggle with their own internal divisions.

$united_states_leadup_events.35.d.body$\n\nWhere many northern black voters were once seriously considering the Long ticket for President, it is now clear that Long has ruptured his relationship with them beyond repair. Though Farmer-Labor offers a civil rights plank, more black voters are inclined to return to the GOP, where nominee Alf Landon has a strong record on civil rights. As for Long...
In 1912, African-American voters were, after decades of failure on civil rights issues, disillusioned with the Republican Party. When Democratic candidate Woodrow Wilson appeared receptive to the concerns of African-Americans, in spite of his southern background, many African-Americans flocked to his campaign. When in office however, Wilson proceeded to segregate the federal government, deny appointments to African-Americans, and increase the severity of segregation in the armed forces, setting back progress on civil rights by decades.\n\nThe African-American community is familiar with such betrayals and disappointments. The Republican Party has taken a largely passive stance on civil rights issues, while the Democratic Party, still with a powerful southern interest, has provided little more hope for change. Perhaps the brightest hope in recent years however has been the Presidency of Al Smith. Smith, traditionally seen as a defender of civil rights, again energised black support for the Democrats. Instead of reneging on his promises like Wilson however, Smith has overseen some notable successes in civil rights policy, most notably the passage of the Costigan-Wagner Anti-Lynching Act in 1935.\n\nWith the entry of Huey Long onto the national scene, African-American voters in the north have looked on the Louisiana upstart with reserved optimism. Long is known for having avoided racial vitriol and demagoguery in his statewide campaigns in Louisiana, and some of his statements surrounding the administration of social security as well as his national approach to racial issues gave rise to a hope that he would be a different kind of southerner. That optimism was shattered however by Long's selection of Eugene Talmadge as his running mate. Talmadge, one of the most infamous race-baiting Governors in the south, has marked a change in direction for the Long campaign. Talmadge frequently espouses racist rhetoric on the campaign trail, seeing no pushback from Long on the matter, who is now silent regarding the concerns of his black constituents.
For them, his story is done.
The Midwest Swelters
As the Heat Wave of 1936 tears through the country, one of the worst-hit sections of the country has seen more suffering than most. As opposed to the lower South, whose inhabitants are generally acclimated to extreme heat, midwestern Americans have almost no frame of reference for such intense waves.\n\nOn July 9th and 10th, a season that has already seen record-breaking heat saw records broken once again: on average, a triangle of states from New York to the Dakotas to Tennessee faced temperatures upwards of 105-115 degrees Fahrenheit, as well as excruciatingly high humidity. Some towns had quite literally never seen temperatures over 95 degrees, not to mention over 115, leaving citizens completely unprepared. In the last week alone, approximately 5,000 American citizens have been killed by the heat directly or through conditions aggravated by the heat.\n\nWhile it seems the worst is over for now, the wave will hardly go away quickly, and it seems to be just another sign that times are not good for the United States of America. Even worse, meteorologists are predicting an unusually cold winter as well!
Even the weather has turned against us.
Gone With The Wind
First released on July 30th, Gone with the Wind has soared to the top of the national bestseller list. A fictionalized account of the experiences of a character named Scarlett O'Hara, the novel follows her life from the ages of sixteen to twenty-eight. Set in Clayton County and Atlanta, Georgia, the novel covers O'Hara's life as the Civil War engulfs the South, O'Hara struggles to maintain her lifestyle as the daughter of a wealthy plantation owner, juggle the social expectations of both her class and gender, and balance it all with her own personal happiness and fulfillment.\n\nFilled with family drama, salacious controversies, and genuine emotion, the book has become an instant hit. It must be admitted, however, as many progressives, socialists, and liberals, reviewers and not, have pointed out - both North and South - the tale is filled with default assumptions of the loyalty of both the enslaved and freed peoples, endorsement of white supremacy, and the idea that women are content in a subordinate role to men. Either way, it cannot be denied that the book already, after a single month, has a strong hold on American popular memory of the Civil War and American literary history broadly.

Olson Gains on Long in the Plains
When Floyd Olson ran for President in 1932, many had doubts over whether or not the candidate would be able to win any states beyond his home state of Minnesota. He soon proved them wrong - polling extremely well in Wisconsin, North Dakota, South Dakota, Iowa, Washington, and other Great Plains states and even notching several outright wins.\n\nThe Farmer-Labor party is determined to maintain that momentum. This time however, he is competing with Huey Long for disaffected, anti-establishment rural voters, making his quest much harder as the two candidates enter into direct competition. Both have attempted to shore up their populist credentials while showing their ability to work within establishment structures as Governors, and while seeking to avoid being implicated in the various scandals dogging their campaigns - whether it be their radical allies or their own histories of alleged corruption and political violence.\n\nOlson seems to be doing fairly well holding his own over Long, who had the initial advantage in peeling off voters from the Republicans and especially disillusioned fellow democrats. Making inroads among progressive Republicans in the north with the help of the Nonpartisan League and making his way into the Democratic scene, things seem to be swinging his way.\n\nThere are of course plenty of more weeks left to go however, and some within the Farmer-Labor Party have criticised Olson's strategy, arguing that the Great Plains has considerably fewer electoral votes in contention. They bemoan the relative lack of attention in the grand prize of New York, and question whether or not Olson's time is being well spent. However, Olson and his allies have defended their decisions, arguing that flipping the Great Plains would go a long way in ultimately winning the election, trusting that Farmer-Labor has sufficient votes to win the Steel Belt.

Thomas Makes a Play for New York
When Floyd Olson ran for President in 1932, many had doubts over whether or not the candidate would be able to win any states beyond his home state of Minnesota. He soon proved them wrong - polling extremely well in Wisconsin, North Dakota, South Dakota, Iowa, Washington, and other Great Plains states and even notching several outright wins.\n\nTo actually win the election however, the Farmer-Labor Party will need to capture states with much larger electoral votes rather than the sparsely populated Great Plains. Consequently, Norman Thomas and the Farmer-Labor Party has been putting much more attention in the Midwest and East, solidifying their hold on areas of growing SPA strength in the Steel Belt.\n\nThis has surprisingly put the extremely valuable state of New York, the largest state in the Union, into play. Norman Thomas has a long history of campaigning in New York, both for himself and his allies, and this has worked to his advantage in 1936. The incumbent New York Republican Party has been thrown into panic about the prospect of losing the state and has been scrambling to consolidate the establishment vote there. A win in New York would go a long way, especially if the Farmer-Labor Party can secure their expected wins in the Midwest, however they will need to survive the GOP counter-attack first.\n\nThomas has however effectively sacrificed the Great Plains in this quest, and many within the party have complained that Farmer-Labor is effectively fighting a rear-guard action there against the Longist surge. They note that even if Thomas could flip New York, the only way Farmer-Labor will be able to get past the electoral threshold to win is if they secure several Great Plains states.
A bold gambit for sure.
The Great Heat Wave Is Over
Since June, high temperatures have borne down on people across the United States. After a historic cold season in the winter earlier into the year, Americans have been faced with historic temperature spikes. The first regions affected were the northeast and south. The brunt of the impact however was borne by the midwest, which sweltered at temperatures often higher than 100 degrees fahrenheit. Without any means to cool themselves, thousands died throughout the summer, which peaked in intensity in mid-July.\n\nThe scorching heat however was not the only thing ailing the plains. A resulting drought has ruined harvests already impacted by the Dust Bowl and the depression, pressing farmers in the southern plains even harder than they had previously imagined possible. Without crops to sell, even more farmers have been faced with the prospect of bankruptcy.\n\nThough the height of the heat peaked in July, August still sweltered for several states, including Texas and Louisiana. Only now in September has the heat wave truly started to subside. All told, over 5000 deaths have been reported nationwide, as well as the loss of livelihoods for many struggling farmers. With the depression raging on, and the financial situations of a great number of people likely to deteriorate further, such a destructive weather event could not have come at a worse time.
At least it's over...
Shots Fired At Robinson
Shocking news has come in from Indiana today: Vice President Joe T. Robinson, the Democratic nominee for president, was shot at while making a speech on the campaign trail with his running mate, Indiana's own Governor Paul V. McNutt. Though Robinson was not injured, a bullet struck Lieutenant Governor M. Clifford Townsend, the Democratic nominee for the governorship, sending him to the hospital, where he is in a critical but stable condition.\n\nThe assailant, local man Daniel Wares, was shot on the spot by Secret Service agents. Though Wares was seemingly a supporter of Huey Long, he is not believed to have had organisational links to any radical or extremist political groups, having seemingly been rejected from joining a local Minutemen chapter. The investigation into the matter has come to the conclusion that Wares was a lone actor with eclectic political views, motivated to shoot the Vice President due to a general dissatisfaction with the Smith Administration.\n\nAll of Robinson's fellow candidates for the presidency have issued statements denouncing the attack, and expressing relief at the vice president's escape from harm. This includes Long himself, who not long ago clashed violently with Robinson for the Democratic nomination. Nevertheless, the radicalising effect of the rhetoric of figures like Long is clearly to some degree at fault for the growing militarisation of American political life.
