The Young Bullmoose
The Vice President rarely receives much attention on the campaign trail, but Quentin Roosevelt might be an exception. The youngest son of President Theodore Roosevelt, Quentin grew up in the White House where he was a notorious troublemaker. He soon grew into an intelligent, thoughtful young man, attending Harvard University and becoming a noted writer. He also married prominent socialite Flora Payne Whitney, a descendant of Cornelius Vanderbilt. Trained in the ROTC in 1916, Quentin largely disliked the experience but even after graduation spent some time in the military and helped them develop a new military air wing.\n\nQuentin inherits his father's political legacy. Theodore Roosevelt Sr. was a prominent liberal Republican at the turn of the century, famous for embracing progressive movement policies at home and adopting an interventionist foreign policy abroad. Closing Arguments
When elections come to a close, they end as an orchestral crescendo. Every candidate seeks to make their core message as widely known as possible, to capture every last undecided voter, to consolidate in the state where they are expected to do well and make a final push in the states which are still up for grabs.\n\nThis year of course is different only in scale. Four viable candidates campaign for the presidency, each with interweaving regional and political bases. The chaos of the four-horse race has allowed voters to cast their ballots without much regard for spoilage or strategic voting. As such, both the Democrats and Republicans have been forced to fight tooth and nail to keep their voters in line.\n\nAs the campaign nears its conclusion, the Republicans have put their young, bright face, Quentin Roosevelt, front and centre. A nationwide tour has seen the GOP recover some of its slippage in the polls, as Roosevelt's charisma and boyish charms make up for any shortcomings at the top of the ticket.\n\nIn recent months meanwhile, the Farmer-Labor campaign has increasingly been staffed by Socialist Party cadres, who have pushed the party's messaging in a more radical direction in spite of the wishes of the convention. Similarly, Huey Long's campaign has also become more and more militant, as the Minutemen briefly lay down their pistols and rifles to go pamphleteering for the Kingfish.\n\nWhere the other three parties are rising, the Democrats are stalling and falling. Though Vice President Robinson is an impassioned speaker, eight years of unpopular Democratic rule has made that party's brand poison, especially for a man so closely tied to Al Smith.\n\nClausewitz says that war is politics by other means. On the campaign trail, the opposite might be said to be true: as in war, each campaign seeks a decisive blow, a through-line, a winning message. As things stand, no breakthrough seems likely in the closing days of the campaign. We await the people's decision with bated breath.
Nothing left to do but wait.
Maritime Workers on Strike
As the nationwide strike wave precipitated by worsening economic conditions continues to spread, militant labour organisations have been further emboldened to strike in key industries. The turn from October to November has seen a substantial up flare in industrial struggle in the maritime industry on both coasts.\n\nIn the west, CIO heavyweight Harry Bridges has sought to maintain the gains and replicate the success of the massive 1934 West Coast Longshoremen Strike, which culminated in a general strike in San Francisco. Bridges has united his International Longshoremen's Association with Harry Lundeberg's Sailors' Union of the Pacific, under the banner of the Maritime Federation of the Pacific, which has now brought all shipping on the West Coast to a halt, with both longshoremen and sailors refusing to work.\n\nOn the gulf coast, parallel developments have led to the emergence of the Maritime Federation of the Gulf Coast, a union inspired by Bridges and Lundeberg's organisation. Rejecting the AFL's International Seamen's Union, the SPA-influenced unionists have initiated a wildcat strike. The 1936 Election
Throughout the year, the American people have been waiting for the election with bated breath. Some have been eager to finally be able to express their full dissatisfaction with the current state of the country, to tear down the current administration and bring about a new dawn by electing their preferred candidate of change. Others have fearfully awaited the likely consequences of a contested and violent election, likely to be the peak of growing radical political activity, which has dominated the headlines this year.\n\nAmericans this year have come to the polls in droves. Turnout has increased compared to 1932 by over 7 percent, driven by increased participation of women and working class voters. Incidents of violence at polling stations, both towards political opponents and poll workers, have been reported in numerous locations, particularly in socialist-dominated northern municipalities (where the Red Guards and Minutemen compete with ferocity), however it has not been as overwhelming an issue as we might have feared. Accusations of Fraud
The indecisive election results have left no parties satisfied. With many devoted partisans (particularly from the radical parties) fuming at their candidate's failure to win decisively, allegations of foul play and systemic rigging of election results have entered the public discourse. Across the nation, claims that local or state or even federal authorities have manipulated the results of the election have grown louder and louder, yet another symptom of collapsing faith in America's institutions.\n\nThe Socialist Party has used reports from their poll watchers of numerous instances of attempted discarding of Socialist and Farmer-Labor ballots to claim a systemic nationwide undercount of Farmer-Labor votes. They have also denounced the suppression of the African-American vote in the south, a fact of life since the end of Reconstruction, and claimed that, had southern blacks been able to vote, they would have delivered several states to the Farmer-Labor column.\n\nHuey Long meanwhile has thrown around numerous claims regarding vote manipulation. Claiming Republican and Socialist municipal politicians cost him hundreds of thousands of city votes, Long has sued numerous states for recounts of their ballots. Such claims seem rather hypocritical however, when accounting for the infamous practices of his own machine, as well as the Democratic machines allied with him, such as the Pendergast Machine in Kansas City.\n\nThough lawsuits surrounding most claims of fraud are unlikely to hold up in court, the very fact that such claims are so commonplace is a dire sign for the legitimacy of American elections. If millions of voters will not accept their candidate's defeat, how can we have a stable and civil political culture?
November is never going to end, is it...
Fear and Loathing in New York
As the aftermath of the election continues to unfold, the myriad disputes and contestations surrounding the results have grown in intensity and stakes. What has emerged as by far the most significant electoral dispute has been that surrounding the election for the governorship of New York. In a tight three-way race, the Democrats, Republicans, and Farmer-Labor have all claimed victory, demanding recounts of various batches of votes they suspect to be fraudulent.\n\nIncumbent Governor Quentin Roosevelt was, at the beginning of the year, widely expected to win re-election handedly. His selection as the GOP's nominee for Vice President however ended his bid for re-election, resulting in an open race for the Republican nomination and the governorship. The new Republican nominee, famed urban planner Robert Moses, holds more conservative positions than Roosevelt. His comparative conservatism allowed the Democratic nominee, former Governor Herbert Lehman, to make a play for the non-socialist progressive vote.\n\nThe race was rounded out by the Farmer-Labor candidate, SPA official Benjamin Gitlow. Though the New York Farmer-Labor Party includes many non-socialist progressives, its largest component by far is the New York Socialist Party. Gitlow, a protege and close ally of John Reed, has, in spite of his radicalism compared to figures such as the Farmer-Labor mayor of New York City, Fiorello La Guardia, cornered the labour vote, and effectively mounted a competitive bid for the governorship.\n\nThough few could predict how the close race would turn out, fewer still would have expected a three-way tie. All three parties have claimed victory, and numerous recounts in key counties have been ordered. As things stand, our advisors expect Lehman to pull ahead based on the numbers available to us, however it appears likely that the Socialists will refuse to concede no matter what any court orders.
Concerning.
The Conservative Coalition
If anything can be gleaned from the election results in November, it is that the conservative politics of the Smith Administration have been utterly repudiated by the American voting public. All three candidates who are eligible to be elected in the contingent election campaigned on a platform of change, be it moderate (in the case of the GOP), progressive (in the case of Farmer-Labor), or populist (in the case of Long). Robinson, the candidate most representative of continuity, was soundly crushed both in the popular vote and the electoral college.\n\nNevertheless, conservatives in Congress have not taken this setback lying down. The Electoral College Meets
Today, the various presidential electors from all 48 states have met to cast their ballots for the presidency. In the United States, votes in presidential elections are technically not cast for the presidential candidates themselves, but rather for slates of electors pledged to vote on behalf of their candidates in the legally binding election. Though usually a mere formality, the electoral college has sometimes had significance beyond mere civic ritual: though electors are generally loyal party men, they, on occasion, break with their pledges to vote for alternative candidates, becoming

Vice President Robinson Dies
Since his smashing defeat in the presidential election the better part of two months ago, Vice President Joe T. Robinson has kept a relatively low profile. With little left in his career but to preside over the certification of the results of the election he disastrously lost, few have expected much of Robinson before his presumed post-vice presidential retirement, especially as the attention of the nation is focused on other, more pressing matters.\n\nNow however, Robinson has been spared the ignominy of presiding over his own defeat. Today, news has come from Washington of the vice president's passing. After complaining of chest pains two days ago, he died of heart failure, probably brought about by the stress of campaigning. The decisive loss of his home state in the election to his enemy, Huey Long, also weighed heavily on the vice president in his last days.\n\nWith Robinson's death, the duty of certifying the results of the election will pass to the president pro tempore of the Senate. Both President Smith and numerous members of both the House and Senate paid their respects to Robinson, a veteran legislator as Senator from Arkansas. Both the Republican and Farmer-Labor nominees sent their condolences, while Huey Long gave a brief acknowledgement of Robinson's death.

Workers Seize GM Plants
General Motors' planned closure of factories in Detroit have run into perhaps the worst case scenario; the spontaneous occupation of the factories by the working class itself. Walter Reuther, still sporting bandages from the so-called Battle of the Overpass from months ago, was seen shaking the hands of many an auto-worker after the UAW led the effort with a series of wildcat strikes and direct actions increasingly bordering on the revolutionary. Organising the workers into elected committees based on factory as well as overall Union affiliation (be it IWW, CIO, or in some cases sparse AFL radicals or previously unaffiliated workers), the SPA have essentially began the direct formation of dual-power structures within the nation's industrial heartland. The state government has completely crumbled in response to the workers' demands, and has immediately agreed to pay markedly increased wages using federal funds, de facto nationalizing the plants without compensation to a furious GM.\n\nA flurry of furious legal suits is nothing new for the times, especially at this point, but the scale is almost unprecedented. The government's panicked concession sent the most worrying message to business leaders across the country, too paralyzed to do anything about the disruption of normal commerce. As the CIO organises the self-defence and armament of the newly socialized factories, a dreadful question once thought unthinkable began to bubble onto the lips of worker and boss alike.

$united_states_leadup_events.59.d.body.start$\n\nThough Farmer-Labor nominee Norman Thomas is also an available candidate, the thought of putting an outright socialist in the White House has been shut down by conservatives and moderate liberals alike.\n\n$united_states_leadup_events.59.d.body.end$
After nearly two months of post-election turmoil, the 75th Congress has met in Washington for the first time. The indecisive results of the Presidential election have resulted in two highly divided chambers, now having to wrangle in order to form any sort of majority, not only to elect a Speaker, but also, since the Electoral College failed to do so, elect a President.\n\nThe Democratic caucus is placed in a unique position compared to the other parties in Congress however: Its candidate for President came fourth in November, and will thus not be a candidate in the contingent election. This leaves the Democratic representatives as de facto kingmakers, as they cannot vote for their own candidate, and must therefore support the nominee of another party.\n\nOn the one hand, most simply, they can form an establishment oriented coalition to elect the Republican nominee. The Democrats and Republicans together have a thin majority, so finding the votes for this should be fairly simple. As the Republicans have indicated a willingness to allow John Nance Garner to remain as Speaker if their candidate is elected, it should be easy to bring most Democrats on board with the idea.\n\nAlternatively, the Democrats could cobble together a coalition of Democrats, Progressive Republicans, and moderate Farmer-Laborites to elect Huey Long President. Though many Democrats disdain Long, he retains significant ties to his old party, and elevating him to the Presidency may help heal the wounds of last year's campaign.
Before a contingent election is held, a Speaker must first be elected to preside over the House. Since the Speaker will also be able to influence the voting rules of the contingent election, it is likely that whatever coalition elects a Speaker will also elect the President. Should the House fail to elect a Speaker, it is likely that it will be difficult for any faction to build a majority behind their candidate, potentially leaving the country in constitutional limbo.

Borah Elected President
After several abortive ballots, it appeared as if the House may be sent into chaos. For a time, it appeared as if the election of a Speaker might take several days, perhaps even delaying the election of a president. With pressure mounting however, a breakthrough occurred not long after voting began. A deal was struck between the Democratic and Republican contingents in the House, as well as a handful of non-socialist Farmer-Laborites.\n\nIn exchange for Republican votes for John Nance Garner for speaker, most Democrats agreed to vote for William Borah for President, contingent on the nomination of several Democrats to the cabinet. With Garner in the speakership, the contingent election went ahead without much incident: only a single round of voting was required to confirm the election of Borah, as the combined Democratic-Republican majority held more than enough state delegations to push him through on the first ballot. With that, William Borah was formally elected the 32nd President of the United States.\n\nBorah's election, widely regarded as the most likely outcome going into the new Congress, went by with little protest from the congressional centre. The Socialists walked out in protest, but broadly the election has been received positively. News of Borah's election travelled quickly, and the new president-elect has now quickly begun to assemble his two-party cabinet. The loss of two months of preparation time between the election and the inauguration has resulted in a rush in Washington, as federal officials only have two weeks to prepare for Borah to take office.\n\nNevertheless, the firm election of a president comes as a relief across the nation. With the country in economic and social crisis, we can only hope that Borah will have more luck than we have had over the past year.

Long Elected President
After several abortive ballots, it appeared as if the House may be sent into chaos. For a time, it appeared as if the election of a Speaker might take several days, perhaps even delaying the election of a president. The Popular Vote Controversy
In our constitution, there is no requirement that the winner of the most votes in the nationwide presidential election is necessarily the winner. On five prior occasions (in 1824, 1876, 1888, 1920, and 1932), the winner of the popular vote did not end up winning the presidency, either because of a divide between the Electoral College and the popular vote, or because a contingent election in the house selected a candidate other than the popular vote winner.\n\nNow, 1936 has become the sixth such occasion, and the third in a space of 17 years. The House has, for the second time in a row, selected a less popular candidate for the presidency. Though this does not have any legal bearing on the president's legitimacy, it is obviously a less than ideal situation for the legitimacy of our democratic institutions: in the wake of the contingent election, small protests popped up across the nation denouncing Congress' choice to

Nevertheless, most Republicans have, reluctantly, accepted the results.

The fact that such a platform has any mainstream appeal at all is a dire sign of the times.

Quentin Roosevelt Elected Vice President
The election of a president in the House of Representatives has broadly come as a relief in Washington. Regardless of the differences of political opinion surrounding the election, the end of the uncertainty that lasted for two months between the voting in November and the contingent election in the House has come as a great relief to the nation.\n\nThe House election however has not resolved all of the loose ends of the election. There remains the question of the vice presidency: in a contingent election, instead of being elected in the House like the president, the vice president is elected in the Senate in a separate vote. Due to the greater hurdles required to be elected to the Senate, the chamber remains dominated by the establishment parties, which, between them, still hold a supermajority.\n\nToday, that supermajority has met to elect the new Vice President. Between the top two candidates in the electoral college, the Senate has elected the Republican nominee, Quentin Roosevelt, to the vice presidency. Roosevelt, the widely popular son of the late Former President Theodore Roosevelt, had little trouble assembling a Senate majority behind him, especially when placed up against the more radical Farmer-Labor candidate.

With Roosevelt expected to take a key role in the administration, it seems likely that the new president will lean on his youth and popularity to support his administration in these troubled times.

Preparations for any incoming administration are impossible when there is no certainty that there will be any new administration at all. Midnight
For the past two weeks, Congress has been locked in an endless gridlock. No party or group has been willing or able to compromise in order to create a majority needed to elect a president or a vice president. As the country descends into rioting, mass strikes, and political violence, the election continues to be uncertified, preventing the election of either a president or a vice president.\n\nYesterday, previous Speaker John Nance Garner made one last desperate push to form a working coalition. With his own party conference unwilling to agree to commit their support to any presidential ticket however, his attempt failed just as all his previous ones had. It was now certain that, come the 20th, there would be no elected president to take office.\n\nPresident Smith has had two weeks to prepare his administration for this eventuality. His solution has been to ask his cabinet not to hand in their resignations (conventionally done upon the inauguration of a new president), and to instead stay in their current positions until a new president is elected. As a result, at 12:00 noon, January 20th, 1937, when Smith was to leave office, Cordell Hull, the incumbent Secretary of State, would become acting president, as per the Presidential Succession Act of 1886.\n\nToday that time has come. At noon, Former President Al Smith left office without a successor, leaving the office vacant for the first time in nearly 150 years. Immediately, Cordell Hull entered the Oval Office as the Acting President of the United States.

Mass Layoffs
Unless you were a farmer, 1925 was, for the most part, a fine year if you weren't a businessman. The collapse in trade with Britain which began the Great Depression did not initially lead to mass unemployment. It was only late in the year that the walloping of business trickled down to the workers, and mass layoffs began. The depression began in the boardroom, but ultimately, it could never have stayed there.\n\nThe relapse in the depression brought about by Black Monday has gone through a similar cycle. February saw the New York Stock Exchange once again plummet, but that did not have an immediate effect on production. Well accustomed to the

Businesses Collapse
When people do not have jobs, they do not have money. When they do not have money, they do not spend it. Such is the vicious cycle of recession and depression. With the spending power of consumers plummeting, businesses become less and less able to turn a profit. A weak decade during the depression means that few smaller businesses have the reserves to maintain operations while in the red, and banks are understandably reluctant to loan money while massive lines of people wait outside their doors to withdraw their savings.\n\nBusiness failure has been an endemic part of the depression. Black Monday has once again brought it about in full force. Small businesses are the worst hit, with many closing their doors or even going bankrupt. In turn, their employees have been returned to the great and growing mass of the unemployed, further fueling the vicious cycle of today's economy.\n\nAs unemployment shockingly begins to return to the nadir of 1929, the depression has further fuelled political radicalisation. Unemployed workers flock to the SPA, as well as the unemployed unions of the IWW. Small business owners seeking lower labour costs to stay afloat have militarised into far-right paramilitaries, openly battling strikers in the streets. Farmers riot and smash up banks, who, desperate to keep their finances in order, have foreclosed on widows' farmsteads for a quick buck.
It's all spiralling down.
Bottoming Out
Under Al Smith, the American economy has had its ups and downs. The narrow avoidance of a total collapse of the U.S. banking sector in 1929 facilitated a few years of modest recovery, before the Creditanstalt collapse of 1931 sent the country back into recession. As Smith won re-election, a slow and arduous climb back to relative normality followed in his second term. For a moment, it appeared as if something resembling recovery might be at hand.\n\nThe American people knew better than to believe.\n\nThe dark days of 1929 have returned. Unemployment, inching towards a low of 13 percent at the beginning of the year, has surged back to 20 percent, and is now rising at a faster rate than at any previous point in the depression. Bankruptcies and business failures have skyrocketed, foreign trade has collapsed (again), and the progress of the Smith years has turned to dust in his last days in office.\n\nIn these days, hope has become the rarest commodity of all. Anger, however, is ubiquitous. Over a decade of failure has crushed confidence in America's political establishment: right and left, radical political forces have transformed politics from an elite and gentlemanly affair into the domain of the mob and mass movements. Paramilitaries roam the streets of major American cities, clashing over partisan allegiances. Decency dies an anonymous death.\n\nGeneral MacArthur has assured the president that the army is well equipped to handle any paramilitary insurrection. Let us hope that this less than reassuring affirmation does not come to pass.
How much farther can we fall?
The Lame Duck Period
For most of American history, the gap between the election of the president and his inauguration has been roughly five months. In the age of the wagon, the space between November and March was necessary for the old administration to get its affairs in order, and for the new to prepare for office.\n\nIn the age of the Great Depression, such a gap was an anachronism. In the five months between President Lowden's defeat and President Smith's inauguration, Lowden was forced to act without any popular mandate. His trouble doing so almost led to a complete collapse in the U.S. banking system, narrowly averted by Smith in his first days.\n\nIn 1933 therefore, the 20th Amendment was adopted, shortening the period between election and inauguration to 2 and a half months. The contingent election of that year was viewed as an aberration, and a shortened

With conventional politics at risk of being overrun by radical newcomers, the emergence of a coalition of the rational centre can only be a good sign.

Violence in Harlan County
Since 1931, Harlan County, Kentucky, has been embroiled in a protracted period of labour unrest. In response to sharp wage cuts, the United Mine Workers attempted to organise the mineworkers of Harlan. As was typical for the declining UMW, they failed, under pressure from both county authorities and company goons. Their failure pushed the workers into the arms of the IWW, quickly expanding from its new strongholds in West Virginia and Colorado, which began to set up soup kitchens and other aid organisations to support striking miners. This too however failed, as the National Labor Relations Act had few enforcement mechanisms to protect the miners, leaving them defenceless against the \
Alarming.
Escalation of Violence in Harlan
The deterioration of economic conditions nationwide in the aftermath of Black Monday has further intensified the IWW's recent unionisation drive in Harlan County. The result has been a further escalation of violence; murders and retaliatory killings are commonplace, and armed assaults on union meetings are increasingly being met with proportionate gunfire. With Harlan being in the state it is, demands for an intervention of some sort to prevent the county from turning into a total warzone have grown louder in Washington.\n\nOn the one hand, many blame Middleton's actions and the local authorities' hardline anti-union stance for the escalation of violence, and suggest a congressional committee look into matters in Harlan. On the other, anti-socialists have pointed the finger at the IWW, which has always been a militant and radical organisation, blaming them for the escalation into two-sided shooting. Ultimately, some sort of statement about the situation in Harlan must be made.
Middleton is to blame: investigate Harlan!
The radicals are to blame: crack down before this spreads!
The La Follette Committee
The Committee on Education and Labor, Subcommittee Investigating Violations of Free Speech and the Rights of Labor, better known as the La Follette Committee, was formed with the passage of the National Labor Arbitration and Enforcement Act to investigate methods utilised by employers to avoid collective bargaining with unions. Specifically targeting the use of industrial espionage, private police, strikebreaking services, and other tactics in industrial warfare, the committee has now turned its eyes towards the upsurge of violence in Harlan County, where many common anti-union practices take place.\n\nWith the support of the administration, an investigation into the conditions in Harlan has begun to take shape. Already the evidence is damning: union members have testified regarding violence against themselves and their families, and the escalating use of force coming from the strikebreakers. Progressives hope that the committee's findings will galvanise the push for change, and facilitate an end to the violence in Harlan, which claimed four lives this week.
Let's hope it helps.
Martial Law Declared in Harlan
With violence in Harlan County reaching new heights, calls for intervention have reached a fever pitch. Continued killings and acts of violence on both sides have necessitated a declaration of martial law by the state government, spurred on by the administration's statement on the Harlan issue. The IWW has already vigorously attacked the declaration, denouncing Governor Chandler as a puppet of big business and a tyrant-enforcer of the bosses' law. Though we hope Governor Chandler will be even-handed with his enforcement of the law in Harlan, there already reports of asymmetric warfare between state forces and organised unionist militias. Nevertheless, our first priority is now to maintain order in Harlan, a goal which should be made much easier with the state's declaration.\n\nIn the meantime, violence in Harlan has claimed four lives this week.
Let's hope this keeps them in line.
Rumours of Weapons Smuggling in Harlan
Concerning reports are coming in from the counties surrounding Harlan. State troopers encountered several armed bands carrying assorted shipments through the Cumberland River Valley. When ordered to halt for questioning, firefights have broken out, in some instances forcing the state troopers to retreat. When the bands have been forced to retreat, the state troopers have found crates of rifles, explosives, and other weapons in their abandoned cargo. The primary suspicion of both state, local, and federal forces has been that these are shipments intended for the IWW's organisers, a theory seemingly confirmed by the testimony of the few prisoners captured after these shootouts.\n\nThe arming of IWW organisers has raised the spectre of the Mingo County War of 1923, when an army of 10,000 miners rose up in southern West Virginia and rooted itself in Mingo and Longan counties. The aftermath of that conflict turned West Virginia into a socialist stronghold, so there is great fear in Kentucky surrounding the possibility of a similar uprising. Thus, a response has been demanded of either state or local forces. The local militias have demanded we deputise them in their fight against the IWW. Though they are strongly against the IWW, they are poorly disciplined, and are closer to the company than they are to the government. Alternatively, we could reinforce the area with more state troopers, including potential National Guard volunteers from Virginia. Both of these options would however escalate the situation. Our final course of action would be to simply reinforce the road patrols. This would do little to inflame things, however there are rumours that the IWW is also running weapons through the mountains, meaning such an action could have limited effectiveness.

La Follette Committee Hears Reports of Abuses in Harlan
Since the La Follette Committee began investigating the ongoing practices of employers and police in Harlan County, numerous cases of abuse and lawbreaking have been uncovered. Extrajudical killings, flagrant denial of the right to assemble, and the recruitment of illegal police and paramilitary forces on the behalf of the mine operators are only some of the abuses discovered by the committee.\n\nThough the committee's report is far from complete, as currently it stands to pin much of the blame for the situation in Harlan squarely on Sheriff Middleton, who has been found as flagrantly violating the law by recruiting disreputable anti-union elements to help suppress union organisers. This finding, and its scapegoating of Middleton, is admittedly politically convenient for us, as calling for his removal is an actionable recommendation that does not require systemic reform. Alternatively however, we could direct the committee to take a more broad approach, looking at the systemic problems in Harlan to reconstruct labour arbitration policy more broadly.

A Federal intervention is needed.
For years, a low-intensity war has simmered in Harlan County. Fighting between IWW unionists and company and police forces took many lives before 1936, as the IWW tried and failed to maintain a union foothold in the county. This year however has seen the violence escalate dramatically, with over a hundred dead or missing in the first months of the year.\n\nThe intensified period of conflict has now come to a head. Having prepared for a final confrontation in Harlan over the past few months, the IWW assembled an army of over 12,000 men, larger than the force that marched on Blair Mountain in 1923. The army was divided between two groups: a larger force that was to march from West Virginia through the Cumberland valley, capturing settlements until it reached the town of Harlan itself, and a smaller force deeper in the county that would dislodge the Sheriff's forces from the southern half of Harlan town.

Far-Right Militias Mobilise
The impact of the recent events in Harlan have reverberated across the nation in many ways. Though the left has been angered into violence by the suppression of the Harlan Reds, the right has seen Harlan as a vindication of both their fears and preferred responses towards socialism. Already, the anti-union militias which took part in the fighting in Harlan County have been lionised and held up as heroes, and violence against unions across the nation has seen a measurable spike.\n\nThe activities of growing far-right and anti-union militias have long caught the eye of the state, but their growth this year has been extremely concerning. Many take the view that the federal government has already been captured by socialists, so even in instances of Red uprising such as Harlan, they cannot be reliable allies of the government.

Harlan Rebellion Quelled
Once it was decided that federal intervention was needed in Harlan, the days of the Red militia were numbered. Federal forces entered the county much as the Reds had, through the Cumberland valley, this time both from the west and the east (much to the protestations of the West Virginia state government). No doubt West Virginia's warnings to the Reds aside, they were no match for an actual army. The remaining Reds in the valley itself were quickly dispatched, and when federal forces attacked the northern Red militia from behind, the stalemate in Harlan collapsed.\n\nThe Reds in Harlan town soon realised what was imminent, and retreated south of Clover fork to make their stand. The courthouse and hospital were reoccupied by Middleton's enthusiastic militia, which, eager for victory, crossed Clover fork, upon which they engaged in brutal and desperate fighting with the Reds. Upon the arrival of federal forces, many of the Reds attempted to surrender, but were ignored by Middleton's militia, until the army restored order and ended the fighting. Others retreated up into the hills, where they have subsequently been hunted, and in many instances killed, by Middleton's men.\n\nThe events in Harlan have overall been highly reminiscent of the Mingo County War of 1923. That conflict turned West Virginia into a stronghold of socialism. The outcome of Harlan remains to be seen.
What a mess.

Though many were captured (and in many instances murdered) after order was restored in Harlan, some have slipped through the grasp of the authorities, and escaped.\n\nThe primary refuge of these fugitives is of course the state of West Virginia. The red bastion has a long history with labour conflicts such as the one recently fought in Harlan, including most prominently the similar Mingo County War of 1923. The Miners' Position
The stalemate in Harlan County has, miraculously, opened a window to resolve the disputes in the county without resorting to full-on bloodshed. Though this window is brief, we have been able to send feelers to the rebel militia, which has obtained their non-negotiable demands in exchange for laying down their arms. They include the following:\n - Federal protection of their right to organise\n - Company recognition of the IWW as their union\n - The arrest of Sheriff Middleton and other members of the anti-union militia\n - The disarming and disbanding of said militia and its component private forces\n\nThough these demands are generally regarded as reasonable, they would represent a concession to a violent insurgency. Many in the administration would therefore prefer for the military to immediately restore order in Harlan, and to suppress the Reds without negotiating.

The Boiling Pot
The aftermath of the conflict in Harlan County has been calmer than was perhaps anticipated. Assorted, aimless protests in Socialist-dominated cities were initially commonplace, but without a coherent grievance or set of demands they quickly fizzled out without incident. The right meanwhile has been largely demoralised by the government's forceful application of the unionists' demands: no large growth in right-wing militia activity has been noted, and labour conflicts elsewhere in the nation have been relatively quiet in the past few weeks.\n\nIn spite of this however, analysts have been careful about suggesting that Harlan has brought about anything more than a brief reprieve. Political and labour violence is still at the all-time high it has been at since Black Monday, and certainly does not seem to be falling. Meanwhile, in Harlan itself, several weapons caches have been discovered by federal forces, obviously created by the militias in case they ever needed to re-arm themselves.\n\nAs the old myth goes, if you try to boil a living frog, you cannot increase the temperature too rapidly, lest it jump out of the pot. Instead, you must slowly increase the temperature, and it will die without protest. Perhaps by slowing the boil of Harlan, we have made ourselves into frogs.

The Reds ruled the county under de facto martial law, as most of the local government had either fled or been imprisoned on charges of collaboration with Middleton. The Demands of the Commune
The decision to negotiate with the Harlan Commune has not been an easy one. Should they fail, we open ourselves to accusations of having been too soft on the syndicalists. Should we succeed, that will apply even more so. Regardless, our envoy was received by the commune without incident, and has reported the situation on the ground, describing the townsfolk as generally enthusiastic about the project, while having reservations about many of the plans of the commune's leaders, as well as the immediate army threat bearing down on them all.\n\nIn any case, our envoy's talks with the leadership was productive, and he received a clear list of demands:\n - The abolition of the county government and its replacement with that of the commune\n - The dissolution of Harlan's police, as well as any associated private militias, and their replacement with the communal militia\n - The recognition of the commune's legal judgements, including the prosecutions of Sheriff Middleton and other local officials\n\nTo many, these demands are clear non-starters. The demand that the rebel militia take over as law enforcement is unpalatable to the extreme to many administration officials. As such, there are demands that we simply tell the commune to go back to the drawing board and put forward more reasonable demands.\n\nAlternatively, some have suggested revising the conditions ourselves, and trying to accomplish as many as reasonably possible. The militia demand, for instance, could perhaps be accommodated if it were to be substantially downsized, stripped of its heavy weapons, and limited only to local volunteers. Additionally, though we cannot undermine the rule of law by granting it solely to the commune, we can promise to prosecute Middleton and others in federal court, so they will not escape justice.\n\nUltimately, we have been given the initiative in negotiations, and have the responsibility to reply to their demands.
They have to be more reasonable.

Negotiations Break Down
Perhaps inevitably, the gap between the positions of the Harlan Commune and the federal government has proven too far to bridge. The commune made clear that its demands were final, and that it would not accept a deal where it was forced to cede power back to the county government. With negotiations at an impasse, the window for a peaceful settlement to the Harlan crisis closed.\n\nNow, both sides mobilise for a final armed confrontation. Makeshift defences now line parts of the county, as the communal militia digs in to try and hold off the army for as long as possible. The army meanwhile moves into position on both the east and west ends of Harlan County, preparing to march in and end the ill-begotten experiment in communal government that Harlan has become.
It was inevitable.
The Commune Comes to an Agreement
In a shocking turn of events, the Harlan Commune has agreed to our revision of their initial list of demands. Though many within the administration viewed a deal as an impossibility, the communal government has proven less intransigent than initially expected. As part of the arrangement, certain figures in Harlan's pre-communal government have been handed over to federal authorities, and the Harlan communal militia has handed over all of its artillery and all but two of its machine guns, as well as expelling all of its members from outside of Harlan County.\n\nThough these concessions both leave a local independent judiciary and leave the communal militia as a force no more powerful than most local police forces, it still means that the commune has now successfully overthrown the legitimate government of an American municipality. Unions Stockpile Weapons
The effective victory of the Harlan communal militia has had yet more knock-on effects. Since the end of the Harlan crisis, reports of unions collecting and stockpiling increasingly heavy armaments have reached the administration. With Harlan's vindication of the power of physical force, and its apparent demonstration that there is an actual path to victory for armed organised labour and physical force unionism, many other unions, including those belonging to the CIO rather than the IWW, have begun to stockpile weapons.\n\nWhile this is obviously not a new phenomenon, the scale and severity of it is. Not only has it increased fears of a general labour uprising, it has also resulted in more immediate violence, as incidents by armed unionists against union enemies have increased dramatically over the past few weeks. With several dead, Harlan seems more and more to be only the beginning of our trouble with labour armies.
What is happening to our country...
Anti-Union Paramilitaries Mobilise
The increasing militarisation of unions has inevitably brought about a harsh response from those opposed to organised labour. Anti-union businessmen and employers, as well as other right-wing elements, have lost faith in the government's ability and willingness to protect them and their property from revolutionary militias. The agreement with the Harlan Commune has revealed to them that the administration is either unable or unwilling to stand with them against union radicals.\n\nAs such, they have taken matters into their own hands. Already, employers' militias have taken to the streets to contest the dominance of the Red Guards, the Socialist Vanguard, and the IWW's assorted paramilitary squads. Now however recruitment and expansion for these groups has exploded, with many employers viewing them, even with their often undisciplined and violent tactics, as the only groups capable of protecting their property.\n\nOne supporter of these groups has emerged in the Senate: never one to miss a chance to skewer President Smith, Huey Long has voiced support for these paramilitaries' efforts to protect private property against socialists and radicals.
Violence begets violence.
Executive Order 7029
The first priority of the new administration is to alleviate the state of chronic unemployment in the United States. Exasperated by Black Monday, unemployment has continually risen for the past year, up from Smith's low of 15% now to nearly 25%, approaching the dark nadir of the later Lowden years.\n\nTo this effect, President Olson has promulgated Executive Order 7029. The order provides for the emergency reappropriation of funds from certain federal departments, particularly the military, towards public works and employment programs. Though this unilateral exercise of executive power is controversial, it is hoped that quick relief will help stop the economic bleeding of the past year.
Let's hope it's enough.
Military Grumbles Over Reappropriations
The President's unilateral reappropriation of federal funds away from the military has been controversial in many circles. Though the outcry from conservatives has been the most prominent, also notable has been the response of the military itself, which has, privately but strenuously, protested the reallocation of its funds towards other projects.\n\nChief of Staff Douglas MacArthur in particular has been vocal to administration officials about his disapproval of the President's scheme. In a strongly worded letter to President Olson, he outlined both the constitutional dubiousness of the measure, as well as the need to maintain the separation between military and civilian affairs. Though MacArthur has little recourse but to comply with our orders, it is perhaps an inauspicious beginning for the administration's relationship with the armed forces.
We should keep an eye on him.

Suit Launched Against Our Administration
Our snubbing of Congress has seemingly resulted in quick blowback. Today, numerous conservatives, moderates, and even some progressives have joined a lawsuit arguing that Executive Order 7029 is unconstitutional, and that the president cannot appropriate funds in such a manner without the consent of Congress.\n\nThough the opposition of conservatives was expected, more concerning is the attachment of names such as those of Senators William Borah and Burton K. Wheeler to the suit. This open sleight against the administration by non-Farmer-Labor progressives is an indication of a growing rift on the centre-left regarding the use of government powers by the administration. Having chosen our course on the matter, the only thing left to do is see this fight to its conclusion.
They show their true colours.
Funding Legislation Stalls
In response to congressional condemnation of Executive Order 7029, we have chosen to throw Congress a bone. Our allies in both the House and Senate have put forward new bills both legitimising the reappropriation of funds featured in EO 7029, as well as authorising funding for further public works projects.\n\nIntended to ameliorate concerns that we are overstepping the constitutional bounds of the presidency, the bills have instead not quite had their intended effect: their introduction, while placating the progressives in our congressional coalition, has been seen as an admission of guilt by conservatives. Many conservative members of congress have now attached themselves to a suit declaring EO 7029 unconstitutional, a suit which now appears to be headed straight to the conservative-leaning Supreme Court.
We did what we could.
Supreme Court Rules Against Us
The administration has suffered a significant setback. The Supreme Court today has ruled that Executive Order 7029 is an unconstitutional exercise of presidential power, and that the president does not have the ability to reappropriate funds in such a manner. Though two members of the court's progressive wing dissented, most sided with the majority against the administration.\n\nThis defeat has substantial implications for the future of our administration. Being forced to push our agenda through Congress will slow our recovery efforts substantially, and lose us precious time in dealing with growling labour and farm unrest. As such, some members of the administration have suggested an alternative approach: ignoring the court.\n\nAn option with some precedent, we could simply declare that the present national state of economic emergency warrants the bypassing of the court's order. This will have significant ramifications however: if Congress was souring on us before, they will have even more to say now.
Back Down.

Justice James McReynolds Assassinated
Shocking news has come in today of an act of political violence in the heart of Washington itself. Associate Justice James R. McReynolds, a vociferous conservative voice on the Supreme Court, was murdered outside his apartment while leaving for the Supreme Court building this morning.\n\nMcReynolds, a key vote against the administration in the recent Supreme Court case regarding Executive Order 7029, was no friend of the administration. His assassination however seems set to spell headaches for us, as the assassin was an unemployed man who was a known supporter of the Farmer-Labor Party. Though no link between him and the administration itself exists, the assassination reflects poorly on the president, and whispers of conspiracy abound on the right.\n\nMcReynolds' assassination was not the first major act of political violence this year, and is unlikely to be the last. Political violence has continually grown over the past decade, both on the left and the right, with McReynolds being merely the highest profile casualty yet.

Impeachment Proceedings Begin
Though the administration's decision to flagrantly violate the ruling of the Supreme Court may have won it praise from the left, it has only deepened the divide between the president and Congress. Today, the ongoing rift between the executive and the legislature has come to a head, with the introduction of articles of impeachment by Congressman Dewey Jackson Short. Short charges President Olson with abuse of power, firmly listing the refusal to comply with the court's ruling as an example of the president overstepping his bounds.\n\nAs relations with even the progressives in Congress have dramatically deteriorated over the past weeks, we cannot guarantee that these proceedings will not garner enough votes to pass the House. Though impeachment will be a drawn out process, House Speaker John Nance Garner has already voiced his openness towards putting it forward for a House vote.
We won't be held back by those reactionaries.
Olson Falls Into a Coma
For several years now, President Olson has known that his time on Earth is limited. Always plagued with pain and health issues, Olson was finally diagnosed with stomach cancer, a fact which was carefully hidden from the public both during his time in the Senate and in the White House. Though he was in immense pain in the later stages of his career, Olson powered on through, acting as a workaholic both on the campaign trail and in office.\n\nOlson's health has finally caught up to him however. As his cancer has taken a turn for the worse, Olson has been hospitalized, and has now fallen into a coma, from which his doctors doubt he will ever wake.\n\nThe sudden absence of the president due to previously unknown health issues has thrown the government into chaos: with no legal mechanism to replace a living but incapacitated president, the executive has been rendered headless for the time being. Meanwhile, speculation as to potential conspiracies have spread like wildfire, with many socialists speculating that the president has been poisoned by the capitalists.
Oh god.
Quentin Roosevelt Assumes Acting Presidency
Olson's rapid and unforeseen withdrawal from public life has drawn the functions of the highest levels of the executive branch to a halt. With the White House in chaos, communications with Congress have totally broken down, and public relations have turned to radio silence. With the power vacuum in Washington impeding the normal functions of government, many have called upon Vice President Roosevelt to assume the presidency in an acting capacity.\n\nToday, Roosevelt has answered those calls. With the support of Olson's relatively moderate cabinet, Roosevelt has declared that he is assuming the functions and duties of the presidency, while clarifying that Olson remains president on a formal basis for the time being.\n\nThough the establishment is relieved that there is now someone in charge again in Washington, others are dismayed at Roosevelt's assumption of power. Farmer-Labor Collapses
The fragile united front of the Farmer-Labor Party has always been held together by a thread. The marriage between Progressives and Socialists mediated by the CIO was predicated on diametrically opposed assumptions and goals held by both sides. The Progressives sought the Socialists' votes and organising for their own campaigns, while the Socialists wanted to capture Farmer-Labor much as the Syndicalist Party of Great Britain captured the Labour Party.\n\nWith both sides only partnered in an alliance of convenience, the eventual end of Socialist affiliation was inevitable. Today, the Socialist Party's Executive Committee has formally and unilaterally severed ties with Farmer-Labor. Farmer-Laborites Defect to the SPA
The recent collapse of the Farmer-Labor Party has left several political forces scrambling to pick up the pieces. As the national situation grows more inflamed and radical, both the Longists and the Socialist Party have made inroads into the former support base of the now hollowed-out party.\n\nIt has been the latter that has had the most success in doing so however. The disappointment of the Olson administration combined with sour feelings over the ascension of Roosevelt has driven many Farmer-Laborites into the arms of the party of Debs and Reed. Additionally, the Socialists have scored a recent coup with the defection of the CIO, which has ended its affiliation with Farmer-Labor and entered into a tripartite agreement with the IWW and the SPA. Overall, it seems that history has vindicated the idea originally posited by the Socialists when they entered Farmer-Labor: that progressives would become labourists, and labourists would become socialists.
They have fallen far from grace.
Socialist Party Walks Out of Congress
The recent chaos in the Farmer-Labor Party has seen attention on the left refocused on the Socialist Party, which has escaped mostly unscathed from the debacles surrounding the (seemingly brief) Olson presidency. With the national situation growing ever more radical and inflamed, the Socialists have denounced recent police actions against strikers, as well as Roosevelt's supposed unilateral usurpation of power.\n\nToday, the Socialists have taken a radical new step. Executive Order 7011
One of the key points of the first Farmer-Labor platform was the appropriation of idle and abandoned factories and works to facilitate employment by the government and alleviate chronic unemployment. A key demand of the Socialists in exchange for their participation, it was a key plank in both of Olson's presidential campaigns, in both 1932 and 1936.\n\nNow, with Olson in office, it is time to fulfil that promise. A question of scope arises however: how broad should the power to expropriate be, and what condition must a factory be in in order to be considered abandoned. Though a stricter definition may lessen the impact of this program, it would likely help it survive an immediate court challenge, a key consideration in any case.
Outline specific conditions for abandonment.
Now is the time for bold action.
GM Sues Michigan
It has not taken long for Executive Order 7011 to ruffle many feathers. As the order enables state governments to undertake expropriations of idle properties, it has been used by the radical Socialist administration in Michigan to legitimize the seizure of General Motors property undertaken by workers late last year.\n\nWith GM obviously disinclined to take this lying down, they have sued both the federal government and the government of Michigan over the infringement of their property rights. They are seeking to have EO 7011 ruled unconstitutional, and their factories returned to them with compensation. Governor Al Renner however has stated that even if the courts rule in GM's favour, his administration will not comply with court orders.
Looks like a showdown.
GM Suit Caught Up in Courts
The suit brought by General Motors has, thanks to the efforts of Socialist Party lawyers in Michigan, faced numerous initial hurdles that have brought its progress to a standstill. Using procedural tactics, as well as the ongoing restructuring of the Michigan court system being undertaken by the new Socialist majority, GM's suit has been obstructed and halted in its tracks.\n\nThough GM is attempting to escalate its federal suit, it too is only slowly making its way through the federal court system. Our efforts at protecting EO 7011 have thus far been successful, a fact which has further emboldened Socialist governors in the midwest to conduct factory seizures.
Excellent.
Supreme Court Rules EO 7011 Unconstitutional
General Motors' suit against the federal government has quickly found its way through the federal court system. The dubious legality of EO 7011, specifically in its broadness and lack of protection for private property rights, has allowed ample openings for GM lawyers to hack away at it in federal court.\n\nThis has culminated today in a ruling by the Supreme Court against the administration. Admonishing the administration for its flagrant disregard for property rights, the court has ordered Michigan to return GM's factories, and rendered EO 7011 a dead letter.\n\nIn Michigan, Governor Renner is not taking the court order lying down. With his continued intransigence, we have two options: either we abide by the court's decision, damaging our relationship with the Socialists, or we leave GM out to dry and let Michigan have their way.

The Detroit Commune Rises
With the victory of the workers' militia in Detroit, the city has fallen under the complete control of the Socialist Party, the CIO, and the IWW. Together, they have initiated a program of total syndicalisation of heavy industry, and have seized the property of reputed reactionary politicians and businessmen.\n\nThe political situation in the city having suddenly radicalised from even its previous Socialist-dominated state, the new state of affairs has been formalised with the formation of the Detroit Commune. A new government based on the model of the French communes has been installed with the backing of the state government under the Renner Administration, now totally bereft of non-socialist influence.\n\nAs a result of the crisis, we have been forced to declare martial law in the state. Shootout in Toledo

Some misunderstandings surrounding the prerogatives of federal arbitrators in a Toledo labour dispute have resulted in an escalation of violence on both sides. Murders in North Carolina
Several days ago, two Socialist Party organisers sent to organise sharecroppers in North Carolina, as well as two local sharecroppers, were shot and killed by unknown assailants, and hastily dumped in a river east of Charlotte. Their bodies were only just now discovered, by employees of the Presidential Commission on Labor and Civil Rights, sent to investigate reports of a lynching in the area.\n\nThe discovery of these four victims has generated national headlines, as both civil rights groups and the Socialist Party have demanded justice. As an intersection of the commission's areas of responsibility, it is both an important and an opportune case for us to pursue, as federal investigators have been sent to the area to uncover any clues as to the identity of the assailants.

Setting Up a Meeting

With this shift to the left however, it appears that this will be more difficult than we anticipated.\n\nThe consequences of our setback surrounding Farmer-Labor have already reverberated in our own caucus: already, we have received concerned letters from several liberal and progressive congressmen within our own coalition requesting the inclusion of additional aid provisions, something which risks alienating the conservatives in our ranks. If we do not act quickly to rally our coalition in the face of this setback, our legislative efforts may falter.
This isn't good...

Recovery Bill Fails
The sense of hope surrounding the election of Alf Landon in January has been gradually dissipating over the course of the president's first weeks in office. Optimism both within establishment circles and among the American people that the new president would be able to turn a new leaf and lead the nation to recovery has been met with the harsh reality of a sharply polarised Congress and ever growing political violence, with intransigent radicals growing bolder by the day.\n\nThough it was hoped that the passage of the president's relief bill could break the stalemate which exists in the nation's capital today, any such optimism has been dashed by the emergence of a clear congressional majority against the bill. With moderate Farmer-Laborites joining the Socialists, Long, and southern conservatives in opposition to the bill, the possibility of Landon's moderate backers passing it on their own approaches zero.\n\nThe relief bill was widely viewed as the administration's main chance at a substantial victory in its first 100 days. With its death on the house floor, confidence in mainstream politics, after years of malaise, has begun to shatter entirely. What comes next is unclear, but as violence continues to consume the nation, nothing good will come of our failure.
The centre cannot hold...
Rallying the Establishment
With President Landon only having been elected a few weeks prior to his inauguration, he has not been afforded nearly the amount of time conventionally allocated to incoming presidents in the lame duck period to prepare to assume the highest office in the land. As such, the new administration has scrambled to gather allies in Congress to support its incoming legislative agenda.\n\nThe first item on that list is a comprehensive business relief package, dryly named the Federal Emergency Relief Act. Aiming to support businesses of all sizes to halt the bleeding in employment, it is a stopgap compromise designed to prevent a further collapse in economic conditions. Though we are confident that we can, in time, get it passed, we will need to bring not only our own Republican Party in line, but also the Democrats.\n\nWithout a unified establishment bloc, there is no hope of passing any legislation through such a divided Congress. The myriad Democratic factions each have conflicting reservations surrounding the proposed bill however: liberals and progressives are sceptical of aid to big businesses, while conservatives gawk at such a high price tag.\n\nIn order to bridge these gaps, it would be prudent to meet with one of the leading figures from each of these respective blocs. Our first choice of meeting, either with liberal Senator Robert F. Wagner, or conservative House Speaker John Nance Garner, will set much of the tone for negotiations surrounding the bill to come.
Focus on the Liberals, meet with Wagner.
Focus on the Conservatives, meet with Garner.
Meeting with Senator Wagner
From the outset, it has been clear that the first priority of the Landon Administration must be to create a united bloc of establishment Democrats and Republicans, as a bulwark against radicals of both the left and right. With the growing prevalence of political violence and contempt for constitutional and democratic norms, unity of those forces still committed to the rule of law and good government is crucial if our republic is to survive this period of turmoil.\n\nToday, we have scored a breakthrough in negotiations with the Democratic contingent in Congress. Citing the need for an urgent improvement in economic conditions, Senator Robert F. Wagner has pledged his support for the president's legislative program in full, representing an important breakthrough in bringing other like-minded liberal Democrats on side.\n\nThough more conservative Democrats remain sceptical of the scale of the relief bill, the early breakthrough with one element of the party suggests that the Democrats as a whole are receptive to the needs of the moment.
A good sign to begin with.
Discussions with Speaker Garner
From the outset, it has been clear that the first priority of the Landon Administration must be to create a united bloc of establishment Democrats and Republicans, as a bulwark against radicals of both the left and right. With the growing prevalence of political violence and contempt for constitutional and democratic norms, unity of those forces still committed to the rule of law and good government is crucial if our republic is to survive this period of turmoil.\n\nToday, we have scored a breakthrough in negotiations with the Democratic contingent in Congress. Citing the need for the immediate revitalisation of the economy, House Speaker John Nance Garner has pledged his support for the president's relief bill, promising to leverage his power as speaker to push the bill through the lower house.\n\nThough this was perhaps expected given that Ganer relies on GOP votes to retain his office, this is nevertheless a good sign that we will be able to assemble a coalition with the mainstream Democrats. With the support of the liberals expected in the coming days, it is hoped that we will be able to press the relief bill through in relatively short order.

Moderate Farmer-Labories Threaten To Split
The rapid assembly of a coalition of establishment forces behind the president's proposed relief bill has sent waves across Washington. Though the Socialists and Long have, expectedly, denounced the bill, reception among the more moderate members of the Farmer-Labor Party in Congress has been more positive. Many members of the party outside of the SPA have always held reservations surrounding their alliance with the Socialists, and have now refused to align with them in their revolutionary intransigence.\n\nNow, members of both the Wisconsin Progressive Party and the North Dakota Nonpartisan League have approached the administration seeking a meeting with the president surrounding the relief proposal. On the one hand, this provides us an opportunity to decisively win over these groups to our program. However, this runs the risk of alienating the conservatives who we have won over so far. Thus, some administration officials have suggested a joint meeting of both these Farmer-Laborites and the other establishment parties, as an alternative to a meeting just with Farmer-Labor.

Conservatives Waver On Recovery Bill
Our recent meeting with the moderate Farmer-Laborites in Congress on the topic of the proposed relief bill concluded positively. Our confidence that a sufficient number of Farmer-Laborites will defect to our side has increased substantially, as we have been able to win over several key members of their congressional caucus through minor concessions on farm relief and other topics.\n\nThough we are pleased by this outcome, the result of the meeting has resulted in blowback from the more conservative elements of our impromptu coalition. Conservative Democrats and Republicans have privately protested the increased price tag of the bill, with some threatening to recant their support if their concerns are not addressed.\n\nWhile House Speaker Garner has remained on our side for now, he has seconded many of these concerns to us, commenting that he cannot guarantee the integrity of the conservative element if the bill is put up for a vote. With the national situation deteriorating however, the president fears that the time for passage is now or never. Thus, we must decide whether to spend more time consolidating a coalition with Farmer-Labor, or to push ahead now, with all the risks that entails.

Counting the Numbers
The inclusion of the moderate Farmer-Laborites in our most recent meeting with congressional representatives has introduced a new dimension to negotiations surrounding the relief bill. Though there was significant receptiveness to our proposed program among the Farmer-Laborites, there were also concerns that the bill did not include sufficient relief for farmers. While we made efforts to alleviate these concerns, the conservatives present in the discussion prevented us from issuing any large concessions to the left.\n\nRegardless, we are optimistic that the Farmer-Laborites will pull through in the end. Our meeting gave us confidence that they are acting in good faith, and now that they have entered into negotiations with us they have much to lose if they fail to help bring about relief. As things stand, our current congressional coalition may, just barely, have the necessary numbers in the house to push the bill through.\n\nGoing forward now however brings certain risks. Our support among the Farmer-Laborites is far from fully consolidated, and defections on our leftmost flank are expected. With the national situation deteriorating however, the president fears that the time for passage is now or never. Thus, we must decide whether to spend more time consolidating our coalition, or to push ahead now, with all the risks that entails.

Establishment Rallies Behind Recovery Bill
After weeks of frenzied negotiations and speculation, the Landon Administration has achieved a key breakthrough in the process of passing our signature relief bill. Conservative members of both the Democratic and Republican parties, once teetering on the edge of defecting from the administration camp, have now publicly announced their support for the relief bill, signalling a turning of the tide in favour of the administration in Congress.\n\nThough the administration's efforts have been rewarded by the support of these conservatives, we are not yet out of the woods. The bill remains stuck in committee, and though we are hopeful that we have the numbers on the floor of the House, we are not yet certain of its passage. Still, a win is a win, and the president hopes that, within the next month, a bill shoring up the jobs of millions of Americans will land on his desk.\n\nThe response of the intransigent radicals has been predictable. Both the Socialists and Long have denounced the bill as a conservative half-measure and as a handout to big business. Long is scrambling to keep his southern allies from joining the tide of southern Democrats supporting our efforts, while the Socialists are attempting to peel off Farmer-Laborites dismayed at the substance of the bill, and the administration's closeness to conservative forces.\n\nStill, a win is a win, and the president hopes that the promise of relief soon to be on its way will politically disarm these radicals.
We'll hold our ground.
Federal Emergency Relief Act Passes
The sense of hope surrounding the election of Alf Landon in January had been gradually dissipating over the course of the president's first weeks in office. Optimism both within establishment circles and among the American people that the new president would be able to turn a new leaf and lead the nation to recovery was at first met with the harsh reality of a sharply polarised Congress and ever growing political violence, with intransigent radicals growing bolder by the day.\n\nThough it appeared at many points to be a nearly doomed effort, the administration has soldiered on in its efforts to pass its signature relief bill. When a slim opportunity seemed to emerge for the bill to be put to a vote in the House, the administration pushed forward. Now it has been rewarded with victory, as the bill has passed both houses of Congress and landed on President Landon's desk, awaiting his signature.\n\nWith the administration achieving a major victory in spite of the odds in its first 100 days, the radicals have been left on the backfoot. Though both Long and the Socialists have denounced the plan as a conservative handout to big business, it is hoped that imminent business relief will help take the wind out of their sails. Though the situation across the nation remains tense and violent, hopefully our success at securing relief will help us lower the temperature somewhat.
We can only hope...
The Crossroads Speech
With growing political instability and violence at the forefront of voters' minds after the election, the president has chosen to make an address from the White House over the radio. Aware of the contentious nature of his election, as well as a perceived lack of legitimacy for the administration, he hopes that a decisive, unifying address will help firmly cement his status as the nation's leader.\n\nSuch a speech however is broader in concept than it will be in practice. As the central issue for most voters today, some combination of the depression and political radicalisation will need to be the topic of discussion. The tone of the speech however is the decisive detail: do we attempt to hold on to a sense of good-old American optimism in spite of grim economic forecasts, or do we attempt to reach out to the people through transparent frankness about the reality of life today?

Southern Indiana has been a regional bastion against socialism, even as much of the steel belt turns red. Coming so soon after the inauguration, it threatens to undermine our efforts to clamp down on the violence that has been afflicting our nation as of late. Now, we must prepare for the blowback...

Red Guards Seize Indiana Railroads
Though we were prepared for some form of retaliation in response to the recent murder of unionists in southern Indiana, we have gravely underestimated the extent of that response. Today, a joint action by the CIO and IWW (already an almost unprecedented development), has seen the occupation of the site of the murders, as well as numerous key positions on railroads in southern Indiana.\n\nDemanding restitution for the murders and the expulsion of the Minutemen from the state, their conflict with both the businessmen alleged to have employed the Minutemen as hired goons, as well as the state government, alleged to have enabled the Minutemen at every turn, threatens to turn even more violent. Already, several shooting incidents and injuries have been reported on the railroads, with more expected in the days to come.

MacArthur Demands Activation of War Plan White
The recent seizure of key railroads in southern Indiana has prompted a surprise meeting between the president and army Chief of Staff General Douglas MacArthur. MacArthur, making clear the severity of a potential nationwide replication of the events in Indiana, briefed the president on War Plan White, a counterinsurgency plan developed by the army under the Smith Administration in order to manage any substantial domestic unrest.\n\nThough the president was in agreement with the necessity of having such a plan on hand, he was shocked by the general's suggestion that it be immediately implemented. Dismissing MacArthur's suggestion for the time being, the president has made clear that the application of military force on American citizens is an absolute last resort. MacArthur left the meeting with a poker face, telling the president that the situation would be resolved in due course.
An absolute last resort...
Share Our Wealth Societies Attacked
Though it was hoped by some that the election of President Long would begin to bridge the political divides that have thrown the nation into chaos, those hopes have proven to be short lived. Already, violent attacks by paramilitary or militia actors have continued to climb after the election, as socialists refuse to take Long's ascendency lying down, and Longists are determined to protect their recent gains.\n\nAmong the most notable instances of violence in the early days of the Long Administration have been a spate of attacks on Share Our Wealth clubs in northern, socialist-dominated cities. Chicago, Cleveland, Detroit, and New York have all seen significant violent acts against the clubs, with the most recent attack in Chicago resulting in the death of two Share Our Wealth members.\n\nDetermined not to let such acts of violence against his supporters go unpunished, the president has ordered a federal investigation into these acts of violence. We have however run into the problem of generally uncooperative state and municipal authorities, unsympathetic to the president's politics.

Minutemen Murder Striking Workers
The most recent spate of political violence has devolved into a nationwide tit-for-tat. The recent attacks on Share Our Wealth members in northern cities have spurred on retaliatory action from the similarly Long-aligned Minutemen. Yesterday, a group of Minutemen in Gary, Indiana, attacked a number of striking workers with knives and even pistols, killing three and severely wounding two more.\n\nThough these strikers were members of the IWW's railroad union, the consequences of this attack have already reverberated beyond the most radical sections of the left. Reports of unionists, even from the CIO and even AFL, arming themselves similarly with everything from clubs to submachine guns has spurred fears of further violence, particularly of a revolutionary nature. Additionally, the violence complicates Long's project to reconcile the AFL and moderate element in the CIO to his movement, spurred on by the progressive element in his coalition.

Open Battle in Toledo
The nationwide paramilitary tit-for-tat between Minutemen and strikers has further escalated. In Toledo, a Socialist stronghold, clashes between the two groups have escalated in scale and intensity for the past week. Though they originally started with clubs, metal bars, and knives, now the situation has escalated to an all-out shooting spree, as several clashes in the city have turned into shootouts.\n\nAlready, martial law has been declared in several northwestern Ohio counties, to prevent the violence from spreading. This has done little to alleviate the situation however, as federal forces have not yet arrived to shut off the bloodletting. Regardless, even once the violence quietens somewhat, the reports from Toledo have already inspired copycat acts of violence across the nation.
