Executive Order 7010
The restoration of order throughout the United States is one of President Long's first and foremost priorities upon taking office. Across the nation, under resourced and overwhelmed local police and militias have been unable to contain the flood of oftentimes violent labour agitation. Though the president supports the right to organise, the radical and socialist unionists have abused that right to promote criminal anarchy, and must be stopped by the means at hand.\n\nTo this end, the president wishes to sign an executive order that will give certain paramilitary organisations such as the Minutemen police powers under certain circumstances. This will undoubtedly be controversial, as socialists denounce any attempts to pacify violent strikers and the establishment decries it as a power grab.\n\nRegardless, we must decide on the specifics of this executive order. Though we could deputise all Minutemen nationwide as federal law enforcement, this would undoubtedly cause enormous uproar. Instead, a more moderate solution may be to, more symbolically, merely encourage local municipalities to deputise them in such a manner.
The Minutemen must be deputised nationwide.

Establishment Liberals Denounce Long
Our decision to deputise all Minutemen nationwide as federal law enforcement officers has faced rather steep blowback. Though the right has been cautiously optimistic about the plan, establishment liberals have fervently denounced the scheme, decrying it as nothing but a bare faced power grab by President Long.\n\nThough we would generally not be too concerned by the denunciations of members of the Washington establishment we have fought so fervently against, it is important to note that many of these concerns have come from the people who helped elect the president, and indeed from those within his own circle. Burton K. Wheeler for instance has personally expressed concern about the potential abuses of power enabled by the executive order.

Socialists Arrested in Philadelphia

Already, numerous socialists have been arrested and charged with a variety of petty and not-so-petty crimes, hopefully clipping the wings of the SPA in the city.

The recent deputisation of members of the Minutemen has instilled a new boldness in many of the organisation's chapters. Where they initially were faced with the threat of law enforcement, now they are capable of acting with more impunity in many areas, encouraging them to take bolder action against socialists, radical unionists, and other perceived enemies of the president.\n\nThe latest example of this has been a particularly violent Minutemen assault on an IWW gathering in Cincinnati. Though the clash resulted in the retreat of the unionists and only resulted in one death, it is emblematic of the result the deputisation program has brought.\n\nAs a result however, even CIO and AFL unionists are beginning to lose faith in the ability and willingness of the government to protect them, a development with many concerning implications.

The recent takeover of Detroit by the Socialist-aligned National Guard has not been without significant pushback. The Minutemen presence in the city, having grown substantially over the past year in response to growing socialist militancy and agitation, attempted, though failed, to resist the SPA's total takeover of the city.\n\nHaving been pushed out of the city proper, the Minutemen have retreated to the reactionary suburb of Dearborn, a community largely insulated from the influence of the Socialist Party. Impeachment Proceedings Begin
For weeks now, the nation has been gripped by the turmoil in the midwest which has followed the president's executive order deputising the Minutemen. Though the order was always expected to cause blowback, the violence unleashed by the president's actions has been well beyond what was expected, as the Minutemen have acted with impunity when granted the powers of law enforcement and local forces have pressed back with open displays of force.\n\nWith the executive order having always been of dubious legality, the expected pushback has occurred. Today, articles of impeachment were introduced by Socialist Congressman Vito Marcantonio, accusing President Long of abusing his powers. Though we would not normally be worried about articles of impeachment introduced by a Socialist, many even in the mainstream parties have now indicated their willingness to seriously consider impeachment.\n\nThis is of course just the latest in a long line of actions by the establishment intended to stop the president in his tracks. Despite the growing opposition in Congress, we have every intention of fighting to the last to hold on to the power to which the president was duly elected.

The President Speaks
President Long was elected by a broad coalition of elements dissatisfied with the status quo, and equally opposed to the menace of socialism. Western and southern farmers, small business owners, and anti-socialist workers have all combined to bring Long into the White House. Squeezed between conventional big business capitalism and radical socialism, They have, in Long's view, appointed him as their tribune to stand up to established interests and forge an economy that works for all.\n\nOn his first day in office therefore, President Long has chosen to give an address over the radio emphasizing his immediate aims in terms of economic policy. For too long, the fat cats of Wall Street have run roughshod over farmers and working people through predatory banking practices. Long therefore has demanded that Congress pass Father Charles Coughlin's proposed banking reform, which will create a Bank of the United States of America under the control of elected officers.\n\nPredictably, there have been immediate objections to this proposed reform. Though Al Smith also pursued banking reform in his first term, none of the measures implemented then are as radical as this. Additionally, there have been concerns surrounding the constitutionality of the plan. Nevertheless, the president has defended the plan as having neither of the primary drawbacks of a private or

Banking Bill Faces Steep Obstacles
Our efforts to make the Nye-Sweeney Banking Bill the centrepiece of our domestic agenda has been received warmly by our base. Already, the administration has been inundated with thankful letters from supportive farmers, who expect a democratised banking system to be friendlier to their needs and interests. In Washington however, it has gone over slightly less smoothly: many groups opposed to us in Congress have voiced their skepticism, and as things stand it appears unlikely that the bill will pass in its current form.\n\nCompromise will likely be needed in order to allow us any hope of passing the bill. The most simple and obvious proposal for compromise would be to simply water down the bill and make the recommendations of the elected directors advisory, as well as removing provisions requiring local banks have 100 percent of demand deposits in reserve. Though this would be a substantial reduction in its scope, it is likely to pass through Congress and give us an early victory. Additionally, when our position is more secure, we could make further reforms to add power to an already established institution.\n\nAlternatively, we could try to again levy the support of the large northern businesses who we were in a surprising marriage with during the campaign. Though European-style state corporatism has previously been anathema to the president, granting corporate representation on the board of directors (which we may try to remove later) could help us get buy-in from capital.\n\nFinally, the more uncompromising and unscrupulous members of our administration have recalled the old tactics we used back in Louisiana. As Governor, Long was not above...lubricating the opposition with pork to get his bills passed. Though we should be wary of treating D.C. as an enlarged Baton Rouge, perhaps the same principle can be applied?
We can cool some heads by moderating the bill's more radical notions.

The Banking and Monetary Control Act Passes
Our compromise regarding the banking bill has had its intended effect. Congressional moderates, satisfied that the bill does not substantially violate the rights of the existing stakeholders in America's banks, gave their tepid support to the president's proposal, giving us a significant legislative win in the first weeks of the administration.\n\nThough the proposal is a significantly watered down version of Father Coughlin's original plan, we still find cause for celebration. The interests of the American people will now be seen and heard in the halls of the highest financial decision making in this country, a stark change of pace from the smoke-filled rooms of Wall Street.\n\nNevertheless, our victory is not absolute. The new elected banking board is sorely lacking in teeth. In time, we aim to grant it stronger powers of enforcement, however for now we will have to temper the expectations of our supporters, who demand an immediate transformation in our country's financial system which is not possible at this moment.
A win is a win.
The Banking and Monetary Control Act Passes
Our compromise regarding the banking bill has had its intended effect. Congressional moderates, satisfied that the bill does not substantially violate the rights of the existing stakeholders in America's banks, gave their tepid support to the president's proposal, giving us a significant legislative win in the first weeks of the administration.\n\nThough the proposal is a significantly altered version of Father Coughlin's original plan, we still find cause for celebration. The interests of the American people will now be seen and heard in the halls of the highest financial decision making in this country, a stark change of pace from the smoke-filled rooms of Wall Street.\n\nNevertheless, our victory is not absolute. The new elected banking board is not solely comprised of representatives of the American people. Instead, it also includes representatives from business, and even the stakeholders of the banks themselves. Though we have inserted the interests of the people into banking governance, for now we will have to temper the expectations of our supporters, who demand an immediate transformation in our country's financial system which is not possible at this moment.
A win is a win.
Socialists Riddicule Banking Reform
As expected, our reforms to the banking system in the United States have generated a wide array of opposition. Though initially Congressional conservatives were up in arms about the Nye-Sweeney Act, our accommodations towards their concerns have somewhat quietened their criticisms. Where they have gone quiet however, the Socialist Party has grown louder, raining on our hoped for honeymoon.\n\nThe Socialists have mocked and ridiculed our accomplishment. Denouncing the Nye-Sweeney Act as a powerless sham, they have emphasised the continued role of private interests in the banking system to denounce Long as just another puppet of big business. They have instead demanded that the banking system immediately be nationalised and centralised without compensation, vowing to crush the capitalists who have had their boots on the necks of the workers and farmers.\n\nThe Socialists' response has elicited a divided reaction. Some of the Farmer-Laborites who at one point or another supported Long have been won over by the view of the SPA. On the other hand, their intransigence and radicalism has further pushed certain northern industrialists into our camp, now viewing us and our willingness to compromise as a viable and acceptable alternative to revolution.\n\nIn any case, it appears our brief honeymoon with the broader public will soon come to a close. Now we must consolidate and maintain our strength for the battles to come.

Bankers Dismiss Board Recommendations
We had initially hoped that the establishment of an elected Board of Directors, even if its powers were only to give recommendations, would rein in the banking system in this country, and align it better with the needs and interests of the people. Though the current members of the board have only been provisionally appointed, we hoped that their bully pulpit would compensate for their lack of formal authority.\n\nUnfortunately however, the large banks have instead elected to ignore some of the first recommendations of the board. Though the board has recommended a freeze on farm foreclosures, this has gone largely ignored by the big banks, giving us a significant black eye.\n\nNow, having failed a key promise to many farmers, the words of the SPA are becoming more appealing by the day. As radicalism across the country grows, we will need to more directly confront the vested interests strangling the common folk of this country.

Bank of the USA Board of Directors Meets
With the passage of the Nye-Sweeney Act, a provisional Board of Directors for the new Bank of the United States of America has been hastily assembled. With the demand for banking reform coming from our base a key rallying point in last year's campaign, President Long has been determined to be seen as delivering on one of his key promises. Though the elected element of the board has not yet been properly elected, Long has provisionally filled the vacancies with officials loyal to him, and amicable to the goals of the reform program.\n\nThe corporate section of the board however has been somewhat more reluctant to go ahead fully with any disruptive measures. A freeze on farm foreclosures was tabled for now, representing a setback for many Long-supporting farmers. Nevertheless, the president remains optimistic that the new national bank will facilitate a return of monetary power to the people, in due course.

Farmers Seize Rural Banks
Though we were successful in passing the Nye-Sweeney Act in the first weeks of the new administration, the compromises we made in doing so have ruffled more than a few feathers among our base. The news that there would not be an effective freeze on farm foreclosures in particular sent many small and poorer farmers into a frenzy. Having voted for Long to put an end to usury and financial exploitation, they have increasingly seen the need to take matters into their own hands.\n\nThough rural unrest and attacks on banks occurred relatively frequently last year, the past week has seen an unprecedented wave of seizures of rural banks by farm militants in the Great Plains and elsewhere. Demanding the full implementation of Father Coughlin's banking program, the decentralised movement has engaged in several serious acts of violence against bank management, including several cases of murder.\n\nThough this movement is broadly aligned with our aims (many farmers within it have reiterated their support for President Long), it represents a potentially dangerous militant tendency that may endanger our fragile political coalition. We will have to tread carefully in dealing with it.

The Farmers' Revolt
Impeachment has quickly become a very popular buzzword in Washington. President Long has never been a popular figure in the nation's capital, being regarded as a conniving, dishonest, provincial populist. The corruption scandal was hardly unexpected on Capitol Hill: it fit every preconceived notion of who and what Long was to a tee, and as such the establishment jumped on the impeachment bandwagon in an instant, wanting to finally be rid of the troublesome president.\n\nInstead, Long has always found his friends among the people. Poorer farmers joined Long's campaign in droves, and cheered his victory as the salvation of the common folk of America. Now with their president under attack by the elite, city-dwelling establishment which has always kept them down, they have become determined to show the true will of the people.\n\nRural militias associated with but not necessarily part of the Minutemen have engaged in a growing series of bank seizures and displays of force against federal authorities. Proclaiming their support for President Long, these farm militias have demanded that Congress halt the impeachment process and pass the president's proposed banking reforms. Several of these militias have gotten into firefights with state militias, or even national guards, as rural unrest grows along with political extremist action in both the north and south.\n\nThough these militias are hardly a threat to government authority, they serve as a reminder that Long still has allies willing to fight for him. Though Congress appears undeterred for now, we would do well to keep tabs on these militias and see how they may be used in future...

Government Paralysis
The continuing failure of Congress to elect a president has placed the nation in an unprecedented situation. For the first time since 1789, the office of President of the United States has become vacant, with no permanent successor to Al Smith in sight.\n\nAs the house has yet again failed to elect a speaker, Secretary of State Cordell Hull has taken to fulfilling the duties of the presidency. Signing official documents as the Acting President of the United States, Hull's decision not to resign with Smith's departure as is standard protocol, and to instead stay on to maintain continuity of government has maintained some small semblance of normality in Washington.\n\nThough he has been praised by his fellow Democrats, members of other parties have taken a more cynical view, with some even accusing the Democrats of prolonging the election so as to maintain power under Hull (since it is legally impossible for a Democrat to be elected president in the house). Though this dissent has not resulted in any significant violence as of yet, many state governments have thus far refused to acknowledge the acting president's authority, setting the stage for a dangerous confrontation between the states and a headless federal government.

Midwestern State Governments Assume Authority
Since January 20th, numerous state governments across the country have refused to recognise Cordell Hull as the acting president. In spite of the lack of any legitimate alternative pole of power in the country, state governments aligned with Huey Long and the SPA have not acknowledged any executive orders or decisions signed by Acting President Hull. Instead, they have administratively almost cut themselves off from the federal government, and have even begun to give orders and directives to federal employees in their respective states in spite of their lack of legal authority over them.\n\nThe most notable instance of this has been in the aftermath of the growing steelworkers' strike in eastern Ohio. The situation has quickly grown incredibly violent, as open gunfights between Minutemen, Red Guards, and other militias have left over a dozen dead in the past week. Federal attempts to force the National Guard to intervene have gone unheeded however, as the National Guard in Ohio refuses to acknowledge Hull's legitimacy. Instead, the Socialist governor has ordered the guard to suppress the Minutemen, which they have begun to do.\n\nOur failure to control the National Guard is a substantial blow to our authority. Already, other state governments, particularly in the midwest, are taking more autonomous action either against or in support of striking workers in labour conflicts. As federal authority further diminishes, we have little expectation that the violence which is sweeping the nation will abate any time soon.

Detroit Commune Forms
The spate of labour-related violence this week has culminated in Detroit. Michigan, under a particularly radical Socialist Party administration since 1935, has for years been a hotbed for labour violence. With the federal government unable to control the National Guard however, the state government has finally seen a chance to strike against their political opponents.\n\nIn a joint assault of the National Guard and the paramilitary Red Guards, the Minutemen and other anti-union militias were routed from key areas in the city. Spontaneous attacks on key strategic points secured the city for the Socialist Party, the CIO, and the IWW, who now have total control over the city.\n\nThe political situation in the city having suddenly radicalised from even its previous Socialist-dominated state, the new state of affairs has been formalised with the formation of the Detroit Commune. A new government based on the model of the French communes has been installed with the backing of the state government under the Renner Administration, now totally bereft of non-socialist influence.\n\nThe suddenness of this takeover has shaken the federal government to its core. With one of the most important states in the union being taken over by an openly revolutionary force, the calls for action from Washington have grown to a crescendo. Our impotence to heed them has all but shattered any remaining confidence in Hull's position, as southern and western state governments mobilise their own National Guards on their own accord to protect their own interests.
Something has to give.
War Plan White Activated
Over the past few weeks, it has become abundantly clear that Acting President Hull's caretaker administration is incapable of restoring order to the country. The federal government has all but lost control completely in both the midwest and deep south, as state governments loyal either to the Socialist Party or Huey Long assert control over federal employees and National Guard units. The continuing failure of Congress to elect either a speaker or a president has sent the federal government's position into a death spiral, as Hull's legitimacy falls further and further.\n\nWith the writing on the wall, Acting President Hull has reluctantly heeded the advice of General Douglas MacArthur. War Plan White, the military counterinsurgency plan intended for an eruption of overwhelming domestic unrest, has been activated, with some modifications.\n\nAdditionally, Hull has chosen to step down as acting president in favour of MacArthur: he has appointed MacArthur as Secretary of State and conditioned his own resignation from that post on his successor's confirmation. The Senate, increasingly dominated by conservative voices, approved MacArthur's appointment, making him acting president.\n\nFew have any illusions about MacArthur's new role. Open conflict between the federal government and radical political forces is now inevitable. Now, all we can do is brace ourselves for the coming storm.

With the state militia and National Guard having bowed to the new regime however, it will likely take a full federal intervention to restore the legitimate government, something which appears unlikely for the time being, as the country falls further into chaos.

Violence in Detroit Escalates
Since the election in November, Detroit has been the site of some of the most intense labour disputes the nation has ever seen. With the state-supported seizure of idle GM plants in December, the conflict between labour and capital has taken on an existential character: the workers, no longer content with mere concessions, now appear to be aiming for full control of the city's industrial heart. In turn, the companies have fought a brutal retreat, aiming to bleed the unions and hopefully suppress them through federal force.\n\nIn the latest escalation, the violence is now characterised by open gunfights in the city's industrial and commercial sectors. It is not uncommon to see Red Guards or impromptu workers' militias barricaded in the streets, shooting at hired goons or Minutemen, or even the police. With the state thoroughly in the hands of the SPA, companies such as GM have ceased to rely on the state government to protect their property rights, bringing the class war further into the open.\n\nA state of open war in a major American city is obviously unacceptable. In this administration's early days, we cannot be seen as weak or to be standing on the sidelines. As such, an immediate federalisation and mobilisation of the Michigan National Guard is recommended.

Michigan Seizes More GM Factories
The initial seizure of GM property in December set off a firestorm in Detroit. Amidst a nearly warlike atmosphere, the Michigan Socialists have taken the next step in their nationalisation program: whereas previously nationalisation was targeted at idle and unused factories, now it has grown to encompass properties currently used by GM. Several factories have been seized, either by impromptu workers' militias or the organised paramilitaries of the SPA and IWW, with the state passing a law allowing for the expropriation of factories by their workers.\n\nThough this law is obviously unconstitutional and violates every principle of private property imaginable, it is quite obvious that the government of Michigan simply does not care. The Michigan SPA, as well as the SPA nationwide, seemingly believes that the opening salvos of an open class war have been fired. The continuing escalation of the civil conflict in Michigan has become quite the headache for the new administration. The War in Michigan
For months now, Michigan has been perhaps the most troubled state in the union. Having been under the control of the most radical SPA government in the union for over two years now, the political divides between the extreme ends of politics have been intensified like nowhere else. This polarisation has resulted in an explosive growth in paramilitarism, as the left feels emboldened by the permissiveness of Governor Al Renner's administration, while the right sees no remaining recourse in the official halls of government.\n\nWith it now being clear that the National Guard will sit out the growing civil conflict in the state, violence has exploded like never before. Where previously smaller tit-for-tat battles had been commonplace, now pitched firefights spanning multiple city blocs have become a relatively frequent occurrence. The level of violence has reached such an extent that the Canadian government has increased their military presence on the border near Detroit by 150% in the past week.\n\nWith the conflict now definitively out of control, General MacArthur has recommended the activation of War Plan White in the state. Concerns have grown however that even regular army units in Michigan are insufficiently loyal to undertake this operation. Regardless of what action we might take, it is now clear that a state of civil war exists in Michigan.

Army Deployed in Washington
The growing nationwide unrest has sparked growing concerns in Washington. In the halls of power in Congress and the White House, fears that rioting or armed paramilitary activity could spread to the nation's capital are growing louder and louder, as conflicts elsewhere in the country have grown more and more intense.\n\nAs extremist activity on both the left and right grows, General Douglas MacArthur has recommended the mobilisation of nearby military reserves, including elements of the Maryland and Virginia national guards, in Washington, D.C., in order to maintain order in an emergency or counterinsurgency situation. General MacArthur assures us that the Virginia and Maryland national guards are reliable for the federal government, and with many members of Congress increasingly concerned about the spread of unrest, we are under substantial pressure to heed his advice.\n\nNevertheless, some have expressed concerns that the mobilisation of a substantial military contingent in the capital could increase tensions. Though we recognise the reasons why some may be concerned, the safety of the capital is paramount. We can only hope this serves to cool tensions rather than intensify them.

The Washington Massacre
For the first day or so, Father Cox's march on Washington proceeded without significant incident. The marchers gathered in the national mall, listened to speeches by politicians, activists, and other public figures, Peacefully, Pennsylvania's jobless and destitute made their voices heard, and some began to discuss the trek back home.\n\nOthers however were agitated by an apparent lack of progress. Having come all this way, only to hear platitudes and the same empty promises as before, a group of perhaps 10-15,000 marched to Capitol Hill to bring the message a little closer to home for Congress, so to speak.\n\nUnbeknownst to them however, a little over 40 miles away in Baltimore, a maritime strike had turned deadly just four hours before. With strikers engaged in a shootout with the Maryland National Guard, and with rumours that a few Marines had even broken ranks to join them, the feeling among the Army units in the capital itself was tense. With rumours of a nationwide uprising swirling, they faced down the angry protesters approaching the halls of government.\n\nWhat began the shooting is still uncertain. General MacArthur has claimed agitators in the crowd fired at his men. Other parties have claimed that the soldiers fired unprovoked. Some reports have suggested something in-between, perhaps a loud bang in the crowd that prompted a lethal response. What we do know is that nearly a hundred died by the soldiers' bullets, and fifty more were killed in the ensuing stampede as the crowd of thousands fled.\n\nAlready, a nation that was previously on the precipice has been set ablaze. Sympathy strikes and protests have turned riotous in the north, as what appears to be an unprecedented wildcat general strike brews among the IWW, CIO, and even AFL. D.C. itself is now under martial law, with the remaining protesters being herded out, but the rest of the nation has erupted in fury.
God help us all...
General Strike!
The Washington Massacre has, in a matter of days, completely transformed the magnitude of industrial conflict in the United States. More workers went on strike last year than in any previous year in US history. That was projected to be beaten by this year had the trends of January and February continued. None however could conceive of so many workers striking that it would be beaten by March.\n\nThe massacre of the supporters of the moderate Father Cox, a man who is distinctly not a socialist, has all but shattered faith in the existing political system among the strongly labour-oriented left. With the CIO and even certain AFL unions joining IWW workers in sympathy strikes, workers across the country have been pushed to radical action. For the first time in recorded history, a wildcat general strike seemed to be on the cards.\n\nNaturally, the now definitively radicalised unions filled the vacuum in leadership, taking the reins of the growing movement. Surprisingly, the CIO beat the IWW to the punch in formally calling for a general strike, with CIO President Sidney Hillman inviting his IWW counterpart Elizabeth Gurley Flynn to take part in a joint strike committee. A day later, the IWW accepted, and the SPA unanimously voted to endorse the strike.\n\nThe aim of the strike remains vague, but in general themes of mass nationalisation and union representation in government, as well as the resignation of [USA_Pre_War_President] and his cabinet have been the most coherent demands commonly placed forwards. Of course, neither side now is of the illusion that these are serious demands. Instead, it is clear to all parties involved that the tripartite alliance of the SPA, CIO, and IWW is pushing for nothing short of revolution.
Is this what it comes to?
President Leaves for Midwest
With the snowballing of the general strike, the nation has quickly been brought to an economic standstill. The industrial heart of the union has either stopped beating or has been turned solely to the purposes of the socialist-dominated de facto dual government which now exists in the states of the Steel Belt. The reaction among other segments of the population has been equally swift: attempts to spread the strike south or west have been met with unceasing violence, both from employers, police, and right-wing militias.\n\nThe nation is on the precipice. Once again, it appears that our house is divided, and civil war appears to be on the horizon. Faced with the prospect of a national calamity, the [USA_Pre_War_President] has decided to take a bold gambit. Declaring his intention to travel on a tour of the midwest to negotiate and talk the strikers down, the President has boarded a train that will take him over the Appalachians, through Kentucky, and into Ohio, Michigan, Indiana, and Illinois.\n\nReactions from the public at-large have been skeptical, to say the least. Some regard this attempt at negotiation to be the dying gasps of a failed administration. With rumours flying of a mobilisation of national guards in both the north and south however, [USA_Pre_War_President] feels that a gambit such as this is perhaps the only way to prevent a full descent into civil war.
One last card...
Disaster on the Railroad
Few expected [USA_Pre_War_President]'s goodwill tour to solve the national crisis.\n\nFewer still expected it to end as badly as this.\n\nSomewhere in eastern Kentucky, a bomb went off on the railroad, derailing the [USA_Pre_War_President]'s train. The commander-in-chief's whereabouts are, as of yet, unknown, as though we know the train has been derailed, we have lost any immediate contact with it. Many in Washington have begun to presume the worst however: with [USA_Pre_War_President] potentially dead, the question of whether anyone at all is capable of governing the country has very suddenly emerged.\n\nWith the worst likely having come to pass, General Douglas MacArthur has unilaterally activated War Plan White in Washington D.C. With the support of the conservative plurality in the rump Congress (now lacking Socialists and Farmer-Laborites, among others), MacArthur has assumed a kind of emergency executive authority in the capital.\n\nThis has been denounced vociferously by several groups across the political playing field. Socialists, Longists, and even moderate liberals have all denounced MacArthur's actions as a blatant seizure of power, with many implicating MacArthur in [USA_Pre_War_President]'s disappearance. As the north braces for revolution and the south awaits its Kingfish however, many in Washington see MacArthur as the only figure strong enough to hold the country together.
Is this the crossing of the Rubicon?
The President Lives!
A day ago, the nation was rocked by the apparent death of [USA_Pre_War_President], seemingly killed by an explosion on the railroad track on which he was travelling. Today however, a markedly different picture has emerged. [USA_Pre_War_President] lives, and, from a Kentucky radio station, has announced his survival to the world.\n\nWhile it was initially thought that he had perished with the train he was travelling in, in fact he had survived the derailment and fled the scene with his Secret Service entourage, so as to avoid encountering those who had planted the bomb to begin with. After finding refuge in an isolated town without a telephone or telegraph, he requisitioned a few cars and made his way to a larger town with contact with the outside world.\n\nIn the days since he announced his plan to visit the midwest, the national situation has deteriorated further. The general strike thunders on, and militias pop up like pustules in the south. As such, it is likely that [USA_Pre_War_President] will attempt to return to Washington to see the crisis through.\n\nThe question of General MacArthur remains however: having seized de facto power in Washington unilaterally, many now wonder whether MacArthur will relinquish what he has taken. The potential for a confrontation between the Army in D.C. and their legal commander-in-chief looms, adding yet another dimension to the brewing national catastrophe.
The plot thickens.
MacArthur Relinquishes Power in Washington
For once, we have had a break of good luck. As the president travels back to Washington, General MacArthur has informed us that the capital has been secured, and that the Army can guarantee the safety of the federal government. Though the words state nothing explicitly, MacArthur's communique is a de facto acknowledgement of the president's authority, and paves the way for his return to day-to-day governance.\n\nRegardless of MacArthur's motivations for unilaterally activating War Plan White in D.C., once the president was revealed to be alive, it soon became apparent that he could not hold on to the power he had briefly gained. Congress' confidence, though shaken, still lies with the legitimate president, and without allies in government willing to back him any potential putsch by MacArthur was dead on arrival.\n\nNevertheless, MacArthur's brief seizure of power has had drastic consequences even outside of Washington. Several prominent military officers have already denounced his actions, while others inclined towards the rapidly militarising radical opposition have taken MacArthur's intervention in civil affairs as licence to use their own forces for political purposes. We may have been spared an American Caesar, but a split army would be the final step towards all out civil war.
The calm before the storm...

The dual shock, both of [USA_Pre_War_President]'s brief disappearance and of his sudden return, have shaken a nation in turmoil to the point of near calamity. With Washington under martial law, state governments have assumed more and more authority previously reserved to the federal government, accelerating the process which we now see has been ongoing for some time.

Government Paralysed by Inaction
Our administration was elected with a mandate to bring the United States out of depression and back into a state of normality. With millions out of work and going hungry, even those who had opposed our campaign last year had hoped that we would be able to aid in the national recovery.\n\nUnfortunately, after a week of inaction both by us and Congress, it has quickly become apparent to the American people that help is not on its way. As the president and Congress bicker and fail to come to any consensus, the federal government calcifies, and the states take up the most important tasks of administration.\n\nAcross the nation, forces mobilise against the stillborn administration. John Reed rallies socialist radicals in the north towards revolution, while in the south, the restive forces of reaction prepare to confront it head on. In Washington the threat is from within, as conservative forces begin to whisper that the republic may only be saved by military discipline, and General MacArthur sees himself in their words.\n\nCapitol hill may be deadlocked, but the nation is not inactive, and it will not be quiet.

Long Returns to Louisiana
With civil war raging across the United States, the war has not just been limited to the frontlines around Red territory. Across the territories still held by the federal government, militias and bushwhackers clash, with many in the nation's periphery swearing allegiance to John Reed's rebel government. In the south, unrest among African-Americans has swelled. An explosion of racial violence as well as propaganda efforts by the Workers' Congress have compelled several groups of sharecroppers and tenant farmers to rise up in local revolts.\n\nWith Louisiana being a state deeply affected by such troubles, Huey Long has chosen to return home in order to help in restoring order. Sidelined by the recent developments in Washington, Long has, recognising his limited ability to have an important part in the war from the capital, determined that his presence would be more impactful in his home state. The unspoken aspect of his decision, of course, is that he also wishes to prepare the next steps for his political movement, so as to win the White House in 1940. Already, he has made several statements critical of our conduct of the war effort, statements which he believes are more safely made in far-away Baton Rouge than in the maw of D.C.

Long Prepares For 1940

Never a conventional politician, no one has done this so openly and flagrantly as Huey Long. Aiming to secure the Democratic nomination so as to make the Democratic convention a coronation, Long has spent much of the past month on a frivolous nationwide tour, in spite of his duties as a senator. Long has demanded harsher prosecutions for reds, as well as stronger action against war profiteers and price gougers. Collapse of the Long Movement
With the death of Huey Long, the movement surrounding him has suffered a devastating blow. Long's central leadership and force of personality drew together a diverse range of political forces, but now his absence leaves the movement without a unifying figure. Without the link binding them together, the movement, arguably already cut down to size by the departure of its more extremist elements, has begun to fall apart entirely.\n\nThe Share Our Wealth clubs, once the backbone of a true mass movement, have gradually dissovled and withered away. Long's allies in Congress have gone their own way, either directionless or returning to the fold of their established parties. For the first time in years, the Long machine is being challenged in Louisiana, both by the old bourbons and newer reform candidates. No candidate from what remains of the Long faction has the sort of stature needed to make a bid for the presidency.\n\nThe administration has watched the events following the assassination with relief. Fears of an upsurge in retaliatory violence failed to materialise, and the closing of the possibility of another Long bid for the presidency comes as a relief to everyone on Capitol Hill. It appears that Longism is likely to be consigned to the dustbin of history, much to the pleasure of the establishment it ultimately failed to overcome.

Electoral Deadlock in the United States
With the political and economic situation in the United States deteriorating throughout the past year, it was widely expected that this year's presidential election would not result in a decisive winner in November. Massacre in Harlan County
Since the beginning of the decade, Harlan County, Kentucky, has been embroiled in conflict. The IWW and other unions have attempted to organise the miners of the country, facing steep, and often armed resistance from local authorities and company forces. This week, fighting in the county came to a head, with a pitched battle in the town of Harlan. The result was the routing of the union militia, with the massacre of over 600 miners by anti-union forces. With this, the town has been fully cleansed of the IWW for the time being.\n\nAlready, the massacre has caused an increase in civil disturbances in the United States, with many northern industrial cities seeing rioting in solidarity with the martyred miners.
Concerning.
You can't keep making martyrs forever.
Escalation of the Harlan County War
Since the beginning of the decade, Harlan County, Kentucky, has been embroiled in conflict. The IWW and other unions have attempted to organise the miners of the country, facing steep, and often armed resistance from local authorities and company forces.\n\nThis week, fighting in the county has escalated, as the union militia seized control of much of the town of Harlan east of the Cumberland river. Anti-union forces have retreated to the town's National Guard depot. Though the unionists have not fully captured the town, the escalation in fighting, which has left dozens dead in the past month, is reminiscent of the brutal Mingo County War of 1923, and has already resulted in unrest across the United States.
Not a good year for the United States.
America's workers are beginning to stand up.
The Harlan Commune
Since the beginning of the decade, Harlan County, Kentucky, has been embroiled in conflict. The IWW and other unions have attempted to organise the miners of the country, facing steep, and often armed resistance from local authorities and company forces.\n\nThis week, fighting in the county came to a head, as miners seized the town of Harlan, including its National Guard depot. Having routed anti-union forces from Harlan, they moved to capture other parts of Harlan County, taking up positions in the Cumberland River Valley before proclaiming a local commune. Floyd Bjørnstjerne Olson
§YBorn:§! §LNovember 13th, 1891, in Minneapolis, Minnesota, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LFloyd B. Olson was never supposed to become President of the United States. Born to a Norwegian father and a Swedish mother, Olson grew up serving as a shabbos goy for the local Jewish community on the north side of Minneapolis, then briefly working for the Northern Pacific Railway. This was before dropping out of university and heading west to work odd jobs in Canada and Alaska, and then Seattle where he joined the Industrial Workers of the World for a time, picking up a quasi-socialist ideology he would hold throughout his life. In 1913, he returned to Minnesota to study law and became the Hennepin County attorney by 1920. He became known as a tough prosecutor, taking on corrupt businessmen, the Ku Klux Klan, and the conservative Minnesota Citizens Alliance after the latter hired a hitman to blow up the home of a union leader. During this time, Olson aligned as a Progressive, a Democrat, and eventually as a nominee for what was then called the Working People's Nonpartisan League - and was rewarded when he became that party's first governor of Minnesota.\n\nWhen his party became the state section of the Farmer-Labor Party in 1930, Olson immediately became a leading figure of the non-socialist wing of that party, and was nominated in 1932 as its first presidential nominee. A historic first-time showing under Olson allowed him to win a Senate seat in 1934, and allowed him to remain a credible option for the presidency in 1936.\n\nAfter much hand wringing, on the back of a coalition of the congressional left, Olson has now become the first president elected from neither of the major parties since Zachary Taylor in 1848. His election was the least of his struggles however: now Olson must manage a fractious coalition that includes both moderates and a radical Socialist Party which remains committed to revolution. With rumours of ill health swirling around him, it remains to be seen if Olson can walk the tightrope...§!
Alfred Emanuel Smith
§YBorn:§! §LDecember 30th, 1873, in New York City, New York, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LAlfred Emanuel Smith began his career as a climber. A working class Irish-American with little formal education, he clawed his way up the ranks of municipal and state politics, relying on his wits and oratory skills to push himself forward. Though he emerged as a creature of Tammany Hall, he was never connected to the notorious corruption of the machine. After years of steady climbing as a progressive reformer, he was elected Governor of New York in 1918.\n\nThroughout his tenure, he fought for civil service reform and workers' protections, and his ambitions soon turned to national politics. With the nation in the midst of depression, the lane was wide open for Smith to take the Democratic nomination and the presidency in 1928.\n\nWhile his presidency initially brought about widespread optimism that better days were ahead, such feelings were short-lived. Though Smith succeeded in preventing a total collapse in the nation's banking system in 1929, the Creditanstalt collapse and subsequent recession in 1931 put a halt to the limited progress towards recovery made in Smith's first term.\n\nAs the depression continued, and Smith's administration failed to construct a strong narrative of recovery, discontent with mainstream politics grew ever stronger. The Democrats' hold over congress became weaker with every election, as Smith was only barely re-elected in the House of Representatives. His once strong popularity has fallen greatly, as he comes to represent the malaise that has consumed the nation since 1925.\n\nNow Smith is but a lame duck. Challenged both from within and outside his own party by radical forces, he is resigned to ensuring his exit from office is as successful and dignified as possible. With the crows circling the Democratic Party however, the American people wait with trepidation to see what comes next...§!
Alben William Barkley
§YBorn:§! §LNovember 24th, 1877, in Wheel, Kentucky, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LAlben Barkley draws from over thirty years of political experience within the Democratic Party and his own smart judgement. A supporter of the reforms of Woodrow Wilson, he continues to carry the torch of progressive Wilsonianism long after the late president's death. After several failed national election bids and a steady voting record, Alben was the right piece on the chess board in this election to gain the White House for the Democrats.§!
Quentin Roosevelt
§YBorn:§! §LNovember 19th, 1897, in Washington, D.C., United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LThe youngest son of former president Theodore Roosevelt, from an early age Quentin was groomed for political activism in his father's Republican Party. Quentin, however, wished to be a pilot, but was injured in his training in 1918. Seeing his family being torn by Archibald Roosevelt's entry into Huey Long's camp, Quentin entered politics and served as Governor of New York during the fateful year of 1936. Now leading the country as one of its youngest ever presidents, Quentin plans to follow in his father's footsteps and push for a new American Fair Deal.§!
Arthur Hendrik Vandenberg
§YBorn:§! §LMarch 22nd, 1884, in Grand Rapids, Michigan, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn in Grand Rapids, Michigan of a family of maily Dutch heritage, Arthur Vandenberg began his career as a journalist. After a stint in New York, Vandenberg settled home to edit and publish the Grand Rapids Herald, aligning the paper's editorials with Theodore Roosevelt-style progressivism, even as he supported Roosevelt's opponent, incumbent William Howard Taft, in the GOP primary of 1912.\n\nAfter gaining for himself a substantial profile, Vandenberg was often touted as a potential Republican candidate for high office. In 1928, he was appointed to fill a vacancy to one of Michigan's US senate seats. In spite of the general GOP drubbing that year, Vandenberg survived the special election to retain his seat, in part thanks to Socialist vote-splitting.\n\nIn the senate, he gained a reputation as a conservative, though a moderate one. He agreed with many of the measures President Smith took to restore economic confidence, as well as his reluctance to resort to any radical spending measures. Though he was touted as a potential candidate for President in 1936, he declined to throw his hat in the ring, fearing that, as a conservative, he might throw the nomination to the progressive William Borah.\n\nIt was in the months following the election that Vandenberg attached himself to Douglas MacArthur's cause, helping to rally congressional legitimacy to the federal government during the Civil War. Allied to MacArthur on the basis of a democratic restoration after the war, Vandenberg has now been rewarded for his loyalty both with that promised restoration, and with the presidency.\n\nWith the country still in ruins, Vandenberg must now manage a more arduous reconstruction than that after the first civil war. Restoring normalcy and conservatism is no easy task, however in doing this Vandenberg can rely on the support of both Congress and an increasingly conservative and isolationist public.§!

Herbert Clark Hoover
§YBorn:§! §LAugust 10th, 1874, in West Branch, Iowa, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a Quaker family in Iowa, Herbert Clark Hoover began his career as a mining geologist. It was the outbreak of the European War which made Hoover famous however. His success as chairman of a committee organised to ensure the safe return of 100,000 Americans stranded in Europe in 1914 allowed him to establish the Commission for Relief in Belgium. From 1914-1920, through entirely voluntary efforts, nearly 10 million people in occupied Belgium and northern France were fed by his organisation.\n\nHoover's sterling reputation as a humanitarian set him up well for a potential political career. Though his name was floated as a potential cabinet pick, Hoover was preoccupied with further aid projects in Europe. With the onset of the Great Depression, Hoover turned his focus back home, organising charitable aid to Americans facing food insecurity. Such actions raised his profile further, and in 1928 his name was placed into nomination at the Democratic convention.\n\nThough Al Smith was ultimately nominated and elected, he appointed the popular Hoover as his Secretary of Commerce. Hoover leveraged his department for disaster relief and other regulatory initiatives intended to mitigate the depression. Though Smith's popularity fell, Hoover's remained strong, and he was perceived as a strong potential candidate in the 1936 election, though he refused to run under his unpopular party's banner.\n\nHaving exited office with Smith, and spent the Civil War in numerous humanitarian positions, Hoover's election as President represents the turning of a new leaf. The main member of the Smith Administration to keep his reputation in-tact, Hoover was elected with the expectation that his years of humanitarian experience would make him an able president during reconstruction. As the nation begins to heal from the wounds of war, time will tell if he is up to the task.§!
Alfred Mossman Landon
§YBorn:§! §LOctober 12th, 1887, in West Middlesex, Pennsylvania, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LThat, of all people who could've been picked for the task, Alfred Mossman Landon was chosen to lead America in its darkest hour is something of a curiosity. Raised in Marietta, Ohio, and finally studying and settling down in Kansas, Landon eventually acquired substantial personal wealth as an oil producer, and became a major figure of the national oil lobby - a group attacked by both the left and right. A supporter of Teddy Roosevelt's Progressive Party and his 1912 election bid, Landon eventually became the leader of the Kansas liberal Republican caucus. In 1932, he was elected as the Kansas state governor in an exceptionally tight race, and narrowly won re-election 2 years later, building a reputation as a soft-spoken reformist Republican in a time where they are becoming an increasingly rare sight.\n\nLandon was backed by the Republican party machinery as a centrist against party insurgent William Borah. Though he was not as radical as Borah, it was expected that he would be able to appeal both to the national mood for reform and the natural conservatism of Americans. Though the Republican Party had not gained substantial popularity during the Smith years, Landon was still considered a favourite for election. Such expectations have now finally been confirmed in the House, as, Landon was elected by an establishment coalition to serve as Smith's successor. In the White House, the President carries a unique political position, a man who is fiscally conservative yet receptive to government intervention: a figure of business interests who is still a supporter of labour unions.\n\nFor the second time, a Republican stands before a house deeply divided - and President Landon has some very large shoes to fill.§!
William Edgar Borah
§YBorn:§! §LJune 29th, 1865, in Jasper Township, Illinois, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA child of frontiersmen, William Borah was born and educated near Fairfield, Illinois. Moving west, initially to Kansas and then to the boom town of Boise, Idaho, he settled and became an attorney, involving himself in state Republican politics. In 1896, Borah joined many of his fellow state party members in abandoning the GOP ticket in favour of William Jennings Bryan's platform of Free Silver, the first of many maverick acts towards the party leadership. Soon, he gained acclaim for his aggressive prosecution of union leaders Paul Corcoran and Bill Haywood, each in separate murder cases.\n\nAs a progressive insurgent in the Senate, Borah supported Roosevelt in 1912 over Taft, opposed US entry into the European War, and supported women's suffrage. Critical of the McAdoo, Lowden, and Smith administrations, Borah hoped to make a serious run for President in the 1920s and ‘30s, but only succeeded in 1936: With conservative Republicans in turmoil, and the nation in a radical mood, Borah was able to clinch the nomination, and win the presidency with the support of house and Senate Democrats.\n\nBorah represents the last great hurrah of Roosevelt-style progressivism. Though an opponent of Smith's economic policies, Borah favours a far more decentralised model of progressivism than either the Farmer-Laborites or Huey Long. His stringent support for states' rights has won him both praise and scorn, with his \
Cordell Hull
§YBorn:§! §LOctober 2nd, 1871, in Olympus, Tennessee, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn in a log cabin in Tennessee, Cordell Hull has been involved in politics for his entire adult life. Elected to the U.S. House in 1906 at 35, on the Ways and Means Committee Hull was a fighter for low tariffs and an income tax, aligning broadly with the policies of fellow southerners Woodrow Wilson and William Gibbs McAdoo.\n\nAfter a brief stint out of Congress and as chairman of the Democratic National Committee, Hull was entered into nomination at the 1928 Democratic National Convention. It was that year however that he was elected to the Senate, where he gained a seat on the Committee on Foreign relations.\n\nHull's big break came upon the departure of President Al Smith's first Secretary of State, Frank L. Polk. Hull was nominated as Polk's replacement, and as Secretary of State pursued lower tariffs (in spite of Smith's reluctance), a relaxed policy in Latin America, and, controversially, recognition of the Union of Britain.\n\nThough his name was again put forward in 1936 for the presidency, the Democratic nomination instead went to Vice President Joe T. Robinson. Mainly focused on the American response to Black Monday and its domino effects, Hull was shocked when Congress fell into deadlock in early 1937. With no new president having been elected, Smith's term was to expire, and the Secretary of State was to become acting president.\n\nForgoing the convention that the president's cabinet departs from office with him, Hull has remained in office past January 20th to maintain some semblance of continuity of government. As acting-president, his position is widely recognised, even by himself, as untenable, and as the nation falls into further chaos it is likely that he will give way to a force more capable of restoring order.§!

A legislator with experience writing the Federal Budget. A diplomat involved in extending US influence into Mexico and maintaining US relations with Germany. His influence over the Democratic National Committee also gives him the power to influence which candidates can run for office.§!
Wendell Lewis Willkie
§YBorn:§! §LFebruary 18th, 1892, in Elwood, Indiana, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LWendell Willkie has been many things in his life before the presidency. He began as a Bryanite, became a socialist in college, and rumours persist that he seduced Song Mei Ling during a diplomatic visit to China in 1933 - not to mention an affair with writer Irita Van Doren. He continued to stand out when he opposed Democrats to push for a bank holiday when the Great Depression hit. This support for financial institutions and his assertions that government aid should not interfere with market competition made him a possible dark horse candidate for the Democratic nomination, and he served well during the 1940 campaign and afterwards, when his easy mannerisms and propensity for a drink won him favour with the press. It remains to be seen whether this polytalented man can handle the many roles of the presidency.§!
Robert Alphonso Taft

He followed his father into a career in law, being admitted to the Ohio bar in 1913 with the best test scores in the state. Dedicating the next few years to his legal practice, Taft served a brief stint in Washington as part of the legal staff for the Food and Drug Administration where he met his idol, Herbert Hoover. While in Washington, Taft grew to despise government inefficiency, an attitude he carried into the Ohio House of Representatives in 1920. His time in Ohio saw him become a leading figure of the Ohio Republican Party's conservative faction and a vigorous opponent of the Ku Klux Klan, famously voting against a Klan-sponsored bill to ban dancing on Sundays and opposing another bill requiring Ohio public schools to read ten Bible verses daily. Throughout his career, Taft has ardently championed the superiority of private initiative over nearly every sphere, and became one of the greatest enemies of Ohio's socialists.\n\nDespite his lacklustre speaking ability, Taft's local notoriety and status as head of the political dynasty turned into national fame, then to the Republican nomination for President, and then to the White House. John Jackson Sparkman
§YBorn:§! §LDecember 20th, 1899, in Hartselle, Alabama, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn in a log cabin and raised on a farm, John Sparkman had a very relatable upbringing. Harold Edward Stassen
§YBorn:§! §LApril 13th, 1907, in West St. Paul, Minnesota, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a German mother and a Minnesota-born Czech-German father, Harold Stassen rose quickly in life. Just a year after receiving his Bachelor of Laws, Stassen opened a law firm. A year after that, he was elected county attorney. Stassen played a leading role in the creation of the Young Republicans committee in Minnesota in the years leading up to the Civil War, just as the Farmer-Labor Party was strengthening its grip over the state.\n\nThe outbreak of war however interrupted Stassen's career. Stassen, refusing to serve the Reds who took control of the state, fled to Federal territory, where he enlisted. Stassen served out the war with distinction, and when hostilities ended he returned to Minnesota to play a leading role in its reconstruction. Elected as the state's first post-war civilian governor, Stassen helped to rebuild the state while passing several important reforms. Civil service reforms helped dismantle the patronage system established by Floyd Olson, and he cooperated with other midwestern governors on farm issues. He also established the Interracial Commission, the first civil rights organisation of Minnesota.\n\nAs a result, Stassen's approval ratings skyrocketed, reaching as high as 91 percent in one poll. Stassen's ambitions soon turned towards the presidency, and many national GOP leaders regarded him as a serious contender in more than one election cycle. After a false start in 1948, Stassen won the Republican nomination and the presidency four years later. Though not quite the youngest president in American history, at 45 years of age he comes close, and his youth appears to be a good omen for a nation that is finally putting the Civil War behind it.§!
Douglas MacArthur
§YBorn:§! §LJanuary 26th, 1880, in Little Rock, Arkansas, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn a military brat and spending his childhood moving from one army camp to another, Douglas MacArthur asserts that he learned to ride and shoot before he could read or write - and those skills were what he tied the rest of his career to. The most successful son of Lt. General Arthur MacArthur, he followed the steps of his father and enrolled in the United States Military Academy at West Point, then - immediately to fighting against insurgencies in the Philippines and the occupation of Veracruz during the Mexican Revolution. By the 1920s, he was already the youngest Major General in the United States Army and the super-intendant of West Point, which he reformed to address the changes in modern warfare since the Weltkrieg. After service in his old academy, he returned to his second home, the Philippines - but his time there was brief, as deteriorating situation in the United States forced him to return in 1930.\n\nAs political battles raged in Congress and behind closed doors, MacArthur's name kept being mentioned as a blessing or as a curse - everyone knew of his persona, and everyone knew what it stood for. To imagine that the United States Army could intervene in civilian politics, undermine democracy, as if it was some tinpot Latin American dictatorship and not the birthplace of democracy... was a hard pill to swallow for many in the upper echelons of government. President Smith found himself relying upon MacArthur's strongarm control of the army more and more to prevent a collapse of order, and now that he's gone, the General made no surprises and did exactly what was foretold.\n\nWrapping himself in the corpse of American democracy, MacArthur now commands a junta of conservative politicians and business interests to defend the America they hold dear from everyone on the political spectrum. To what end? To be a Cincinnatus, or a Caesar? Only the flamboyant, egotistical, yet surprisingly enigmatic General in Washington knows.§!

Malin Craig
§YBorn:§! §LAugust 5th, 1875, in St. Joseph, Missouri, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LMalin Craig graduated from the United States Military Academy in 1898 and was commissioned as a second lieutenant and assigned to the 4th Infantry Division. However, he was quickly transferred to the Cavalry corps, to the 6th Cavalry, where he took part of the Santiago Campaign in Cuba, and later take part of the China Relief Expedition fighting the Boxers, where he was promoted to First Lieutenant. He then attended the Infantry and Cavalry School between 1903 and 1904, and the Staff College between 1904 and 1905. After graduating his courses, he was promoted to Captain and posted with the 10th Cavalry in Fort Leavenworth. In 1910 he entered the Army War College and graduated the next year, becoming a member of the General Staff and Chief of Staff of the Maneuver Division. After several appointments and relocations, he was posted as director of the Army War College, reached the rank of Colonel and was assigned to the District of Arizona in 1920. He was promoted to Brigadier General the following year and assigned as commandant of the Cavalry School in Fort Riley. Due to his exemplary service, he was promoted to Major General in 1924 and assigned as Chief of Cavalry. He later served in a series of very important senior staff positions until becoming Commandant of Army War College from 1930 to 1935, when he was promoted to Three Star General.§!\n\n§YNotes: He has expressed in High Command Meetings and the Congress that the Army is lacking of preparedness in manpower and material, stressing the essentiality of lead time in military preparedness and focused attention on army planning as keys to victory. While he has agreed in the past with other Cavalry Officers that Mechanisation may be inevitable, he has stressed that the US Army first needs a large standing army to protect its industry before the Army can dream on fielding Tanks on a large scale.§!

Lloyd Ralston Fredendall
§YBorn:§! §LDecember 28th, 1883, in Cheyenne, Wyoming, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LLloyd Ralston Fredendall entered the United States Military Academy in 1905 thanks to his father's army connections and the nomination of Wyoming Senator Francis E. Warren. However, he did poorly and was dismissed from the academy in just one semester. His mother managed to convince the Senator to appoint him again the next year, but he dropped out, and while the Senator tried to appoint him for a third time the following year, he was rejected by the academy itself. Instead, Fredendall attended the Massachusetts Institute of Technology, and undeterred by his experience in West Point, he took the officer's qualifying exam in 1906, achieving the highest grade of all the applicants. On February 13th, 1907, he was finally commissioned as an infantry second lieutenant. Lloyd would then spend the rest of the decade working in several of the army's overseas schools, where he built a reputation of being an excellent teacher, trainer and administrator of troops. Like many other officers, he filled a series of staff and garrison duties in the United States during the twenties. He became both an instructor and student at the U.S. Army Infantry School, graduating in 1923 with distinction from the U.S. Army Command and General Staff School and graduating from the U.S. Army War College. During the early thirties, he was posted at the Statistics Branch of Washington, as the Inspector General's Department and later as Executive officer of the Office of the Chief of Infantry. During these staff duties, he met and has held close relations with both George Marshall and Lesley McNair, both of which nominated Fredendall for the rank of Brigadier General, a request that was granted by MacArthur in late 1935. Since then, Fredendall has strengthened his relations with both McNair, Marshall and Marshall's protege, Dwight Eisenhower.§!
Lucian King Truscott Jr.
§YBorn:§! §LJanuary 9th, 1895, in Chatfield, Texas, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LLucian King Truscott Jr. began his military career by lying his way into officer training, claiming he was a high school graduate who had completed an equivalent to a first year of College. After being accepted, he graduated from Fort Logan H. Roots and commissioned as a cavalry second lieutenant. He remained in the Mexican border for the rest of the decade, serving with the 17th Cavalry Regiment in Arizona, becoming a first lieutenant in late 1918, and a Captain in 1920. He served in various cavalry and staff assignments during the twenties and early thirties, which included a graduation from the Cavalry Officers Course and from the United States Army Command and General Staff College, which earned him the rank of Major in 1934. With the growing unrest in the nation, Truscott was promoted to Brigadier General in case the situation deteriorates and War Plan White has to be executed.§!
Walter Krueger
§YBorn:§! §LJanuary 26th, 1881, in Flatow, West Prussia, Kingdom of Prussia, German Empire§!\n§YBackground:§! §LWalter Krueger emigrated to the United States with his mother and his two siblings after his father's death in 1890. He enlisted in the United States Army in 1898 to fight the Spanish-American War with the 2nd United States Volunteer Infantry Regiment, reaching the rank of sergeant during the campaign. He re-enlisted for the Philippine-American War and joined the 12th Infantry Regiment, where he fought under the command of General Arthur MacArthur against the Insurrecto rebels. In 1901, he was finally commissioned as a second lieutenant and posted with the 30th Infantry Regiment in Marinduque until it was transferred back to the United States in 1903. While his unit did mostly garrison duties, Krueger attended the Infantry-Cavalry School and the Command and General Staff College, graduating in 1904 and 1907 respectively. After a second tour in the Philippines, he was assigned to the Department of Languages until 1914, and with the outbreak of the Weltkrieg, Krueger was offered a post as an observer with the German Army, but refused and was posted with the 10th Regiment of the National Guard. He was mobilised towards Mexico, where he took part in Pershing's Punitive Expedition. In late 1918, Krueger accepted to be an observer in Germany, where he was able to come into contact with the top-of-the-line German tactics, which Krueger would carry home when he returned to America in 1920. He was then posted to the Infantry School at Fort Benning, where he began teaching the basics of German Squad tactics to the eager staff, being promoted to major for his work. He'd continue perfecting his abilities, assisting the Army War College and graduating in 1922, and then leaving once more Germany, where he tried to foster good relations between the two countries' general staffs, but failing due to the hostile political climate of Germany towards the US. Krueger would then be assigned to the War Plans Division of the War Department General Staff, being one of the main engineers of the War Plan White, a hypothetical plan in case of another civil within the US. He was promoted to colonel in 1932, and later to Brigadier General for his new involvement in the War Plans Division.§!

Daniel Van Voorhis
§YBorn:§! §LOctober 24th, 1878, in Zanesville, Ohio, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LDaniel Van Voorhis began his military career when he left the Washington and Jefferson College in order to enlist for the Spanish-American War as a corporal. He served in the 10th Pennsylvania Infantry Regiment and had attained the rank of Captain by the end of the war. After the Spanish-American War Van Voorhis accepted a commission as a second lieutenant in the Regular Army and served in the Philippines from 1900 to 1914. He'd be transferred back to Texas in 1914 during Pershing's Punitive Expedition, and remained in Texas as the commander of the 16th Cavalry Regiment. In 1924 he was assigned as Executive Officer to the Chief of Cavalry, and in 1929 he graduated from the Army War College as a lieutenant colonel. In 1930 Van Voorhis was appointed to command the Army's first experimental mechanised force, receiving the promotion to brigadier general. With the experience he got from his experiment, he developed an organisation system and new tactics for mechanised combat that has placed the United States along with other developed military powers like Germany. Since his appointment to the mechanised 7th Cavalry Brigade, Daniel has been working closely with Adna R. Chaffee Jr. in order to get congressional approval to create a separate and independent armour branch of the Army.§!

Thomas Cassin Kinkaid
§YBorn:§! §LApril 3rd, 1888, in Hanover, New Hampshire, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LThomas Cassin Kinkaid, the second child of naval officer Thomas Wright Kinkaid, graduated from the U.S. Naval Academy in June 1908. His early commissioned service was spent in the battleships Nebraska and Minnesota. In 1913, he began instruction in ordnance engineering and served in that field for the next few years. Lieutenant Kinkaid was an officer of the battleship Pennsylvania in 1917-18 and later in 1918 became Gunnery Officer of USS Arizona. He remained in that ship until mid-1919, when he was assigned to the Bureau of Ordnance In Washington, D.C. Lieutenant Commander Kinkaid was next placed in command of the destroyer Hopkins and in 1925-27 was assigned to the Naval Gun Factory. For the following two years, Commander Kinkaid served as Fleet Gunnery Officer and Aide to the Commander-in-Chief, U.S. Fleet. Studies at the Naval War College in 1929-30 were followed by duty as Secretary of the Navy's General Board. He was Executive Officer of the battleship Colorado in 1933-34 and served with the Bureau of Navigation, in charge of the Officers' Detail Section, until mid-1935 when he took command of the USS Tennessee. With increasing tensions in U.S he is considered next in the line for promotion to the flag rank.§!

Alfred Melville Pride
§YBorn:§! §LSeptember 10th, 1897, in Somerville, Massachusetts, United States of America§!\n§YBackground:§! §LAlfred Melville Pride studied engineering at Tufts University in Medford, Massachusetts, for several years before dropping out to enlist in the Navy during Weltkrieg. He served first as a machinist's mate in the Naval Reserve, but was soon given the chance to receive flight training and gain a commission as an ensign. In the early 1920s, having joined the Regular Navy, Pride became involved in the experiments to develop U.S. aircraft carriers. He served aboard the USS Langley and also took part in the development of the carriers USS Ranger and USS Constellation, as a member of the original crews. In the early 1930s he went on to study aeronautical engineering at the Massachusetts Institute of Technology. In 1931, he became the first person to land an autogiro on an aircraft carrier. From 1934-1936 he headed the Flight Test Section at Naval Air Station Anacostia, and with start of the Civil War he was rapidly promoted to the rank of rear admiral.§!
